Page 23

電影專刊

好萊塢保護小演員的方法　加利福尼亞法律的森嚴　足供律師一年研究之用

— 茂德

前天寫了一篇「好萊塢最可愛的一個小孩子」之後，自己覺得很有趣，而想再補充一下。這篇「好萊塢保護小演員的方法」，就是繼續上文而來的。好萊塢的電影職業中央介紹所，永遠是有幾千個小孩子的名字存記着，等待各公司的選用的。裏面什麽國籍的人都有，中國，日本，印度，斐洲黑人，墨西哥人，暹邏或婆羅洲的人全有。他們各有各的用處，等到要用着的時，黑人的小孩子，價値亦不比白人的低，或者因爲稀少的緣故，價錢還要貴些。

這些小演員旣在攝影塲裏，佔了很重要的地位，於是地方當局，就不能不想方法，去保障他們的健康安全。加利福尼亞州的法律，對於保障這種小演員的，實在嚴厲得很。我們現在可以略爲叙述一點，盼望我們的各電影公司，能不等法律來裁判，就自動的採用任何可能的保護小演員的各種方法，爲這般可愛的小演員造幸福。

據加利福尼亞的法律，小演員在六個月以下的，祗准每天停留在公司裏兩個鐘頭，而在攝影塲裏工作，每天不得超過二十分鐘，並且每次上鏡頭，不能超過三十秒鐘。小演員年齡在六個月以上，二足年以下者，每天祇准停留在公司裏四個鐘頭，其中工作不得超過兩個鐘頭。小演員自兩歲以上到六歲的，每天可以停留在公司裏六小時，但工作不得超過三小時，童年演員自六歲以上至十八歲的，每天可以停留公司裏八小時，而每天工作亦不得超過四小時。小演員應當得的薪水，亦係由地方當局規定的。小演員生下後不滿一個月的，每天的薪水，係美金七十五元；一個月以上，三個月以下的，係每天五十元；自三個月至六個月的，每天二十五元。

以上的不過是些簡略的幾種大綱，其實好萊塢保護小演員的法律，繁重得非凡。許多禁例，足供法律家當作一種專門功課研究之用。例如因爲要保護小演員的目力，就禁止用强烈的燈光射在他們的臉上。攝影塲上必定有看護。此外還有什麽婦女會咧，慈幼會咧，他們的代表每天來監視着。小演員的哺乳或食物，都有一定的時間規定。公司裏僱用一個小演員，先須經過敎育機關騐過體格。以後若繼續工作，則三個月必須重騐一次。公司裏的幼兒室如何佈置等等，亦都有法律詳細規定的。小演員的工作時間，亦不能在下午十時以後。其餘的，因限於篇幅，亦不能細述了。

影片談評

評「媳婦淚」　ＡnotherＬanguaqe　丨米高梅出品　國泰開映丨

— 凌鶴

自「白姊妹」開映之後，漢倫海絲給與了我們最深刻的印象。不管她是否就是當代第一悲劇明星，然而她在「戰地情天」等悲劇中確是極有成績的。我們在「白姊妹」中，看到她戴着白頭巾在修道院中隔着鐵柵門和情人泣别的時候，面對着聖壇剪髮的時候，那種嚴肅的Ｓentiment，擊碎了每一個觀衆的情懷，在「戰地情天」中，當她在英雄的銅像前接受了情人恩愛的時候，那一種熱烈而怯弱的内心表演，也祗有她才有如此眞實的情感。像這樣的表演技巧，無論如何，是値得我們竭誠注意的。同樣，在這一影片中，她寫出了自身對於丈夫的熱愛，雖然丈夫的愛情並不如自已所理想的那般甜蜜，雖然夫家的人們常對自身加以難堪的戲弄，但是她忍耐着，她仍然捧着整個純潔的心而等候愛情的復活。然而她始終一個怯弱者，她終於接受了姪兒的情愛，雖然她也理智的覺着這種行動的不當。尤其是在那打破了石膏像的高潮之後，丈夫憤怒而出，她抱着姪兒接吻而又推開他的時候，那種矛盾心情之深刻表現，眞顯出她獨到的才能。

同時，　丈夫的洛伯特蒙高茂萊，也是和在「紐約一婦人」，「兩婦之間難爲夫，」二片中一様，一貫的那般輕鬆佻達，瀟洒風流。不是麽？一個演員有了他特殊的個性，總可以在適當的劇本中獲得長足的成功。在這裏，我們雖然不能看出他比以前更有猛烈的進展，然而他適當的盡了他應有的責任却是非常明白的事實。我們看，當他在看報的時候，不耐煩的問着「誰打開了那窗子，」更眼看着姪兒帶着妻子出門的時候，以及看着妻和姪子痴情的跳舞，在母親家裏等待，淘氣了一夜的妻子來找他的時候，都是别人難於做到的哭笑不得的塲面。

除了主角之外，其餘諸配角，也都十分盡職。甚至於那青年ＪohoＢeal也極力拿出了那純樸而豐富的情感，如打碎石膏像的前後，如在祖母家給父母追問着昨晚之去處的時候。

有了優秀的演員，無論如何，總使作品獲得大部份的成功。反之，中國電影在目前的狀態之下，其内容的充實，未嘗不駕於美國影片之上，可是常因爲缺乏好的演員，不能夠隨着一切技巧在畫面上完美的表現出來。

我們决不能否認美國片已經有了成熟的演出技巧，尤其是不少演員能有充分的學識上的修養，更爲其影片生色不少。因此附帶的勸告中國的電影演員們，不必使用全部精力來徒鶩虛名，一定要努力的在修養上提高自身的技藝，同時對於中國電影盡了極大的責任，假使他們或她們也認識了中國電影之前途的話。

說了幾句題外的話，但這决不是廢話。現在再說到「媳婦淚」的其他各方面。

首先我們得注意這一劇本的構成，這是一個非常文學的，而描寫細緻的作品。常有人說純文藝的電影不爲一般觀衆所歡迎，（「春蠶」不像「滿江紅」那般賣座，便是好例。）但是這種劇本自有它極高的價値，也是無可否認的。即如這一影片，我們無論如何，也得承認劇作者描寫手段的高强。

他取材於小市爾喬亞汜的家庭小事，細緻的寫出少年夫婦　那種普通常有的愛情的波折。我想凡是結過婚的人，都有這種奇怪的經騐，不管自身對於對方的愛情是如何的信任，然而總會有幾次淘氣。等到一番平心靜氣的解釋之後，自會和好如初。

在這裏使我們連想起「陌路幽情」，那是說明因經濟拮据致使丈夫任性的煩惱，而與妻子决裂，直至十年之後，才重復團圓。「陌路幽情」能指明這經濟的關係，自然是比這「媳婦淚」更爲强調一些。但是後者也寫實的描寫這種小事，很坦白的寫小布爾喬亞汜生活的一部，也極有它存在的價値。至於描寫的細膩，我們只消在姪兒親手擊碎叔父的彫像，或妯娣們小氣的吃糕餅上表現出來。

導演的高强，因限於篇幅，不能細說，很明顯的導演在這裏有着極大的成功。

「三鏢客」評　丨中央映丨　▲發一點議論

— 摩爾

因爲觀衆的要求，中國電影的題材，大槪都要多少觸到些社會的現實。這一點，即使比較落後的所謂「小公司」的出品，也反映了出來。最近開映的一「血路」，「晨曦」，即其明證。但歷史的發展，永遠是曲線酌。在「狂流」之後，在「春蠶」之前，居然有所謂「滿江紅」也者，給我們看。那末，攝製於兩年之前的武俠片「三鏢客」放映於今日，我們也用不到驚異吧！

「火燒紅蓮寺」禁止了，說是太荒誕，而美國的西部影片却充斥於市場。當然，「火燒紅蓮寺」和「西部影片」是有一點不不同的，这不同只在於程度上，而不在本質上。所以在目前很多人難認中國電影在内容方面，已經突過了美國片，幷不是没有理由的。那末「三鏢客」雖則和西部影片差不多，而在中國電影的發展上，「三鏢客」的放映，不得不認爲較嚴重的。

但是由「三鏢客」這張片子，我們看到中國電影的進步，不但在内容方面，就是技術方面，（包括導演等）也有長足的進步。而增加我們對中國電影前途的樂觀，這是閑話。

▲影片本身

「三鏢客」的故事是千篇一律的，俠義英雄，除暴安良。本來結尾還有大團圓的，就是說明書上也寫着「蕙芬蕙芳匹笪宋」，「美姑偶王斌」「三雙鴛侶及張發老翁其樂紅塵餘年」。（原文）如此而在畫面上，我們只看到王斌傷愈，接着一個風技搖曳，大槪是剪掉了，而剪掉至少是有點聰明的。

「三鏢客」的缺點我想具體的寫下一些：

一，故事方面，縣長旣然乘官船，而船夥偏是盜黨，旣是盜黨，何以不刦財於先？或響應於玉蝴蝶與「三鏢客」大戰之時，而刦財於玉蝴蝶已死之後？其他事之巧遇等，更無論矣。

二，導演方面，開幕時介紹人物太呆版，一個鏡頭，一個字幕，中間也是這樣，字幕太多，使觀衆的注意力隔斷。

三，用日光攝影，光線太差，露天佈景，衣服飄動太甚！

四，演員王元龍笪子春，宋莪荃皆甚惡劣。張美玉雖然不佳，但有幾個表情尙好。

小說電影盛筵難再Ｄinner　at　Ｅight（九）

— 馬騰

馬克斯走了，雷瑙德搖搖不定的站著。顫抖的手摸著他的額角。他的帽子掉了，他亦不覺得。他四面看看，但覺四週的一切，都在嘲笑他，戲弄他，威脅他。他珊蹣着跑到着衣鏡前面，自己看見自己　他用手掩蓋著自己的臉，不敢再看了。他給起那張電報來，看了一半，就擲掉了。地板上倒着一個酒瓶，他拿起來對着嘴倒着，但是理面已是一滴都没有了。他仍舊把酒瓶擲掉了。

一回兒飯店的經理先生又來了。他很客氣地和雷瑙德商量，請他遷讓出那間大房間，因爲一個老主顧在那間房間裏住慣了，如同家裏一樣必須要得到牠。雷瑙德問他，倘使他讓出那間房，有什麽别的房間給他住呢？那位經理說「現在正蓬着寳馬的時候，各處的人都來了，飯店裏實在一間空房都没有。勞萊聽了，做出一種怪樣子笑道：「不要緊，不要緊，我正要通知賬房我快搬了。有幾位朋友在派姆别趣請我去呢。花車已經定好了……這間房你們什麽時候要？」那經理道：「不忙，不忙，明天中午好不好？」雷瑙德下意識地黠着頭。那位經理道：「謝謝你，雷瑙德先生。使你種種不方便，實在對不起得很。」他鞠着躬出去了。

雷瑙德呆望著飯店的經理先生出去了。一回兒他漸漸蘇醒過來。他聽見外面馬路上有搖琴的聲音。他走近窗口看着馬路上許多團看的人。他檢起那張電報紙，從口袋袖掏出那一角七分錢來，拿在手裏看了一回兒，拿電報紙包了那錢，就從窗口擲給那位馬路音樂師了。他猛力地關上窗，退走了幾步，就倒在椅子裏了。他儘力想振作，可是已經没有振作的力量了。他眼花繚亂地望着壁爐上放的寳勒的婷婷倩影，他似夢囈似的對着它道：「讓我們設想這就是我們的家。又讓我們設想這是一個眞的火爐，而不是燒煤氣的假木頭」

「煤氣！煤氣！」他忽然聯想到。他彎著腰試騐了一下，極可怖的思想直攻到他瑙筋裏。他開了煤氣管子的小門，聽着煤氣嘶嘶出來的聲音，他覺得着了勝利了。他又把氣管關了起來，四面在屋子裏巡視了一週。他看屋子的四面角落裏，都有黑影子，預備立卽爬到他的身上來。他一躍而前，跑到門跟前，把鑰匙一轉，將門反鎖了。他拿身上的禮服，撕了下來，塞住了門底下的漏縫。又到浴室裏拿了許多衣服，拿所有的空縫都塞住了。他又四面巡視了一下，覺得很滿意。他拿領帶拉拉直，着了一件長袍。最後的儀容，他亦不肯一些疏忽。他又拿電燈都熄了，祗留了一盞。他把煤氣管的門又開了。他仰着躺在椅子裏，眼看着寳勒的照相。旁邊還有一個電話，他的手摸索着，要想打個電話給寳勒。　（未完）

1933.11.09

Huang Fu Revisits Okamura to Continue Discussing Traffic Issues, Four Measures Largely Agreed Upon, Discussed Postal Issues Last Night, No Further Consultations Between the Two Parties Today

(Beiping) This morning, Huang Fu visited Okamura to continue discussing the issues of the Beining Road and traffic to Ping and Shen. The results were: (1) The Japanese army will be fully responsible for traffic protection matters on the Guandong section. (2) The distribution of freight fees will be divided equally between China and Japan. (3) Traffic matters outside the customs will be handled by a transportation organization established by the Japanese South Manchuria Railway Company. (4) Vehicles from the pseudo-Fengshan Road will not enter the customs. The above items have been largely agreed upon. As for postal issues, due to the complexity of the content, they will be discussed at length when Ho hosts a banquet for Okamura tonight, and a solution can be decided. At this point, all issues have reached a conclusion, and no further consultations will be held tomorrow. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to Okamura, his visit to meet with Huang and Ho to discuss matters in the war zone was only for preliminary discussions. Yesterday's discussion focused on the issues of the Great Wall passes. There was no discussion on postal, customs, or traffic matters. He hopes that solutions to the above issues can be obtained as soon as possible. In terms of Sino-Japanese relations, the political aspect is still difficult to open up, but the economic aspect has recently shown a trend towards rapprochement. As for Russo-Japanese relations, the Soviet Union has deployed a total of twelve or thirteen divisions of troops on the border, and there are also five or six warships constantly traveling between the Heilongjiang and Vladivostok. Its naval port is located in Vladivostok, where smaller warships are also docked. The situation is extremely tense. Japan has not made any preparations for this. It is rumored that ten Japanese aircraft flew to the Amur region for reconnaissance, which is not confirmed. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Okamura is scheduled to visit the Summer Palace on the 9th. Tomorrow evening, he will host a banquet at the Japanese Embassy to thank Ho and Huang for their hospitality. He will go to Tianjin on the 10th. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Okamura's discussions with Huang and Ho on unresolved issues in the war zone have yielded concrete results. He attended Ho's banquet last night, which ended at midnight. This morning, Huang and Ho went to the Japanese Embassy to return Okamura's visit, talking for more than two hours before leaving. Okamura will still visit various scenic spots this afternoon. (8th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways has sent Xia Guangyu north to assist in negotiations regarding the Ping-Shen traffic matters. (8th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Zhao Pilian telegraphed Shi Qingyang, stating that they are still staying in Guihua to discuss solutions with Chuan Zuoyi. Before a proper solution is reached, it will be temporarily difficult to enter Mongolia. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Today, Okamura, Ho Yingqin, and Huang Fu met again for three hours. Afterwards, Okamura stated that the Japanese army is currently rushing to build barracks north of the Great Wall. Once completed, the Chinese army can take over the key passes of the Great Wall at any time. Regarding postal and customs matters, only general principles were discussed. Detailed measures will be discussed later. Regarding traffic between Beiping and Shenyang, Okamura suggested that the authorities should negotiate. No further meetings will be held between the two parties. Okamura is scheduled to meet Yu Xuezhong in Tianjin on Friday. (8th Reuters)

Ariyoshi Returns to Beiping from Tianjin

(Beiping) Ariyoshi returned to Beiping from Tianjin tonight. (8th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Japanese Ambassador Ariyoshi came to Tianjin from Beiping on the 7th and visited Chairman Yu. Tanaka, the Japanese consul in Tianjin, hosted a banquet for Yu and Ariyoshi at the consulate on the same day to strengthen ties. At noon on the 8th, Yu hosted a return banquet for Ariyoshi and Tanaka at his government office. At 4 p.m., Ariyoshi left for Beiping. According to his conversation with reporters at the station, after arriving in Beiping, he will take his family south in the near future and denied that there were direct negotiations between the Chinese and Japanese authorities after his arrival in the north. However, he believes that the friendly relations between the two countries will gradually improve. (8th Central News Agency)

British House of Lords Debates China Policy

(London) Lord Peel will express his views during the House of Lords debate on British policy towards China today, believing that Nanjing has indeed made noticeable progress in the past six months. The current government is probably the most effective government in China for many years, holding truly practical ideas. Lord Peel will also say that British policy seems indecisive and is extremely incompatible with its great interests in the Far East and the well-being of China. China is facing great difficulties and the spread of communism and is willing to welcome assistance. Therefore, Britain must carefully observe its position in light of China's changes. Sending a new minister to China now presents a good opportunity. It is reported that those who support Lord Peel's views include Mr. Melchett, director of Imperial Chemical Industries, Mr. Aiding, former custodian of enemy property in China, and the Marquesses of Salisbury. (8th Reuters)

Central Political Council Discusses Diplomacy towards Japan, Regarding Local Negotiations in North China, Many Committee Members Expressed Opinions, To Be Further Discussed at Next Week's Meeting

(Nanjing) Regarding the news of local negotiations in North China, the authorities said that after the Japanese Minister Ariyoshi arrived in Beiping, he proposed negotiations to the North China authorities to resolve local issues. The content was that the Japanese side would return the passes of the Great Wall and continue to discuss the establishment of customs, traffic, and postal services. Huang Fu, the chairman of the Political Affairs Committee in Beiping, telegraphed Nanjing on the 2nd to request the opinions of the Executive Yuan on the Japanese side's request. Under the fundamental principles of not recognizing the pseudo-organization, not giving up the four eastern provinces, and the diplomatic policy of not losing rights or humiliating the country, negotiations can be considered. The sections of Huang Fu's telegram were sent to the competent authorities for careful study. The customs issue was handed over to the Ministry of Finance, the traffic issue to the Ministry of Railways, and the postal issue to the Ministry of Transportation, to formulate plans and submit written opinions separately. Premier Wang took the opportunity to fly to Jiangxi the day before yesterday to seek the opinions of Chairman Chiang on the above issues. Wang returned to Nanjing yesterday afternoon. The results are still unknown. The Central Political Council held a routine meeting yesterday morning, which has already been put forward for discussion. Many committee members expressed their opinions, which lasted about three hours. It is reported that no conclusion has been reached yet, and it will be left for further discussion at next week's meeting. It can be seen that reports that negotiations have already begun in North China are indeed not yet timely. (8th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 382nd meeting at 8 a.m. on the 8th. The committee members present were Ju Zheng, Gu Mengyu, Zhu Peide, Shao Yuanchong, Chen Lifu, Bai Yunti, Shi Qingyang, Chen Gongbo, Gan Naiguang, Shi Ying, Ding Chaowu, Zhang Zhen, Kong Xiangxi, He Yaozu, Chen Shuren, Zhang Daofan, Jiao Yitang, Miao Peicheng, Xiao Jishan, Duan Xipeng, Luo Jialun, Huang Musong, Wang Qi, Gu Zhenggang, Tang Youren, Chu Minyi, Wu Jingheng, Hong Ludong, Xiao Zhongzhen, Deng Feihuang, and others, more than thirty people in total. Ju Zheng chaired the meeting and discussed many routine cases. The meeting adjourned at 12:30 p.m. (8th Central News Agency)

Ning County Magistrate Returns to City, Bandits Continue to Cause Trouble Inside the Passes, Japanese Side Suggests Pursuit, Traitor Activities in Various Counties of Luandong

Changli The Ning County Magistrate Liu Xingpei passed through Changli on the morning of the 8th to return to Ning City. It has now been discovered in various counties of Luandong that there are personnel claiming to be working for the War Zone Investigation Committee, and they are distributing declarations stating that they are ordered to enter the customs for investigation. In fact, they are contacting local gentry and inciting local militias to engage in extralegal attempts. The declaration is signed by Zheng Yanhou and Liu Tiechen. (8th Dispatch)

Changli After the bandits fled from Ning City, according to recent reports from the Japanese side, most of them have fled out of the passes from various passes near Huaguoshan. There are about two thousand people between Yushulin and Huashudianzi. Near Taitouying inside the passes, there are still three to four hundred people from Wenquanyu to Xingxingyu. The Japanese side suggested that we send Liu Zuozhou's troops to pursue.

(Beiping) After the remnants of the bandits in Ning fled towards the Taitouying area, they no longer have the ability to counterattack. The order in Ning City has not yet stabilized. The security team is searching for the remnants of the bandits. Refugees have been flocking back in recent days, but because their fields and houses have been reduced to ruins, they have no place to live and are suffering terribly. The local maintenance committee, together with the county government, is rushing to provide emergency relief to help the refugees. Also, the request by the Japanese staff officer Endo to station Liu Zuozhou's troops in Ning City is not the intention of the Japanese side, but the action of one or two soldiers and is not a problem. It has now been handed over to the provincial government for handling. (8th Central News Agency)

Huang and Zhao Schedule Departure to the Temple Tomorrow, Sui Provincial Government Will Send Troops to Escort, Li Songfeng Goes Ahead to Arrange the Headquarters, Mongolian Banner Princes No Longer Insist on Organizing an Autonomous Government, Huang's First Step After Arriving at the Temple Is to Implement the Central Plan, If Time Permits, He Also Plans to Inspect Various Leagues and Banners of Inner Mongolia

Guihua Li Songfeng returned to Sui on the night of the 7th, reporting on the progress of the talks in Bailing Temple. Huang and Zhao are scheduled to go to the temple on the morning of the 10th. The Sui Provincial Government has prepared vehicles and sent a small number of guards to escort them. Li Songfeng said that although Prince De and others have not made specific statements, they are generally well-behaved and do not insist on organizing a government. All measures will be decided after Huang goes there. As for Huang's trip to the temple, his first step is to urge Prince De and others to accept the central plan. Within the scope of the central plan, adjustments can also be made as appropriate. If time permits, Huang plans to inspect the leagues and banners in the temple. Panchen will begin to return to the temple. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Li Songfeng is scheduled to go to Bailing Temple on the 9th to arrange the headquarters. Huang said that he is scheduled to go to Bai on the 10th and hopes that the princes can accept the central plan to resolve the Mongolian issue. Otherwise, other solutions will still need to be found. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Huang Shaoxiong and Yan Xishan have reached an understanding on the issue of Mongolian autonomy. Therefore, Huang no longer needs to go to Shanxi. Huang is currently still in Guihua, and it is uncertain whether he will go to Bailing Temple. (8th Reuters)

(Beiping) Bryingdalai, the commander of the Inner Mongolia Xilingol League Uqaan Guard, arrived in Beiping late at night under the order of Prince De to meet with Ho and Huang, reporting on the truth of the Inner Mongolia Autonomous Conference, and will also visit various Inner Mongolian princes in Beiping to discuss everything. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Huo Yunzhang, a member of the Suiyuan Provincial Party Department, and Bu Wenlin, a representative of the Inner Mongolia Smed Banner, arrived in Beiping tonight from Sui for the Inner Mongolia autonomy matter. After a short rest, they will go to Nanjing to discuss important matters. Bu said that as a result of the meeting between Prince De's representative and Huang in Sui, opinions on the Inner Mongolia autonomy issue have gradually become consistent. However, the date for Huang's visit to Bailing Temple has not yet been determined. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Bao Yueqing returned to Bailing Temple this afternoon, carrying Ho Yingqin's letter to Prince De. He will visit Huang when passing through Sui. (8th Dispatch)

Japanese Military Train Bombed in Beianzhen, 82 Japanese Soldiers Wounded, 91 Dead, Train and All Shells Destroyed

(Tianjin) According to transportation sources, a Japanese military train carrying 520 Japanese soldiers and a large number of shells was suddenly attacked by a Korean man holding eight bombs at the Beianzhen train station. The bombs hit the ammunition car and were ignited. According to the investigation results, 82 Japanese soldiers were wounded, 91 died, all the shells were destroyed, and five carriages of the train were bombed. The bomber escaped. (8th Central News Agency)

Kong Xiangxi Flies to Jiangxi

(Nanjing) Chairman Chiang, taking advantage of Wang's return to Nanjing, sent an aide on the same plane carrying a letter inviting Finance Minister Kong to Jiangxi for a meeting. After receiving the letter, Kong took a Ford aircraft to Jiangxi at 2:01 p.m., accompanied by Tan Guang, the secretary of the Ministry of Finance. According to Kong, there were many affairs to be handled in the ministry, so he will only stay in Jiangxi for one night and return to Nanjing on the same plane the next day. (8th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Finance Minister Kong arrived here at 5 p.m. on the 8th at the invitation of Chairman Chiang. He had dinner at Chiang's residence in Beitan at 7 p.m. and discussed financial issues for a long time. Kong will return to Nanjing within a few days. (8th Central News Agency)

Chiang Plans Reconstruction of Recovered Areas

(Nanjing) Chiang telegraphed the Economic Committee, health, highway, and other experts, inviting them to Jiangxi to plan the reconstruction of the recovered bandit areas. It is reported that they have all packed their luggage and are preparing to depart. Those traveling together include Dr. Stamp and Mr. Borcic, health commissioners of the League of Nations. The Health Experiment Department of the Economic Committee also sent Mei Yilin to accompany them. (8th Dispatch)

Entire Legislative Yuan Committee Requests Wang Report on Diplomacy

(Nanjing) The entire committee of the Legislative Yuan, in order to understand the current diplomatic policy held by the government, proposed at last Friday's general meeting to invite Premier Wang to report to the Yuan. At the same time, the Legislative Yuan has many opinions to offer to the government to serve as a reference for the government's handling of diplomacy. At that time, it was decided that President Sun would verbally agree on a date with Premier Wang. If it is not possible within this week, then Wang will be invited to attend the report next week. (8th Dispatch)

US Ambassador Johnson Arrives in Nanjing

(Nanjing) US Ambassador Johnson arrived in Nanjing at Shenshi on the 8th and is temporarily staying at the US Consulate in Saji Bay. He will stay in Nanjing for about four or five days and will first meet with Wang, the concurrent Foreign Minister. He has sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs requesting a meeting. (8th Dispatch)

Luo Wen'gan Arrives in Tianjin, Says the New Province Is Full of Good People, No Contact with Russian Diplomats, Diplomatic Opinions Are Inconvenient to Express, Scheduled to Go South to Nanjing Tonight and Then to Jiangxi Immediately, Determined to Resign from Both the Foreign Affairs and Justice Ministries

(Tianjin) Luo Wen'gan arrived outside Dagu Port at 5 p.m. on the 8th and immediately boarded the Haihai gunboat with his secretary Lin Donghai and Wang Lanjin, bringing four pieces of luggage and a hunting rifle. Luo was in good spirits. He arrived in Tanggu at 7:30 p.m., boarded a special train, and made a prepared speech to reporters from Beiping, Tianjin, Nanjing, Shanghai, and Wuhan. The special train departed at 9 p.m. Luo talked to reporters on the train as follows: Regarding diplomatic events, I am sorry that it is inconvenient for me to express my opinion. For example, when four people are playing cards, they are all scheming and cannot show their cards to others. I took a plane from Nanjing, passed through Shaanxi and entered Xinjiang, stayed in Dihua for five days, and then took the Touxi Railway to New Asia and then to Asia before arriving in Vladivostok. My impression of the Soviet Union is that everyone has a job and everyone has food to eat. Modern women who have no food to eat are despised. I telegraphed Dean Hu of Tianjin, setting the 8th as the date of arrival in Tianjin, but unexpectedly, the code was unclear and translated into the word "trap," causing everyone to wait for many days, which I deeply regret. My eye disease has healed, I eat three meals a day, I don't drink alcohol, and I don't know what pain is. The Sino-Russian Non-Aggression Treaty was carried out when I was in Nanjing. What I can tell you now is that because I entered Russian territory, I did not have any formal contact with Soviet diplomats. I don't understand Russian and cannot know the details of the Soviet Union's national conditions, but I know that its construction industry has made amazing progress. As far as the situation in the new province is concerned, I feel that they are all good people. Only with laws can they live and work in peace, and only if there is no war can there be construction. On August 27, Ma Zhongying and Sheng Shicai started a fire. When I arrived in the new province, I heard that Sheng had retreated to the provincial capital. I don't know what happened later. The climate on the new border is uneven. Morning, noon, evening, and night are like spring, summer, autumn, and winter. Jin Shuren used high-handed tactics against the people in the new province. The people in a certain city were all killed, causing the people in the new province to have no choice but to welcome foreigners with food and drink. I feel that Russia is not to be feared. What is to be feared is our own trouble. The current situation between China and Japan is like two men sleeping with one woman, which is already indecent, and to insist on talking about marriage is not a joke. I am determined to resign from both the Minister of Foreign Affairs and the Minister of Justice. He arrived in Tianjin at 10 p.m. and rested at the Six Nations Hotel. At 10:30 p.m., Hu Xianglin and Zhou Zuhai, the presidents of the Higher Court, hosted a welcome banquet at Dongxinglou. Luo is scheduled to go south to Nanjing on the night of the 9th and will go to Jiangxi immediately after arriving in Nanjing to visit Chiang. (8th Dispatch)

(Beiping) It is reported that Luo Wen'gan's mission for this inspection of Xinjiang was to investigate the contents of the secret agreement signed by Jin Shuren and the Soviet Union in Dihua in order to declare it invalid to Russia, and to expose Jin's crimes. After Luo arrives in Tianjin, he will come to Beiping for a while to meet with the authorities. (8th Dispatch)

Premier Wang Returns to Nanjing Yesterday, Ye Chucang Still Stays in Jiangxi

(Nanjing) Premier Wang, at the invitation of Chiang, went to Jiangxi on the afternoon of the 7th with Ye Chucang and Zeng Zhongwu on a Ford aircraft and arrived in Nanchang in the afternoon. He had an all-night talk with Chiang about important matters. On the morning of the 8th, he returned to Nanjing on the same plane with Zeng Zhongming. Zeng said that Premier Wang's trip at the invitation of Chairman Chiang was to discuss central affairs and there were no special matters. Because he had to attend a meeting, he returned to Nanjing today. Ye Chucang went to Jiangxi to inspect party affairs. He went along on the plane yesterday and is still in Jiangxi. He will return to Nanjing after the party affairs inspection is completed. (8th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Wang, Ye, and Zeng have finished discussing with Chiang on financial, internal affairs, bandit suppression, post-war reconstruction funds, Inner Mongolian autonomy, and various important government policies in the province, and will fly back to Nanjing on the same plane today. (8th Dispatch)

Beiping Military Branch Meeting, Huang and He Attend to Report

(Beiping) The Military Branch held a routine meeting this morning. More than ten people including He Yingqin, Bao Wenwei, Zou Zuohua, and Men Zhizhong attended. Huang attended as an observer. Chairman He reported on: (1) the progress of the negotiations on the war zone; (2) the Hebei Provincial Government should remit 500,000 yuan in monthly military expenses to the Military Branch, the Chahar Provincial Government should remit 300,000 yuan in military expenses, and the Beiping City should remit 50,000 yuan. Sui owes for many months and has requested exemption from payment. A telegram has been sent urging them to remit according to the monthly amount to maintain the source of funds. Next, Huang reported on the diplomatic process of the negotiations with Okamura on the North China war zone. (8th Dispatch)

Security Team Stationed in Miyun Opens Fire in the Western Part of the County to Defend Against Bandits

(Beiping) The headquarters of the Second Security Brigade of Miyun County, led by Xu Shiying, has decided to establish a joint association in the seventh district. A detachment will be sent to the Kanggezhuang area in the western part of the county to prevent bandits in the Dashuiyukou area. After the Japanese army in Shixiazhen withdrew to Rehe, the first detachment of the fifth squadron of the security team, led by squadron leader Zeng Zhan'ao, with about forty people, has now been dispatched to the town. (8th Dispatch)

He Jian Arrives in Pingxiang to Supervise Suppression, Xiao Ke's Remnant Bandits Completely Eliminated

(Changsha) He Jian arrived in Pingxiang on the 8th to supervise the suppression of bandits in western Jiangxi. (8th Dispatch)

(Changsha) He Jian telegraphed the Hunan-Jiangxi Provincial Government to allocate education funds for the recovered bandit areas, 2,000 yuan per county. Eight provinces will form a grain transportation and sales organization, with Hunan government officials and merchants each responsible for 100,000 yuan in capital. (8th Dispatch)

(Changsha) He Jian went to Pingxiang to supervise the suppression at 8 a.m. on the 8th, accompanied by He Haoruo, Ling Zhang, Qi Zhigan, and others. (8th Central News Agency)

(Hankou) He Jian telegraphed Wuhan, saying that Xiao Ke's remnant bandits who had fled to the Pingli Liling area have now been completely eliminated. (8th Central News Agency)

(Hong Kong) He Jian telegraphed Guangdong on the 6th, saying that on the 4th, Jiangxi bandits attempted to break through our army's defense line and were defeated by our army. The elite were almost all killed or wounded. The remnant bandits retreated to Yichun in western Jiangxi. In this battle, 500 enemy weapons were seized. I plan to go to Pingxiang on the 8th to inspect. (8th Dispatch)

Liu Xiang Orders the Five Route Army to Capture Suiding Within a Time Limit

(Hankou) Liu Xiang ordered the Five Route Army to capture Suiding within a time limit. Wang Lingji was ordered to lead several regiments in a fierce battle with the bandits at ShibanDian, 50 miles from the city, on the 4th. On the 5th, they advanced to MuguaPu, and on the 6th, they had approached Leiyinpu in the suburbs of Suiding and will be able to capture it within days. Also, the bandits divided into two routes, one attacking Kaijiang Yongxingchang and the other attacking Qilixia, but both were repelled. They are stubbornly defending the Donglin River, and both Bemiaochang, Nanba, and Guanyinshan have built fortifications to prevent the advance of the national army. (8th Dispatch)

Chen and Jiang Leave Hong Kong for Fujian

(Hong Kong) Chen Mingshu and Jiang Guangnai left Hong Kong on the Jinan wheel at 5 p.m. on the 8th to go to the country. Zhang Yan accompanied them. Chen and Jiang talked on the verge of departure, saying that they had been summoned by Lin Sen to return to Fujian to discuss the current situation. After arriving in Fujian, they will convene an important meeting. (8th Dispatch)

(Fuzhou) Jiang Guangnai left Hong Kong on the 8th, passed through Xiamen, and will first go to Zhangzhou to meet with Cai and then fly to the province. Lin Sen was still touring Fuqing yesterday. Today, a naval brigade will be waiting at the Haikou. Lin will turn to Changle to inspect Lianbing Port. He may be able to go to the province tomorrow. He will return to Nanjing after meeting with Chiang. (8th Dispatch)

Current Commentary

Rectifying Military Discipline

— Ren

It is reported that Chairman Chiang has issued a strict order to rectify military discipline in order to eliminate the malpractices of the army. He has warned officers and soldiers to treat the people as if they were wounded and not to arbitrarily extort money from the people by relying on force. These words are not only what the people of the country are eagerly hoping for at the moment, but also have extremely important significance on this day when bandits are rampant and the army is advancing to suppress them. Therefore, I dare to borrow Chairman Chiang's words to discuss it.

Our country supports an army of 2.7 million, which costs the national treasury 340 million yuan annually, accounting for more than 80% of the total annual expenditure. The conscription of troops stationed in other provinces is not included. The only hope of the people, who exhaust their efforts to support the army, is that the army will be the armed force of the people themselves, able to defend the country and maintain the local people. However, looking back at the facts of the past twenty years, the army not only does not serve as the armed force of the people, but also participates in civil wars, often causing the people in the war zone to suffer the pain of family ruin and death. Even in peacetime, there are unavoidable acts of bullying. As Chairman Chiang said, those who arbitrarily extort money by relying on force cause the people to fear officers and soldiers like tigers, and a gap arises between the people and the army.

Therefore, today, if military discipline can be rectified, the people will be like clouds in a great drought. If each division and brigade can refrain from even the slightest offense while advancing to suppress bandits in the bandit areas, and everywhere comfort the victims of disasters, show sympathy for the difficult, and comfort the sick, then not only can the past impression of the people towards the army be changed, but also the great effect of integrating the people and the army can be achieved. The facts of cooperation between the army and the people during the Northern Expedition in the past are still vividly in our memory.

So, what is the crux of the problem of why military discipline is not strict? Today's general commentators often say that soldiers have low levels of knowledge, or that soldiers' salaries are meager. These are all reasonable points. However, can soldiers with low levels of knowledge be absolutely impossible to use well? Can meager salaries be absolutely impossible to maintain their lives? We believe that soldiers with low levels of knowledge, if they have good officers to guide them, make them understand the great righteousness of patriotism, and do not drive them as private tools, can also be transformed into useful and healthy children of the country. As for the meager salaries, under today's living standards, if the soldiers' due salaries can be paid out monthly, then even if they cannot have a rich life, they will not suffer from hunger and cold. What is worrying is that the soldiers' salaries are already meager, but they are also intercepted by officers, or even dragged on for years without being paid. Then the soldiers will truly have no way to maintain their lives, and the idea of illegality will arise. The fault lies in the officers' poor training and their exclusive focus on self-interest without considering the soldiers. Moreover, if the generals are focused on promotion and fortune, then their thoughts of loving the country and loving the people are less, and they have no time to consider the deep relationship between the people and the army. As a result, the phenomenon of the people and the army being separated into two is formed.

Therefore, in seeking the rectification of military discipline today, we believe that the officers of each army should first suddenly awaken and strive to eliminate the mistakes of the past. Then, with strict military orders, rectify the troops and change the accumulated abuses of the past. The masses and the army can love, be close to, and help each other, and then the army and the masses can become one. Then the army will truly become the armed force of the people. In this way, not only can the victory of suppressing bandits be expected, but also foreign insults will not be feared. May the generals of each army deeply understand Chairman Chiang's words.

The relationship between Japan and Russia is increasingly dangerous.

Russia's Leader Blatantly Expresses Himself, Causing Great Unease in Japan and Korea: Considered a Deliberate Challenge, Ambassador to Russia May Be Recalled

(Tokyo) On the 6th, the Soviet Union held a grand meeting commemorating the 16th anniversary of the October Revolution. Molotov, Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars, delivered a speech at the meeting, believing that an attack by Japan was unavoidable and that the Soviet Union was always fully prepared for a sudden attack by Japan. The sole responsibility of the Red Army was to completely defeat the enemy and ensure its victory. After Molotov's speech, which highly praised the Red Army, reached Japan, all sectors of society were indignant at the Soviet Union's arrogant and challenging attitude. Government authorities also attached great importance to the matter, stating their attitude toward Russia. The entire nation should not be misled by talk of Russo-Japanese friendship, but should quickly establish a complete national policy toward Russia. The government believes that Molotov's speech was a second tactic to challenge Japan, aimed at gaining a favorable position, after the previous incident of the "strange document" had no major impact on Japan. His intentions are as follows: (1) At the time when Litvinov was visiting the United States to begin negotiations on the re-establishment of US-Soviet relations, he deliberately released an atmosphere of worsening Japanese-Russian relations in order to force the United States to recognize the Soviet Union, as a strategy to contain Japan. (2) To stimulate the Japanese military to actively carry out war preparations against Russia, inducing anti-military sentiment among the Japanese people, with the aim of creating internal turmoil in Japan. If the Japanese authorities take such remarks from the Russian side as domestic policy teaching and stand idly by, it will only allow the Soviet Union to inflate its arrogance and promote Soviet ideology to the world, which will inevitably lead to major events between the two countries. This is a very obvious fact. At this important juncture, the Japanese government and the public should quickly unify national opinion and express important intentions to the Soviet Union, namely, to implement countermeasures against the Soviet Union's political and diplomatic aims focused on "strength." Unless the Soviet Union changes its challenging attitude toward Japan, it will consistently respond with a tough policy toward Russia. The first step of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' plan is to urgently recall Ambassador to Russia Ota to hear about the actual situation in Russia and to study what attitude the Soviet Union will adopt toward Japan in the future. On the surface, Russo-Japanese relations are disguised as peaceful through the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, but in reality, the undercurrents between the two countries are gradually emerging. (8th, United News Agency)

Japanese Authorities Deliberately Show Calm, Claiming It Was Intended for Domestic Consumption

(Tokyo) The sharp speech made by Molotov, Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, yesterday, is not given much importance here, as it is intended to divert the people's, especially the farmers', attention from their own suffering. Spokesmen for both the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of the Army stated that Molotov's speech was not worth mentioning and was unlikely to disturb the Japanese people. Japanese newspapers also completely ignored it. The spokesman for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs said, "We do not pay attention to what Molotov said. We cannot interfere with his thinking." When asked if Molotov intended to sway the United States, the spokesman replied, "The United States is very wise and will not be swayed by Molotov. Molotov's remarks first attacked France, then England, then the Vatican, and then Japan. I really do not understand his true intentions." The spokesman for the Ministry of the Army said, "The people of the Soviet Union are suffering unspeakably from the brutal implementation of the Five-Year Plan, not to mention the invasion of famine. Molotov's remarks are intended to stabilize people's hearts, and since rebellions have occurred in several places in the Soviet Union, Molotov suddenly issued a speech challenging Japan, in fact, to shift the people's attention abroad and forget their domestic suffering. The Soviet Union is now concentrating troops on the border between Biran and 'Manchukuo' and is dealing with Japan by destroying international credibility. This is very noteworthy." (8th, Reuters)

Full Text of Molotov's Speech

(Moscow) The Moscow Soviet held a solemn meeting yesterday to commemorate the 16th anniversary of the October Revolution. Representatives from various agencies, factories, and trade unions attended. Stalin, Molotov, Kalinin, Kaganovich, and several members of the Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union presided over the meeting. The audience welcomed them warmly as they took their seats. Then, Molotov, Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars, delivered the main speech. He began by saying that the great achievements of the First Five-Year Plan had been summarized at the beginning of this year, and there was no need to repeat the results. In the past October alone, the results and victories of the First Five-Year Plan have been fully demonstrated, which is only the beginning of the Soviet Union's success. At present, there is no other country in the world that is carrying out construction work like the Soviet Union. Only the Soviet Union is diligently engaged in construction work, investing millions to develop industry and consolidate national power. At the same time, the panic in capitalist countries has not diminished, and various attempts to continue to reduce this panic have not been successful. Capitalism has indeed failed to find a way out of panic. The number of countries ruled by the bourgeoisie and fascist forces has been increasing, and they have incited the reactionary forces of the bourgeoisie, ignited the dim enthusiasm of nationalism, and frankly exposed the entire essence of their policies. At the same time, they have revealed the fact that the possibility of getting out of panic by reorganizing internally is decreasing, so they are increasingly devoted to war and the competition of armaments. As for the Soviet Union, it has always implemented its policy of consolidating friendship with various countries and has mobilized all its strength to oppose war and strive for peace." Molotov then elaborated on several issues concerning the economic life of the Soviet Union, saying, "To this day, we have been able to steadily increase the productivity of a large number of new and old factories and industrial sectors that have sprung up in recent years." When Molotov mentioned the development of agriculture, he elaborated on the achievements of collective farms, saying that the state has collected 100 million poods of grain, which has exceeded the total amount of the entire year last year. When Molotov discussed the Soviet Union's foreign policy, he emphasized that even most of the Soviet Union's enemies have had to admit the Soviet government's peaceful policy, which has always been the foundation of the Soviet Union's foreign policy. The Soviet Union's foreign policy is directly linked to the success of economic and cultural construction, which has greatly consolidated the Soviet Union's international position. From this point of view, President Roosevelt's proposal to the Soviet government to appoint representatives to discuss US-Soviet relations is very important. The significance of the negotiations between Roosevelt and Litvinov is not limited to the United States and the Soviet Union, but also has international importance. We do not want to guess what the outcome of the Washington talks will be. Kalinin's reply has strongly stated our position, saying that if there are or will be various difficulties between the two countries, these difficulties "can undoubtedly only be resolved when there is direct contact between the two countries. Conversely, if this contact is lacking, these difficulties can never be resolved." I would like to express this belief that the meeting between Litvinov and the US President will have a satisfactory result for the interests of both countries and world peace. However, although the Soviet Union is loyal to its peaceful policy, the implementation of this policy does not only depend on ourselves. At present, the danger of military attacks on us is particularly serious, so we must pay special attention to the imperialist plans to disrupt peace, the situation in the Far East, and our relations with Japan. These issues, whether in the past or now, are issues of particular concern to our workers. Our policy in the Far East and our relations with our neighbors in the Far East will always be peaceful, and we will strive to maintain peaceful relations with them. Examples include the request for Japan to sign a non-aggression pact and the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway. We will not change this policy at present. However, we must take into account the Manchurian Incident, the destruction of the agreements concluded with us, and the fact that the policy of destroying these agreements is being vigorously implemented. We understand that our task is to expose the truth of all such actions, thoroughly defend the interests of the Soviet Union, and always protect the borders of the Soviet Union. When we read the ridiculous plans of some Japanese dignitaries to seize Siberia and the coastal areas, and when these arguments and plans beneficial to them become more and more frank and shameless, we have to pay close attention to them. "The Manchurian government is not an important factor in these issues. The world knows that Japan is the actual master of Manchukuo, and the responsibility should also be borne by Japan." Molotov then spoke about some of the remarks made by the Japanese, saying that Europeans thought it was too stupid to declare war before starting military action. Molotov then said, "These gentlemen are in favor of launching a sudden attack on the Soviet Union as soon as possible. We cannot ignore these remarks. They are forcing us to fully prepare for this unexpected and serious attack. We have considered these facts in the necessary ways. We are now convinced that our main task is to expose all adventurous actions that disrupt peace, strengthen the Red Army and national defense, and vigorously implement a policy of peace and good-neighborly relations with our neighbors. If the time for the enemy to attack the Soviet Union comes, our only task will be to completely defeat the enemy and achieve the victory of our Red Army. The imperialists' preparations for war are not only expanding in the East, but also in the West. When we pay attention to these events, we must observe the events in the Far East with special attention. We have strengthened and are strengthening the strength of the Red Army. We are convinced that these military leaders will understand what it means to succumb to this invincible Red Army when the necessary opportunity arises." Molotov's speech ended in cheers from the entire audience. (7th, TASS)

Japanese Ronin Disgrace the National Image by Planting Opium in Leased Territory in East Africa; Japanese Representative Declares That This Did Not Happen

(Geneva) It was rumored that the East African country of Abyssinia wanted to lease land to Japan to plant opium. At a meeting of the Opium Advisory Committee yesterday, the Japanese representative declared that this was not true. Today, the Secretariat of the League of Nations issued a special bulletin, mentioning the declaration of the Japanese representative yesterday, stating that the rumor of Abyssinia leasing land to plant opium originated from a telegram published in the Osaka Asahi Shimbun, which was done by a ronin named Kitagawa. The bulletin concluded by saying that the Japanese representative of the Opium Advisory Committee believed that it was regrettable that this kind of ronin conspiracy incident had resulted in rumors that disgraced Japan's national image. He hoped that this statement would be sufficient to dispel all misunderstandings, and he hoped that the official declaration of the Japanese representative would be heard by the international press. (8th, Havas)

(Geneva) The Japanese representative to the Opium Advisory Committee, Yokoyama, issued an important statement today regarding the rumor that Japan had obtained a concession in Abyssinia to plant poppies. According to the statement, he had sent a telegram to Tokyo inquiring about the details because the news had caused reasonable alarm. He has now learned that a destitute adventurer named Kida claimed to have obtained a concession in Abyssinia in order to glorify himself. This is a strategy that cannot be believed. He wishes to inform the world to dispel doubts. In any case, the Abyssinian government must prohibit the planting of poppies within its borders. This afternoon, the Opium Committee passed a draft of articles inquiring about the implementation of Chapter 4 of the Hague Convention, which will be sent to the Chinese government and the authorities of the leased territories in China. The draft report mentions the current situation in China, especially the danger of establishing secret drug manufacturing plants in the area, which is a source of great concern for China and the world. (7th, Reuters)

Japanese Goods Infiltrate Everywhere and Develop into Iraq

(London) The Department of Commerce received a report from the commercial counselor of the British Embassy in Iraq, which was released this morning. It stated that Japanese goods are competing in the Iraqi market and are developing greatly. Cotton merchants who used to trade with Manchester in England are now mostly purchasing goods from Japan, and the Iraqi government has also changed its source of supply for the cloth used to make military uniforms to Tokyo. The commercial counselor pointed out several figures to prove the increase in Japanese exports to Iraq. Compared to the 1930-31 and 1931-32 fiscal years, Japanese cloth imports to Iraq increased from 298,000 meters to 325,000 meters, but British cloth exports to Iraq remained the same. (8th, Havas)

Roosevelt Receives Russian Foreign Minister in White House Blue Room: Conversation Filled with Friendly Spirit; US-Soviet Diplomatic Recognition to Be Realized Soon

(Washington) Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov arrived at Union Station in this city at 3:45 this afternoon. US Secretary of State Hull and other dignitaries were at the station to welcome him. Litvinov then went to the White House at 5:20 and was received by the US President in the Blue Room of the White House. Afterwards, according to Litvinov's remarks to reporters, he was deeply moved by the President's sincere attitude and friendly spirit. He had issued a statement when he landed in Jersey City this morning, saying that he was confident that an agreement could be reached soon, including a commercial treaty that would hopefully greatly increase trade between the two sides. Now that he has paid a visit to the President tonight, he feels that his statement was not overly optimistic. (7th, National Telegram)

(Washington) According to today's news, the first purpose of Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov's mission to the United States is to restore Russian-American relations and to conclude a commercial treaty as soon as possible. Other issues, such as the non-aggression pact, the elimination of malicious propaganda, and the claims for compensation by the Russian and American people, will be left to diplomats to handle. It is heard that the former Russian ambassador to Japan, Troyanovsky, may be appointed as the first Russian ambassador to the United States. It is also heard that President Roosevelt has decided not to seek a formal treaty in the current negotiations. (8th, Reuters)

(Washington) Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov has had his first meeting with President Roosevelt, lasting 20 minutes. It was purely a courtesy visit. Most people believe that the United States will recognize Russia in a matter of hours. The issue of prohibiting the propagation of communism seems easy to resolve, while the debts owed to the United States by the Imperial Russian and Provisional governments are more difficult to resolve, as the Soviet government has always refused to acknowledge debts of a political nature incurred by previous Russian governments. Regarding commercial issues, it is generally believed that the Soviet Union can place orders in the American market for as much as $100 million, but cannot pay in cash immediately. The American side may allow credit for 10 to 15 years. It is generally believed that Russia will order the first batch of goods starting this week, namely wheat, seeds, and livestock. Before visiting Roosevelt, Litvinov declared to the press that his talks with the President would proceed smoothly because "the Soviet Union has countless precedents for restoring diplomatic relations with other countries and establishing peaceful cooperation, which can be used as a reference. The United States and Russia are about to discuss various issues, which can be used as examples." This shows that the Soviet Union's view on the war debt issue will not change because of the United States. (7th, Havas)

Litvinov Makes a Statement in New York, Saying That There Is Absolutely No Possibility of Conflict Between the Two Countries and That He Has Infinite Hope for the Future of Diplomatic Relations

(New York) Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov arrived here at 9:30 this morning. He was greeted on board by the director of the State Department's Office of Protocol and various dignitaries concerned about US-Russian relations. The reception ceremony was the same as that for envoys sent by countries that the United States has already recognized. Litvinov told reporters that he very much hoped that after the restoration of US-Russian diplomatic relations, he would be able to achieve "genuine disarmament." When asked about the mission of his visit, Litvinov replied, "I will not negotiate any treaties during my visit to the United States." He then took a ferry to Jersey City, where he transferred to a special train to Washington. Before the train departed, Litvinov declared to reporters, "I have infinite hope for the mission of this trip and the future of US-Russian diplomatic relations. The two countries have no disputes in history and will not have any conflicts in the future. Moreover, both countries control natural resources with human power to meet human needs. Therefore, the United States and Russia, as the most technologically advanced countries in the world, have a mutual attraction. All we have to do is to find a way to formally recognize this mutual attraction. The two countries have a solid foundation for cooperation in economics, technology, and culture. If we can develop it, it will be beneficial to both countries. The only thing both countries hope for is peace." (7th, Havas)

Train Arrives in Washington, Hull Welcomes at the Station

(Washington) Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov has arrived here. Only a few official representatives of the press were allowed to enter the station. Secretary of State Hull welcomed him at the station, exchanging pleasantries. Others who came to the station to greet him included Under Secretary of State Phillips and Roosevelt's personal representative, McIntyre. The station was crowded with onlookers on both sides. When Litvinov left the station, he was protected by more than 100 police officers. (7th, Havas)

US-Russian Relations: White House Makes Preparations in Advance

(Washington) As Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov disembarked in New York, several people in the US official circles gathered to discuss US-Russian relations. Secretary of State Hull, Director of the Agricultural Relief Bureau Morgenthau, and Assistant Secretary of State Berle will all participate when the President meets with Litvinov. Therefore, preparations were made in advance. After the meeting, Secretary of State Hull went to the White House to pay a visit to the President. (7th, Havas)

British-American Negotiations Suspended to Handle Debts to Russia

(Washington) After the British-American war debt negotiations were announced today that Britain would pay a small amount of promissory notes in mid-December, they were effectively suspended, and Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov arrived here this afternoon to discuss another, more complex debt issue in preparation for the restoration of US-Russian diplomatic relations. When the White House announced the suspension of British-American negotiations, it stated that the British war debt issue could not be resolved due to the turbulent world situation, so it had accepted the British method of paying promissory notes. The President will not recognize Britain's failure to fulfill its debt obligations, and this suspension of negotiations does not prevent any government from negotiating in the future. (7th, National Telegram)

Czechoslovakia Prepares to Recognize Soviet Russia, Dutch Government Unchanged

Prague The movement within the Czech Republic to legally recognize the Soviet government has shown signs for some time, and recently the Czech government has also expressed its approval. The outline of this movement is becoming increasingly clear. (7th, Havas)

The Hague The Dutch government replied to the Communist Party's question in the Second Chamber today, stating that the Dutch government will not recognize Soviet Russia. Although a certain country will restore diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia, the Dutch government will not change its will because of this. (8th, National Telegram)

US Fleet to Patrol the Atlantic Next Summer and Return to the Pacific in Early Autumn

San Francisco It was heard tonight that the US fleet will begin patrolling the Atlantic on April 9 next year and will return to the Pacific in early autumn. According to the plan released here, once the ships have gathered in the ports of San Pedro and San Diego and are ready, they will depart. They will arrive in New York around June 1. After conducting a large-scale patrol in the Atlantic, they will leave the Atlantic on August 1 and return to their Pacific base on September 1. (7th, National Telegram)

French Air Force Flies Through Colonies in Africa, Twenty-Seven Aircraft Continue to Depart

Istre Twenty-seven French military aircraft, under the command of General Fuleran, departed from here at 7:47 this morning to fly around the African colonies for a week, a journey of 25,000 kilometers before returning. (8th, National Telegram)

Asian Birth Control Conference to Be Held in London in Late November; Duncombe Joins as Sponsor

(London) The Asian Birth Control Conference will be held in London on the 24th and 25th of this month. The venue will be the London School of Hygiene and Tropical Medicine. The chairman will be Sir Holford, chairman of the British Birth Control Federation. Sponsors include Guo Taiqi, Gu Weijun, Mrs. Sanger, an American who strongly advocates birth control, Mrs. Ishimoto, a Japanese baroness, and Roso, among other celebrities. The motivation for convening this conference was that the American Birth Control Federation recently received letters from Chinese and English doctors and social workers in India and China, inquiring about birth control methods, so this conference was specially convened to allow for open discussion. (7th, Reuters)

Disarmament Senior Executives Meet Today; No Representatives from Italian and French Governments Attend; Simon Cancels Trip to Geneva at Last Minute

(Paris) The Presidium of the Disarmament Conference is scheduled to reconvene on the 9th of this month. British Foreign Secretary Simon will fly to Geneva tomorrow to participate. He will arrive here in the afternoon and will stay briefly to discuss disarmament issues with Prime Minister Sarraut and Foreign Minister Pangou. (7th, Havas)

(London) Foreign Secretary Simon was originally scheduled to fly to Geneva at noon today to attend the meeting of the Presidium of the Disarmament Conference. He also planned to meet with French Prime Minister Sarraut and Foreign Minister Pangou when passing through Paris. Now Simon has canceled his trip to Geneva. According to official sources, the French and Italian governments will not have representatives attending the meeting of the Armaments Presidium, so Simon made the above decision. (8th, Havas)

(Geneva) The Presidium of the Disarmament Conference is scheduled to meet at 3:30 p.m. tomorrow. Chairman Henderson will return here tonight to chair tomorrow's meeting. It is expected that after exchanging views on the working procedures at tomorrow's meeting, the Presidium will divide the work listed in the agenda into various committees, which will meet separately next week to discuss them. In addition, the technical staff of the Disarmament Conference's Military Expenditure Committee has completed the first reading and discussion of the draft of the budgetary supervision system. This draft is based on the principle of announcing national defense expenditures stipulated in the resolution of the Disarmament Conference on June 8 this year. The second reading of this draft by the technical staff is expected to be submitted to the general council of the Disarmament Committee in December. (8th, Havas)

Hitler Scheduled to Give Nationwide Radio Address Tomorrow to Awaken Public Support for Current Government; Withdrawal from League of Nations to Be Decided by Public Vote; Cabinet Reorganization Rumors Are Nonsense

(Berlin) This Friday, the 5th, will be the climax of this parliamentary election and the referendum on Germany's withdrawal from the League of Nations. On that afternoon, from 1:00 p.m. to 2:00 p.m., all factories across the country will stop work for one hour and gather in public places to listen to the radio broadcast of Prime Minister Hitler's speech. The general idea of ​​Hitler's speech is to awaken the unanimous support of the entire German people for the current government, to strive for equality and peace in the world, and to express the unity of the entire German people. At the same time, when Germany hears the bell ringing once, all traffic will stop, all pedestrians will stop, and be silent for one minute. All factories will sound their sirens to report the start of the Prime Minister's speech. Furthermore, this speech will also be broadcast simultaneously in all schools and homes, so it can be said to be an unprecedented broadcasting demonstration. It is also heard that President Hindenburg will also deliver a speech to the nation on Saturday, which is his first since his speech on the last Labor Day, so it is especially valued by the people. (7th, National Telegram)

(Berlin) Recently, there have been rumors that the German cabinet will be reorganized after the general election in Germany on the 12th of this month. According to reliable sources here, this statement is completely unfounded. The German cabinet is still unanimously supporting Hitler's policies, and it can be said that there is internal and external unity, and there is no talk of wavering. (7th, National Telegram)

Hitler's Autographed Letter of Regards

Rome: When Prussian Prime Minister Hermann Göring of Germany met with Italian Prime Minister Benito Mussolini today, he presented Mussolini with an autographed letter from German Chancellor Adolf Hitler. Subsequently, the Italian Prime Minister issued a statement saying that the autographed letter from the German Chancellor expressed gratitude to Mussolini for his efforts in the equal management of international relations and stated Germany's current position on the issue of disarmament. It is said that during Göring's meeting with Mussolini, he also elaborated on Germany's position in detail and the talks lasted for a long time. Mussolini held a grand banquet on Tuesday to entertain Göring, who will leave Italy tomorrow morning to return to Germany. The Italian public also attaches great importance to Göring's mission to Italy this time. (National Telegram, 7th)

Rome: People here unanimously believe that Prussian Prime Minister Göring's visit to Italy is the first step in Germany's awakening. After Germany withdrew from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference, other countries ignored it. Germany realized that it could not remain isolated diplomatically for long. Italian officials believe that Göring's visit is not only to seek assistance from the Italian government, but also has a more concrete purpose. Italy has close ties with Britain and France, and Germany wants to use the Four-Power Pact to leverage Italy's power to approach Britain and France. (Havas Telegram, 8th)

British House of Commons Debates Germany's Withdrawal from the League: Simon Claims the Door to Mediation Remains Open, Eden Defends France's Position, Conservatives Criticize Germany as Warlike, Liberal Party Alone Expresses Sympathy for Germany, French Foreign Minister Reintroduces Arms Control System, Hoping for Unified Action by All Countries Against Germany

(London) British Foreign Secretary Simon, at the reopening of Parliament today, first debated disarmament, saying that although the situation is serious, some speakers have exaggerated. Britain seeks calmness and does not know what is called panic. There is no reason for Hitler to dissolve the parliament and hold elections when he withdraws from the League of Nations, taking such alarming means. The German Foreign Minister Neurath's speech yesterday criticizing the League of Nations shows that this kind of step has long been planned. Britain's failure to promote disarmament has greatly reduced its own military strength. The Labour leader Cripps's claim that Britain has taken no action is not true. Those who request fair treatment for Germany must not forget that Britain should also receive fair treatment. Britain has been at the forefront of restoring Germany's equal status, eliminating discrimination against Germany, and making Germany a member of the League of Nations and a member of the Administrative Council. Moreover, Britain has been instrumental in the withdrawal of troops from the Rhineland, and the history of reparations from the Dawes Plan to Lausanne is another evidence of Britain's actions. The Four-Power Pact has stipulated the principle of German equality, but Germany's recent declarations have made international disarmament work even more difficult. What is gratifying is that France and Italy have recently drawn closer. Britain's greatest purpose is to carry out disarmament. Britain will use its moral authority to seek friendship and peace among all countries. Simon reiterated his defense of Britain's actions to promote disarmament, stating that Germany could revoke its decision to withdraw from the League of Nations, and that all countries must sincerely hope that events will allow Germany to rejoin the League of Nations. Many events will occur in the next two years, and Britain will devote all its efforts to reconciliation. After consulting with French jurists, the British government now holds a view on the effectiveness of the Locarno Treaty, believing that the withdrawal of any country from this treaty does not release other countries from their obligations. If Germany does withdraw from this treaty, it will raise issues of a very serious nature, which cannot be publicly stated without careful consideration and consultation with other countries. He advised the people of the country not to regard the door currently closed by Germany as having been locked and bolted. Britain must use every opportunity to engage with Germany, just as it engages with other signatories of the Locarno Treaty. Former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain spoke out against Germany's warmongering spirit, saying that the Treaty of Versailles did not stipulate that the victorious countries would disarm to the same extent as the defeated countries, but hoped that German disarmament would be the first step towards general arms limitation. Liberal leader George spoke, citing various figures to show the increase in armaments after the war, saying that since the conclusion of the Locarno Treaty, France has increased cannons and bombers by 50 percent. In 1914, France had 35,000 tons of pursuit ships, but today it has increased to 198,000 tons. The United States had 40,000 tons of destroyers in 1914, but now it has increased to 259,000 tons. However, the United States and France are talking about peace more than other countries. France has increased its military budget twice after the signing of the Locarno Treaty, and the United States has also increased it from 590 million yuan to 709 million yuan. George also said that it is unknown to the world that Germany cannot manufacture cannons, so there is no reason to stipulate a trial period. Former Naval Minister, Conservative Party member Amery, said that Germany is now rearming, and no one can stop it. It is urgent to reconsider British policy. Britain should no longer entangle France and others to make them participate in disarmament. Britain should no longer interfere too much in European affairs, but should strengthen ties with the United States to deal with matters in British autonomous territories. Former Finance Minister, Conservative Party member Churchill, spoke, refuting George's defense of Germany, saying that the philosophy of bloodshed is now being injected into the hearts of German youth, and it is no wonder that neighboring countries are terrified by it. Britain should not leave the European League of Nations, but should speak to Germany collectively. All countries should collectively relieve Germany of some of its suffering, and not wait until its military equipment is restored to a stage where it can endanger world peace. Undersecretary of State for Foreign Affairs Eden then rose to make concluding remarks, saying that if Europe had accepted the British disarmament convention in March of this year, we could have reduced the term of military service to eight months, and all heavy artillery and tanks could have been abolished. If a plan to manage civil aviation could be drafted, then land, sea, and air forces could also disappear. Some people have pointed out that British arms factories are thriving because of the development of the automobile business. A certain manufacturer said that slums were destroyed by explosives, which greatly increased its business. The crowd was amused by this. Eden continued, saying that Britain had previously promulgated a very effective system to manage the export of military supplies. Britain is still doing so. Eden later defended France, saying that France was not the one who left the meeting, so we must speak cautiously. While we want to be fair to Germany, we cannot be unfair to other parties. Eden concluded by saying that there is no reason to be disappointed. Today's debate has shown that isolation has no friends. Germany's previous accession to the League of Nations was largely promoted by British policy. Britain still hopes that Germany can withdraw its notice of withdrawal before the two-year notice period expires. Thus, the debate in the House of Commons ended with this optimistic remark. (Reuters Telegram, 7th)

(Paris) Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour today explained to the Senate France's foreign policy after Germany's withdrawal from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference. Paul-Boncour explained the changes that have taken place in the plan for mutual and permanent universal arms control, and said that some countries have already approved the principle that the arms control system should be tested for several years. Unexpectedly, when the Paris consideration method was gradually determined by the presidium of the Disarmament Conference, Germany suddenly withdrew from the conference. Regarding the rearmament of Germany, Paul-Boncour said that all countries must first take unified diplomatic action to prevent it. Paul-Boncour concluded that the French government is paying close attention to this issue, and at the same time has ordered all embassies to pay attention at all times. The General Committee of the Disarmament Conference will still discuss this matter on December 4. (Havas Telegram, 7th)

Street Fights Erupt in New York City Mayoral Election, Nothing More Than a Struggle for Jobs, La Guardia Elected Mayor

(New York) La Guardia was elected Mayor of New York City with approximately 200,000 votes. (Reuters Telegram, 7th)

(New York) Today's mayoral election here was the most intense and disorderly competition seen in decades. Mayoral candidate La Guardia, in a fit of rage, actually fought with 20 thugs from the Tammany Hall party in the streets, and there were also fierce clashes in various electoral districts of Greater New York City. The New York City government has been controlled by the Tammany Hall party for a long time. If the current mayor, O'Brien, whom they support, fails, more than several thousand people will lose their jobs. Therefore, in this three-way election, they must fight to the death. Therefore, they widely dispatched party members to intimidate voters from other parties or prevent them from voting. Today, La Guardia personally patrolled the streets to investigate whether there were any intimidation of voters. When he arrived in a certain district, he saw 20 Tammany Hall thugs in front of a polling station, pushing away voters from other parties, and some of them were wearing the insignia of Curry or McKee. Because he wanted to call the police to intervene, but there were no police nearby, and he was familiar with boxing, in a fit of rage, he personally got out of the car and swung several punches, and all 20 thugs were defeated. When the police arrived after being summoned, they arrested most of these people. Similar fights also occurred on other thoroughfares, but the leaders of the election campaigns of La Guardia and McKee were not as powerful as La Guardia, and were mostly beaten and injured. However, the Tammany Hall party also claimed that some of its members had been beaten, and claimed that some street fights were started by the opposing party, hoping to gain the sympathy of the public. According to the report when the vote count was nearing completion at 11:00 PM tonight, La Guardia had won a great victory, having obtained 329,191 votes. His strong opponent McKee (independent Democratic candidate) only had 249,754 votes, and the Tammany Hall candidate O'Brien only had 238,205 votes. La Guardia is a Republican candidate, and many Republican figures support him. (National Telegram, 7th)

Voting Results in Various U.S. States: Opening Alcohol Prohibition Prevails

(New York) The states of Utah, Washington, and Pennsylvania have all voted in favor of repealing prohibition. As of now, 36 states oppose prohibition, which is the necessary two-thirds majority required to amend the Constitution. After the state conferences formally accept Amendment 21 repealing Article 18 of the Constitution on December 5, the sale of alcohol will no longer be illegal. (Reuters Telegram, 8th)

Specialist from Academia Sinica Collects Meteorites and Takes Them to Nanjing: Fell in Shadun Township, Dangtu, Three Times Heavier Than Ordinary Rocks

(Nanjing) Zhang Zuwang, dispatched by Academia Sinica to Dangtu to collect meteorites, took them to Nanjing today. According to him, a large number of meteorites did fall in the area from Shadun Township, Bowang Town, to Changliuzui on the evening of the 23rd of last month. The larger ones were as big as a dou (a Chinese peck measure), and the smaller ones were as small as fists. Before they fell, a strong sound like an airplane passing by was heard in the sky, and purple-green lightning was seen at the same time. The meteorites fell one after another, covering an area of 15 li (a Chinese unit of distance). Fortunately, the area is located near Shijiu Lake and is a remote area. Most of the meteorites fell into the lake and in the fields, so no one was injured. The people in the area, fearing that they were violent, mostly threw them into Shijiu Lake. Later, after explanation by those who knew a little science, they thought they were rare commodities and collected them one after another. The heads of villages and towns offered ten pieces for research in Nanjing. According to reports, these meteorites are small meteors in the sky and move without any regular pattern. Sometimes they can be attracted by large meteors. However, these meteorites may have been hit by other meteors, causing them to fall after being agitated in the air. At the same time, they rub against the atmosphere in the air, so a very loud noise is heard. The meteorites are oddly black in color and have no luster and are uneven. Compared to ordinary rocks, the specific gravity is about equal to three. Academia Sinica plans to cut these meteorites into thin slices or grind them into fine powder for detailed and in-depth study so that they can understand their construction. It is also reported that meteorites have been found in Hangzhou and Anhui. The academy will continue to send people to investigate, conduct further research, and compile a systematic report for researchers' reference. (Special Telegram, 8th)

An Official of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission on the Opinions of the Department of Border Affairs

(Nanjing) An official of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission said that the system of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission is not good, and the intention to change it to the Department of Border Affairs is sincere. I have found that the biggest drawback of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission is that its internal organization is not centered on political affairs, but on various boundaries. The establishment of Mongolian and Tibetan affairs offices not only provides a target for the old and new factions of the Mongolian and Tibetan ethnic groups to compete for power, but also causes traces of ethnic division, which is very inappropriate. When changing to a department, this pattern should be eliminated. The Central Government should set up the Department of Border Affairs to handle border affairs, and it should not contain ethnic boundaries or border concepts. In particular, border affairs should be regarded as an integral part of the Central Government's political issues, and should include all ethnic groups in the Northwest and Southwest, not only handle Mongolian and Tibetan affairs, which is not helpful to the reality. Based on this reason, the internal organization of the Department of Border Affairs should be completely centered on political affairs, and various divisions should be established to handle border areas' religion, politics, industry, transportation, education, land, and other work, without having to divide them into Mongolian, Tibetan, Manchu, and Hui divisions, so as to avoid ethnic concepts from becoming increasingly visible. (Special Telegram, 8th)

A Major Fire on Da Tong Street in Xuzhou: About a Hundred Buildings Burned

(Xuzhou) At 5 PM on the 8th, a major fire broke out on Datong Street in Xuzhou, starting from the front building of the Huayuan Hotel in the west and extending to the front building of the National Goods Store in the east. About a hundred buildings on both sides of the road burned. The cause of the fire was the explosion of a gasoline lamp in the Xietongshun Silk Shop in the front building of the Huayuan Hotel. The flying gasoline caused the fire to spread rapidly. The fire brigade and the entire city, as well as the Tianjin-Pukou and Longhai Railway fire brigades, were dispatched together. The cadres of the Seventh Division and the Public Security Bureau police were all dispatched to guard the area. The fire spread from the north side of the road to the south side and was extinguished after burning for four hours. It is estimated that dozens of shops, including Xietongshun Tianzhang Silk Shop, Juqinglong, Dinghua Beijing Goods Store, Yuanzhang Paper Shop, Tonghegong Grocery Store, Jiuzhang Military Clothing Shop, and Meihua Photo Studio, were burned, with losses reaching more than 500,000. Datong Street is the most prosperous area in Xuzhou, especially the eastern section, which is the commercial center. The essence was all destroyed in one fell swoop. The Shanghai National Goods Traveling Troupe Exhibition, which set up shop for promotion in the Huayuan Hotel, was not affected. Wang Jun and She Nianci and others personally went to the fire scene to direct the response. Datong Street was under curfew all night. (Special Telegram, 8th)
