The Zhejiang Construction Department has hired three British and American bridge experts who have arrived in Hangzhou from Europe to oversee the construction project. Work can begin as soon as funding is secured. Furthermore, the bridge foundation will extend from the Jakou to the opposite bank, and the bridge will be 1,600 feet long. He is scheduled to go to Nanjing within a few days to have substantive discussions with the Railway Ministry on the specific arrangements for cooperation between the ministry and the province. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Japanese Military Representative Okamura Arrives in Beiping: Tasked with Resolving War Zone Issues with Huang and He; Agreement Reached on Railway and Postal Service, Establishment of Customs at the Great Wall Passes; Okamura States Results Are Extremely Satisfactory

Beiping Correspondence: Regarding the issues of receiving the Great Wall passes, restoring railway service on the Beining Line, establishing customs for tax collection, and restoring postal service, the Japanese side believes that these are local matters and should be negotiated by the Japanese Kwantung Army with our side. On the Japanese Kwantung Army side, Military Attaché Shibayama of the Japanese Embassy is responsible for liaising. After both sides consulted, it was decided to send a representative to Yuguan to negotiate. Shibayama was then summoned to Changchun by the Japanese Kwantung Army to report on the liaison situation. The views of the two sides are very close, and all principles are largely agreed upon. Shibayama returned to Beiping from the Northeast a few days ago and visited Huang Fu and He Yingqin to report on the views of the Kwantung Army. Huang and He were also understanding. The Kwantung Army then dispatched Deputy Chief of Staff Okamura Yasuji, along with Staff Officer Kita Seiichi, Secretary Hanawa, and Aide Izumi, to Beiping yesterday for formal discussions. They arrived at Nanyuan by plane at 11:25 AM on the morning of the 6th. Huang and He had previously sent military police to guard the Nanyuan airfield. Huang's representative, Yin Tong; He's representative, Zhu Shiqin; Police Chief Yu Jinghe; Japanese Embassy Military Attaché Shibayama; and Secretary Nakayama, along with twenty or so others, were present to welcome them. After disembarking, Okamura and others entered the city by car and stayed at the Fuso Hotel in Dongdan. The original plane flew back to Jinzhou at noon. At 2:30 PM in the afternoon, Okamura, accompanied by Shibayama, visited Huang Fu at the Foreign Affairs Building and then went to Jurentang at 3:30 PM to see He Yingqin. They first exchanged diplomatic pleasantries. Huang Fu hosted a banquet at the Foreign Affairs Building that evening. This morning (the 7th) at 10:00 AM, Okamura, Kita, and Shibayama returned to the Foreign Affairs Building and formally consulted with Huang and He, and formally passed principles on resolving various issues in the war zone. The consultation ended at around 11:00 AM. With the principles established, the details will be discussed at any time. It was decided that our side would receive the Great Wall passes, and the Japanese army would withdraw to the Great Wall line. However, because the Japanese barracks outside the passes have not yet been completed, the small number of Japanese troops temporarily stationed inside the passes will have to stay until next spring. After our side completes the receiving procedures, personnel can be sent to the passes for formal reception. Regarding the issue of restoring railway service on the Beining Line, our side is taking the non-recognition of the puppet state as a prerequisite, and the restoration of traffic is under conditions where it does not leave traces. Detailed methods will be discussed by the authorities of the Beining Railway Bureau and the puppet Fengshan Railway Bureau. Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, and Xia Guangyu, representative of the Ministry of Railways, are currently in Beiping working on it and can be implemented in the near future. Both sides have largely agreed on the establishment of customs and tax collection at the Great Wall passes. Customs checkpoints will be established by both sides to collect transit taxes on goods entering and leaving. After the finance authorities dispatch personnel to conduct thorough investigations and planning, they will be established. Regarding the issue of restoring postal service, it was agreed that the puppet state's stamps cannot enter the customs, and a workaround will be used. Okamura is scheduled to visit Yu Xuezhong in Tianjin on the 10th to exchange views. On the 12th, the Japanese Kwantung Army will still send a plane to Tianjin to take him back to Changchun. Japanese ambassador Arima Setaro traveled to Tianjin by car at 7:00 AM this morning for some communication. He plans to return to Beiping within two or three days. Okamura said this afternoon, "I came here to discuss the issue of receiving the Great Wall passes. I paid respects to Chairman Huang and He yesterday, which was a visit in nature, and nothing was discussed. I formally met with Chairman Huang and He this morning. The results are extremely satisfactory, and there are no more problems. There is no need for further discussion. The Great Wall passes can be received at any time. As soon as China's preparations are complete, personnel can be dispatched. My task can be considered complete. This afternoon, I plan to visit Beihai and the Summer Palace. In the evening, I will attend Chairman He's banquet. I will visit various places of interest again tomorrow and leave for Tianjin on the 10th. After a short stay, I will return to Changchun." (November 7th)

Early Resolution Expected for the Bandit Situation in Luandong; Security Forces Attack Funing County; Li Jichun Telegrams Hebei Provincial Government to Resign

Tianjin Correspondence: Lao Haozi, a notorious bandit in Luandong, has occupied Funing County for more than a month. These bandits are groups of fifteen or so, temporarily gathered, and have no organization to speak of. If formal security forces were to be sent to suppress them, it would not be difficult to eliminate them in one fell swoop. However, the incident arose because there were many bandits, and the security forces stationed in the various counties of Luandong were weak and unable to resist. After agreeing with the Japanese side to send additional security forces to suppress the bandits, the Japanese side repeatedly used excuses to prevent the security forces from bringing heavy artillery into the recovered war zone. The security forces were stranded in Lutai and unable to advance. The situation has been going on for several weeks, so the bandit forces have spread further. By the time the security forces were able to advance into Luandong, the bandits had already occupied Funing County, making it difficult to attack. In addition, there was secret support from some party, making the matter even more difficult. Initially, the provincial government thought that if the bandits were willing to surrender, they would be pacified to avoid bloodshed during the siege, but the bandits remained ambiguous and never complied. Subsequently, Zhang Xiguang, the Commander of the Bandit Suppression, went to Yuguan to discuss with Endo on the Japanese side, who allowed the transport of mortars for the purpose of bombarding the city. Otherwise, with only rifles, the bandits would defend the city and there would be no hope of suppressing them. After the negotiations were completed, Zhang telegraphed the provincial government. The Chairman transferred security forces stationed in Yangcun and Jinghai to transport more than ten mortars and three cavalry units to suppress the bandits for the attack on the city. After arriving, they launched a fierce artillery attack on Funing County in the last two days, resulting in fierce fighting. It was reported that many bandits were killed in the South Gate. Due to the overwhelming force, there were rumors that the bandits would surrender and disarm on the fourth day. However, the bandits still used cunning tricks, taking advantage of the security forces' unpreparedness, and on the morning of the 4th, more than six hundred people emerged from the South Gate again, attempting to break through the security forces' defense line. Fortunately, it had been discovered beforehand, and the bandits' plan failed. Last night and this morning, the fighting at the front is still fierce. According to people who stayed at the rear camp today, there are only about two thousand bandits in Funing City. After this heavy suppression, it is thought that the situation can be resolved in a few days. However, when the security forces attacked the city, the bandits drove innocent civilians to the city walls to resist the artillery fire, forcing the security forces to stop the attack. At the same time, the Japanese side still hoped to pacify the bandits, but our authorities believe that providing money and disarming them is acceptable, but pacifying them is difficult. In short, the bandits in Luandong are seen as disguised troops from a certain party, so it is difficult to quell them. However, according to recent diplomatic trends, it may be resolved in the near future. As for Li Jichun, the Chairman of the Luandong Mixed Troops Reorganization Committee, has telegraphed the Beiping Military Branch and the Hebei Provincial Government, declaring his resignation and requesting the allocation of 115,000 yuan for reorganization expenses and local advances, which the provincial government has agreed to allocate. He will conclude his work in the near future. As for Li personally, although he outwardly claims that he plans to reside in Dalian after his resignation, he is still engaged in activities with the Japanese side and considers himself the overlord of Luandong. Regarding the two security units of Zhao Lei and Liu Zuo, which are affiliated to Li, the provincial government has decided to directly command them when Li resigns, so as to control military power. (5th)

Qufu: Discovery of Han Dynasty Tomb Stone Carvings; Images Strange and Ancient, Characters Large, Measuring a Foot; Important Discovery in Nearly a Century

Jinan Correspondence: Ancient Han Dynasty tombs have recently been discovered in Qufu, southern Shandong. There are many images in the tombs, and the engraved characters are as large as one foot in diameter, which is especially valuable. It is an important discovery in nearly a century. The Provincial Library is currently planning to transport them to Jinan for preservation. According to Wang Xiantang, Director of the Library, the process of discovering the Han tombs and the recently purchased edict plate from the first year of Qin Shi Huang and the Qin Ge are very valuable. It is said that Qufu is the hometown of Confucius, with a long history, so ancient artifacts are discovered every year, which is highly valued by the world. Last month, continuous heavy rains caused the ground beside the road twelve miles east of the city to be flooded, revealing an ancient tomb. The tomb is a combined burial of two tombs, and the inside of the tomb is completely stone-carved images, which are extremely strange and ancient. The two tombs are separated by a stone wall, six or seven feet wide and more than ten feet long. On this stone wall, there are ten large characters engraved: "Mountains of Lu city East Anhan borough, Yu stone also". The characters are written in seal script, seven or eight inches square. The mountain character is drawn in double strokes. Judging from the font, it must be from the late Western Han Dynasty at the latest. According to the recent discovery of Han Dynasty stone carvings in Shandong, those with characters are very few. Occasionally, there are characters, mostly in small clerical script, and the large seal script characters with a diameter of one foot are considered to be the original creation. It is the most valuable among the Han stones discovered in Shandong in nearly a century. However, the meaning of the characters is ancient and obscure, and most of them are incomprehensible. "Mountains of Lu city East Anhan borough" may be the place name of the day, but it is also untraceable. "Yu" is the ancient character for "corner". Translating according to meaning, it may be that the mountain stones in the corner of the borough are the best, and the stonemason specially marked that the stone used was the mountain stone to show its value. However, it is still only a far-fetched interpretation, and further investigation is needed. After the discovery, it was reported to the county government. The county magistrate went to inspect it in person. The tomb was destroyed and nothing was left except for the stone carvings. Collectors took the opportunity to collect them. The county government ordered the land to be leveled and forbade rubbing and printing. The library is currently planning to transport the stones here for preservation to avoid loss. As for the edict plate from the first year of Qin Shi Huang, after Qin annexed the six kingdoms, the system of weights and measures was extremely chaotic, so an edict was issued to unify the system. The edict was made into a copper plate, placed on liters, pecks, and spoons, or cast on weights. This edict plate has the distinction between the first year of the edict and the twenty-sixth year of the edict, written by Li Si. It is said that the twenty-sixth year edition is the most valuable. Chen Fujia, a collector of antiquities in Weixian, Shandong, is famous at home and abroad for Mao Gong Ding, Wan Yin Shi Zhong, etc., most of which were sold by later generations. There are still the so-called ten edicts in the collection, including the edict plate ordered by Qin Shi Huang on Shengshao, which has recently been scattered and lost. Only one edict plate remains, three inches long and two inches wide, with a corner missing in the upper left corner. The characters are "The Prime Minister Si and Qu Ji made the measure and the law was exhausted by the First Emperor in the first year of his reign, and all had engraved words on them. If it is said that today, when the Emperor is to take over the throne and has his engraved title, the First Emperor, who has been ruling for a long time, shall take care of his descendants, so that they should not have cause to speak of success or outstanding virtue. Therefore, the edict is inscribed to the left, so that the mother should not doubt". (The original version is missing a corner, and the text is incomplete, so it is recorded from the ancient books.) This edict plate was unearthed in Chang'an. Liu Yanting's "Changan Obtains Ancient Manuscripts" and Chen Fujia's own "Fujia Jijing Record" both have records. In addition, there is a Jin Ge from the second year of Qin Shi Huang and a Zhou Ge, which are also fine products collected by Chen Fujia and are also valuable. The above-mentioned edict plate and two Ge are all purchased and preserved by the library. The recent calligraphy, painting, bronze and stone exhibition in Jinan was displayed with this for public viewing. (5th)

Yu Family Robbery in Dongmen Results in Losses of Over 20,000 Yuan

At the home of Yu Youqing, a wealthy man outside the East Gate, at around 6:00 PM last night (the 7th), the main gate was already closed when five thugs suddenly arrived, knocked on the gate, and forced a servant to lead them in. They first entered Yu Youqing's bedroom, pointed a gun at Yu Youqing's wife, Ms. Wu, and demanded to know the location of the safe. When told that the safe was kept in Shanghai, they went upstairs and attacked Yu Youqing's mother, Ms. Zhang, in her bedroom. Ms. Zhang knew they were robbers, kneeled and begged for mercy, but the thugs ordered the victims and their male and female servants to be locked in one room, and then wantonly searched, robbing a leather bag containing jewelry and about 700 yuan in cash. They re-entered Yu Youqing's bedroom. At that time, Yu Youqing was already lying in bed. One robber opened the bed curtains and was about to do something to Yu Youqing when another robber said that the person in bed was suffering from a mental illness and should not be disturbed. They also called the maid "Nanny," speaking in what sounded like a Pudong accent, as if they were very familiar with her. They also robbed a spring jewelry box in Yu Youqing's room and left through the main gate. After a while, the family reported the incident to the Fourth Police Station, which relayed it to the Public Security Bureau, which dispatched a large number of detectives to intercept them on various roads, searching all night, but without any trace. This morning, in the bamboo garden in North Yu Tang, villagers passing by spotted an old rattan basket and a small iron box. They later learned that they were the items stolen from the Yu family. The original items were returned. The small iron box was the jewelry box that had been stolen from Yu Youqing's bedroom. The lid of the box had been pried open, and the box could not be opened. It was abandoned on the ground, so the item was returned to its owner. The rattan basket contained a few letters and a set of broken clothes, which are believed to belong to the bandits. The Public Security Bureau has taken them back for investigation and has begun to search the various opium dens, but has found no clues. The Yu family has filed a loss report, estimating the losses at over 20,000 yuan, including three taels and three maces of gold leaf, a pearl-inlaid cornucopia pearl flower and more than 600 large and small pearls, one Xinhe pearl, and many jadeite inlays. It is said that the cornucopia is a family heirloom, and the victim is most grieved by its loss.

County Government Meeting on Rent Collection Quality

This year's rice harvest is slightly better than last year's. No famine reports have been sent to the county. The period for various industries to open their warehouses to collect rent is approaching. The county government checked the existing cases and convened a meeting at the county government on the 8th, attended by representatives from various districts, various industries, various charitable organizations, and the county party headquarters. County Magistrate Jin, the chairman, reported the purpose of the meeting. The representative from the Party Headquarters advocated setting the rent collection quality at 74% due to the decline of the rural economy this year. However, the various industry representatives argued that there were reports of famine last year, and the provincial committee surveyed and reduced it by 10%. There were no reports of famine this year, so some insisted on setting it at 79%. After a vote, the rent collection quality for this year was unanimously passed at 77%.

Suzhou

Robbery and Serious Case in Song Xian Zhou Alley

On the 7th, around 2 AM, four robbers broke into No. 10 Song Xian Zhou Alley inside Changmen. They first tied up the seven men and women in the house and then proceeded to search and loot until 5 AM when they fled with their stolen goods. The loss is estimated to be over a thousand yuan. Three suspects in the case have been detained by the authorities and are under investigation. The details are as follows: The house is inhabited by three families. One is Hu Zixian, who currently runs the Baofeng Fur Shop in front of the Tianku (he has a wife, Cao, and a son). Another is the family of Yao, who is deceased, leaving behind his wife, Chen, and a three-year-old daughter. The third is Tang, formerly an employee of the Shanghai Wuhua Bank, now unemployed. His father is currently the manager of the Xiangda Foreign Goods Store in the West Central Market. Tang lives with his concubine, Zhu, with whom he has a daughter. Excluding the children, there are a total of five men and women living in the house. Recently, Zhu's uncle, Zhu Xiangsheng, came to Suzhou from Shanghai and is staying in Tang's house. On the 6th, Hu Zixian stayed at the store. After nightfall, his wife and Yao Chen's family went to sleep early. At that time, Tang suddenly announced that he would take an early train to Shanghai to seek employment. He and his concubine整理箱件etc. prepared luggage, staying up all night. At 12 o'clock midnight, a rickshaw puller, Zhang Riyan, pulled his rickshaw to the door to wait. Tang thought it was still early and specifically opened the door to let him pull the rickshaw in and park it in the garden, then closed the front door. Around 2 AM on the 7th, there was a sudden, urgent knocking on the door. Without asking questions, Tang immediately went out and opened the door. As soon as he opened the door, four burly men wearing short blue cloth shirts and trousers, wearing felt hats, and speaking with a Jiangbei accent, rushed in, each holding a flashlight and hemp rope. One person stood at the door as a lookout. The other three robbers entered and first silenced the people in the house, then fired a shot in the living room with a gun-like object. They then tied the rickshaw puller to a tree. At the same time, they tied up the six men and women from the Hu, Yao, and Tang families in their respective rooms. Then, the three robbers turned over and searched the boxes and luggage in the three families' rooms one by one, taking all the valuables. It was not until 5:30 AM that they packed up and fled with the stolen goods. After the robbers left, Tang untied himself and then helped untie the others one by one. Hu's wife immediately went to the Baofeng Shop in front of the Tianku to report to her husband. Upon hearing the news, Hu Zixian immediately returned home to check the stolen items. He was about to report to the police station when Tang suddenly stopped him, saying that if he reported it, something serious might happen to his life. However, Hu eventually reported it. The detective team immediately sent detectives Wu Rongshan and Zhang Yunquan to investigate in detail. According to Hu Cao's and Yao Chen's statements, Tang knew the robbers because they had heard Tang call out the robbers' names: A'er, Jinbao, Xiaomazi, Zhuangjin, and so on. They also said that Tang himself did not return until 1 AM on the 6th and brought a rickshaw puller to stay at home, so the double doors were not closed properly. Also, during the robbery, one of the robbers said to Hu Cao, "You have 300 yuan in cash and two gold rings. You exchanged them yesterday. Where is the money hidden? Otherwise, we will kidnap your son and you will have to redeem him for 500 yuan." Detective Wu, based on Yao Chen's statements, believed that Tang, the rickshaw puller Zhang Riyan, and the related person Zhu Xiangsheng were highly suspicious. They were immediately detained. Tang and the other two were sent to the General Bureau yesterday (the 8th) for interrogation.

The county government's case to promote the new system of weights and measures has repeatedly issued orders to various industries, setting a deadline for conversion. However, the rice, bean, and grain industries are fundamentally different in nature from other industries. Not only are the procedures troublesome, but there are also many obstacles, making it difficult to implement. The important reasons are related to loans for mortgages from banks, money houses, and堆棧, as well as various fees for storage rent, train freight, boat fares, and barge縫包. Although various items can be converted, the rice industry is difficult to resolve. The county government specifically invited representatives from relevant industries to hold a meeting yesterday, chaired by Zhang Fulin. The representative of the儲棧industry, Cai Jian San, was unable to attend due to matters. The rent and usage fees of the棧厫of the industry were previously calculated using Cao斛and漕秤. The ratio of the new measuring instrument to the old斛is 93.3%, and the ratio of the new衡器to the old秤is 85.5%. If this is not resolved, the rice industry will suffer a significant loss in expenses. The discussion resulted in that after the implementation of the rice, bean, and grain industries, the other industries will not have any problems. County Magistrate Yan Shenyu plans to contact the 儲棧industry at a certain time to unify it as soon as possible.

Dismissed Policeman Arrested for Forging Official Seals

Li Xiangtao from Huai'an, about twenty years old, used to work as a policeman in various public security sub-bureaus in this county. Due to his corrupt behavior, he was dismissed. After losing his job, Li lived in Meng Zhaoxiang's house at No. 175 Nancangmen. Also, Meng used to work as a policeman in the Second Sub-bureau with Li, so they were acquainted. Recently, Zhou Erkai, the Chief Prosecutor of the County Court, discovered that Li was forging court seals outside to defraud and extort. Therefore, at around 7 AM yesterday, he dispatched two prosecutors, Shen and Ren, leading通班法警, to search in separate directions. Prosecutor Ren led the police to search the home of Zhang Jinpei, a small vendor in Ping'anli, Dongxin Road, but found nothing. Prosecutor Shen led the police to search Meng Zhaoxiang's house in Nancangmen for over two hours but also found no evidence. Shen then ordered the police to take Meng Zhaoxiang to the court. At the same time, Prosecutor Ren had also ordered the police to take Zhang Jinpei and Zhang Ding to the court. After the joint trial by Prosecutor Shen, the result was to order Zhang Jinpei to be dismissed, Zhang Ding and Meng Zhaoxiang released on bail temporarily, and immediately find Li Xiangtao to bring him to justice. Hangzhou

Two Suicides Due to Economic Oppression

Lu Asi, a peddler from Shaoxing, aged fifty-eight, at No. 5 Yunxi Alley, Shangtianzhu, West Lake, relies on the income from the spring incense season every year to make a living. This year, due to the weak spring incense, his income was short, and his livelihood was difficult. Recently, his pawns have been exhausted, and debts have piled up, unable to repay them. Yesterday (the 6th), he suddenly had a pessimistic thought and hanged himself in his closed house around 6 PM. His wife discovered it, but it was too late to save him. She reported it to the police station, which forwarded it to the court for inspection and coffin burial. Also, Liu Zhang, the proprietress of the Gonghe Village Hotel on Wushan Road, Hangzhou, has been suffering from poor business and heavy losses. It was difficult to pay the bills to various suppliers. Yesterday afternoon at 6 PM, she secretly went to Hongfu Bridge and jumped into the water to commit suicide. Fortunately, she was rescued by the patrolling police, detained at the police station, and interrogated to ascertain the reason. She was ordered to be released home.

Chairman Lu Visits Shaoxing for Inspection

The Chairman of Zhejiang Province, Lu Dipin, departed from Shanghai a few days ago and went to Ningbo to inspect Zhenhai, Cixi, Yuyao, and other places. He came to Shaoxing on the 7th. In the afternoon, he crossed the Baiguan River. County Magistrate Tang went to greet him and took a special train on the Cao-Shao Road, passing through Donghu. Because the place is a famous scenic spot in Yuezhong, the train stopped for a week's tour. It did not arrive in Shaoxing until about 3 PM. He got off at Wuyun Station. Those who came with him were Lu's adjutant and two attendants. County Magistrate Tang led Chairman Lu and others to take the prepared畫舫 to Yuling to visit famous scenic spots and historical sites and pay respects to the sage. Around 7 PM, they returned to Wuyun Station, took a car, and went from Beihai Bridge to Shangda Road Street, and then to the County Government. After a short rest, he inquired about the county's security and financial situation from the head of public security, Lai, and the head of finance, Zhang. Then, he took a chartered car to Shaoxing Station. At about 8 PM that night, the special train left for Xiao to return to the province.

Local News

Chief Commissioner of Customs, Fetes Former Minister of Finance Song, Presents Silver Tripod, Gives Important Speech

Chief Commissioner of Customs, Mr. Meyrick, hosted a banquet for former Minister of Finance Song Ziwen at his residence on Avenue Joffre yesterday, inviting dignitaries from the business and gentry circles to accompany him. During the banquet, Meyrick delivered a speech and, on behalf of the Customs colleagues, presented a silver tripod as a memento. Li Ming, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, and others then delivered speeches in succession. Finally, Mr. Song replied. The guests and hosts were delighted and the event ended. The various speeches are summarized below.

Speech by Customs Commissioner Meyrick

Dr. Song, distinguished guests, Dr. Song has served as Minister of Finance for six years. Now, he is retreating bravely and resolutely resigning. All of us in the Customs have been under his care for a long time. We cannot remain indifferent to his departure. However, in terms of Dr. Song's contributions to the country, we cannot help but admire him. In terms of Dr. Song's measures for the Customs, we are even more grateful. Recalling Dr. Song's tenure, he served during a time of global economic panic and depletion of domestic financial resources, coupled with the arrival of internal and external troubles. The difficulty of the environment can be imagined. Relying on Dr. Song's ability to shoulder the heavy burden, he rectified the national economy on one hand and focused on people's livelihood on the other. All his measures are comparable to those of financial experts around the world. It is fitting that his envoys were praised throughout Europe and the United States. Future historians will record his name for posterity. The Customs is an agency directly under the Ministry of Finance, and Dr. Song's policy towards the Customs is especially respected and remembered by all of us in the Customs. Now, I will list the most important ones as follows: Customs revenue is related to the credibility of various debts and reparations, and whether the credibility is solid depends on whether there are any changes in the current organization of the Customs. Dr. Song insightfully recognized this and followed the principle of retaining the old traditions to promote the progress of Customs administration. Therefore, the country's domestic and foreign credibility has become increasingly solid, and the belief of Chinese and foreign merchants in the Customs has become increasingly deep. Without Dr. Song's farsightedness, how could this have been achieved? This is one point. China has been plagued by internal wars and local unrest for several years. Customs administration has often been affected, even undermining the unity of Customs administration. Relying on Dr. Song's adaptation to the situation, he was able to support the precarious situation and achieve initial success. For example, the implementation of customs autonomy and the revision of the Customs tariff have opened a new era for Chinese Customs. In terms of tax revenue, the tax revenue in the 17th year of the Republic was only 128,270,000 yuan, and now it has increased to more than 348,480,000 yuan. In this eventful period for the country, not only was it able to recover the sovereignty of customs duties, but it was also able to increase the revenue of the national treasury. The greatness of its achievements is unparalleled. This is the second point. The treatment of Chinese Customs officers has always been inferior to that of foreign officers. This situation is not only unfair but also has an impact on work efficiency. In the 18th year, Dr. Song supervised former Director Zhang and Lehe to improve the treatment of Chinese officers and improve their status. As a result, the number of Chinese officers who hold important positions has gradually increased, and Chinese and foreign personnel have a spirit of harmony and cooperation, which has resulted in a synergy that is of great benefit to Customs administration. This is the third point. Previously, the Chinese government was somewhat separated from Customs administration. Since Dr. Song took office, he has thoroughly reformed it. Therefore, since then, all Customs administration has been handled in accordance with the deployments and orders, which is no different from other Chinese agencies. China's sovereignty over Customs has been completely restored. This is the fourth point. Since the increase in customs duties, smuggling has become increasingly rampant. The anti-smuggling task has become the most important task of the Customs. However, the Chinese coast has Dalian in the north, Taiwan in the east, and Hong Kong, Macau, and Guangzhou Bay in the south, all of which are sources of smuggled goods. The Customs is facing extreme difficulties in handling anti-smuggling affairs. Relying on Dr. Song's insight into this situation, all facilities and funds for anti-smuggling were readily approved whenever Lehe made a request. As a result, the organization of various anti-smuggling departments has gradually expanded internally, and various maritime巡輪have been added externally. Therefore, the current anti-smuggling equipment has gradually become complete, and the effectiveness has been significant. This is all due to Dr. Song's effective supervision. This is the fifth point. Looking at Dr. Song's past achievements, it can be said that he has made great contributions to the country and benefited the people. Now, he has retired successfully, which is deeply regretted by both the government and the public. Fortunately, I heard that Dr. Song has agreed to continue to serve as a member of the Standing Committee of the National Economic Council. He will apply his experience and knowledge in finance to controlled economics, and the benefits he will bring to the people are immeasurable. The joy is beyond words. Fortunately, Dr. Kong has succeeded as Minister. All of us in the Customs welcome him. I hope he will use his great strategy to save the world and express his grand plan to enrich the country. The future of the Party and the country will depend on him. As for the Customs, if he can understand the actual situation, maintain the current organization, attach importance to national credit, and benefit Customs administration, then we will be fortunate. Now, on behalf of all the Customs personnel, I am pleased to present Dr. Song with a silver tripod as a memorial and to express my admiration. I wish Dr. Song and Dr. Kong good health.

Li Ming's Speech

Today, the Chief Commissioner of Customs and the Customs colleagues are presenting a souvenir to Minister Song in honor of his departure from the ministry, and inviting us to participate and gather together. I am very happy. At this critical juncture in the overall national situation, Minister Song suddenly left his post. It is certainly wise for Minister Song to rest temporarily after years of hard work, but the people cannot help but regret it. I would like to represent the Banking Association and the Foundation Committee to say a few words about my feelings. Minister Song has been in charge of finance for several years, and his achievements are great and brilliant, and they are obvious to all. Commissioner Meyrick has already said enough to represent general public opinion. However, in my opinion, Minister Song's achievements during his tenure are particularly great in three respects, and they occupy an extremely important position in the history of Chinese finance, so I must mention them. First, the abolition of Likin. Likin has been a major scourge for hundreds of years. The motion to abolish it has been around for decades, but it has never been done. Minister Song accomplished it with one hand, overcoming all difficulties with his perseverance, eliminating the ills of the finance of a hundred years and relieving the merchants and people from immeasurable suffering. Second, customs autonomy. This matter has been brewing for several years and is related to diplomacy, similar to pending cases. Minister Song also spent a lot of effort to solve the first step of customs autonomy. From then on, national tax revenue was increased, which had a major impact on industry and commerce. Third, the abolition of taels and the reform of yuan. The currency of our country has always been inconvenient in all aspects because both silver taels and silver yuan are in circulation at the same time. The proposal to abolish taels has also been around for decades, but it has never been achieved. This year, after careful deliberation by Minister Song, he resolutely abolished taels and reformed the yuan, and the currency has a unified foundation, benefiting industry and commerce immeasurably. The above three are the most prominent and significant aspects of Minister Song's achievements during his tenure. In addition, there are other important matters. Minister Song has made every effort to maintain national credit and has taken into account both domestic and foreign debts for many years, which is seen by both Chinese and foreigners. However, the source of maintaining credit relies entirely on customs tax revenue, and this cannot but be attributed to Chief Commissioner Meyrick's conscientious performance of his duties and effective guidance. We believe that although Minister Song has now left his ministry, Chief Commissioner Meyrick is still in charge of taxation. We sincerely hope that the Customs tax revenue will continue to improve in the future, maintain a perfect system, and provide sufficient tax revenue to make the credit increasingly stable. The new Minister Kong has always been of the same mind as Minister Song and has known us well. At this time, he will certainly continue to take raising national credit as a prerequisite, and Chief Commissioner Meyrick will also be able to continue to guide him, complementing each other.

Former Minister Song's Reply

Today, I am honored to receive a souvenir from the Customs officers and to receive so much praise from Chief Commissioner Meyrick. I am really ashamed and grateful. Recalling that during my tenure as Minister of Finance, the Customs has achieved a lot. Customs tax revenue has increased three times from before after customs autonomy. The service personnel are all able to be faithful to the public and do not tarnish their past reputation. The Customs administration has also been able to maintain its inherent integrity. I am very fortunate for this. Now that I have left the Ministry of Finance, there are some misunderstandings about the status of the Customs in the outside world. At this time, I will briefly discuss it with you. After the Northern Expedition was completed, the National Government established its capital in Nanjing. At that time, there were many criticisms of the Customs from both the government and the public. Some said that the Chinese Customs was like a government within a government, no less than an appendage of the foreign powers' embassies in China. Some even said that the words of the Chief Commissioner of Customs were as effective as the laws of the Ministry of Finance, and that the fate of the Finance Minister of the Beijing government was in the hands of the Chief Commissioner of Customs, and that the Customs revenue was entirely deposited in foreign banks, which made their power in China increasingly strong, and Chinese banks were left out in the cold, and that the appointment of senior Customs officials was limited to foreign Customs officers. At that time, there was a unanimous call from the government and the public to thoroughly improve the organization of the Customs. However, at that time, according to my observation, the involvement of the Customs in the political vortex had nothing to do with its own organization. The internal organization of the Customs was very sound. The points of criticism from the outside world could be corrected without shaking its organization. I am very fortunate that the above observations have been proven by facts to be correct. Today, the position of the Chief Commissioner of Customs is already a loyal servant of the government, completely obedient to the Minister of Finance. The raising of national funds is entirely the responsibility of the Minister of Finance and has nothing to do with the Commissioner of Customs. The storage of tax revenues is now entirely concentrated in national banks. The promotion and transfer of Customs officers is now entirely based on service performance and has nothing to do with nationality. Foreign Customs officers, except for a few specialized technical personnel, are no longer recruited. And the treatment of all current foreign Customs officers is still based on fairness. Customs personnel, from Mr. Meyrick down, have all made efforts to implement the above improvements. You should feel that the people's faith and goodwill towards the Customs and Commerce have been improving with the times, and the purpose of the Customs is to become a non-partisan Chinese agency. The service rules for Customs public officials are very good in my opinion, and I want all the departments of the Ministry of Finance to follow suit. During my tenure as Minister of Finance, I often encouraged the members of the Ministry to be loyal to the government, not just to one person or group. Otherwise, the change of the Minister would affect the Ministry's affairs. Therefore, when I retired this time, I encouraged all the subordinates, except for the secretaries and attendants, to continue to work as usual, unless the new Minister had other candidates. This is because public officials take loyalty to the government as a prerequisite. In my opinion, we should not affect the overall situation with the progress or retreat of individuals. Fortunately, my retirement this time did not cause any disorder in finance. Otherwise, I would not have fulfilled my duty to the government. I have served as Minister of Finance for a short time and have made few contributions. However, I have always encouraged myself and my colleagues with the words "be loyal to the government and be loyal to what you do." Customs officers can be regarded as examples. Therefore, the progress of Customs can only improve with the times. This is all I want to say. I thank you for the gifts and the spirit of cooperation that has always been there. You will certainly continue to maintain this spirit towards the new Minister. I have great expectations.

The Chinese Merchants' Yarn and Cloth Exchange Resumes Cotton Yarn Auctions Today; Zou Bingwen and Others Return to Shanghai Yesterday After Petitioning in Beijing; Rejection of New Yarn to Be Remedied with Alternative Measures; Exchange and Brokers Held Meetings Yesterday to Report Progress

According to the New Voice News Agency, following the Ministry of Industry's order to the Chinese Merchants' Yarn and Cloth Exchange to reject new yarn from manufacturers from November to the end of December of this year, due to opposition from brokers who requested the revocation of the order, cotton yarn auctions were temporarily suspended for three days starting on the 6th of this month. Zou Bingwen, a standing committee member of the Cotton Industry Control Committee, and Mu Jiechu, chairman of the Exchange's board of directors, traveled to Beijing to negotiate, and returned to Shanghai yesterday. A decision was made on alternative measures, and it was decided that auctions would resume as usual today. The Cotton Yarn Exchange held a board meeting yesterday, and the brokers held a general meeting to report on the progress. The details are as follows:

Zou Bingwen and Others Return to Shanghai

After the brokers petitioned for the revocation of the order to reject new yarn from manufacturers, Zou Bingwen, a standing committee member of the National Economic Committee's Cotton Industry Control Committee, and Mu Jiechu, chairman of the Chinese Merchants' Yarn and Cloth Exchange, traveled to Beijing on the 6th to negotiate with Chen Gongbo, the Minister of Industry. They returned to Shanghai from Beijing the night before last. Yesterday morning, Mu Jiechu, Zou Bingwen, and others convened a meeting at the Cotton Industry Control Committee, deciding to comply with the Ministry of Industry's order and to remedy the brokers' request for revocation with alternative measures.

Exchange Board Meeting

The Chinese Merchants' Yarn and Cloth Exchange held a special board meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included Mu Jiechu, Ye Zhuotang, Li Fuxun, Lin Kanghou, Gu Zipan, Wu Zhongchi, and others. Chairman Mu Jiechu reported on the progress of Zou Bingwen and others' negotiation with Chen Gongbo, the Minister of Industry. A decision was made on alternative measures for rejecting new yarn delivered by manufacturers from November to the end of December. It was resolved that cotton yarn auctions would resume on November 9th. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. After the meeting, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency interviewed Mu Jiechu, who stated that a decision had been made to resume cotton yarn auctions as usual starting on the 9th. Alternative measures for rejecting new yarn had been decided, and there were no major issues. However, the details of the measures would be announced after the auctions resumed.

Brokers Hold General Meeting

The Chinese Merchants' Yarn and Cloth Exchange Brokers' Association held a general meeting at 5:00 PM yesterday. Fifty-three brokers attended, chaired by Zhu Guangcheng, who reported on the alternative measures for rejecting new yarn from manufacturers from November to the end of December. A resolution was unanimously passed, and the meeting adjourned at 5:30 PM. After the meeting, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency interviewed Zhu Guangcheng, who stated that the brokers' request for revocation was due to practical difficulties. As for the so-called alternative measures, they were to remedy these difficulties. Now that the difficulties have been remedied, there are no problems.

Notice of Resumption of Auctions

The Yarn and Cloth Exchange issued two notices at 6:00 PM yesterday, which are transcribed below: (1) Cotton yarn auctions will resume as usual starting on the morning of the 9th of this month. This is announced in addition to notifying the Brokers' Association. (2) For both buyers and sellers of cotton yarn for November and December of this year, a special margin of 22 yuan in cash will be added per bale, starting on the morning of the 9th of this month. This is announced in addition to notifying the Brokers' Association.

Details of Alternative Measures

The Cotton Industry Control Committee petitioned the Ministry of Industry to order the Chinese Merchants' Yarn and Cloth Exchange to reject new yarn delivered by manufacturers from November to the end of December in order to fundamentally remedy the sharp decline in the price of Chinese yarn. The brokers' request for revocation was because customers had already entered into contracts for new yarn that had been traded, and failure to fulfill these contracts would inevitably cause difficulties. As for the decided alternative measures, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency learned from various sources that since the Ministry of Industry's order had been issued, revocation would affect the government's credibility. However, the brokers' practical difficulties were real. Therefore, it was decided that when cotton yarn auctions resume from November to the end of December, the Cotton Industry Control Committee will exchange the new yarn rejected by the Exchange in accordance with the Ministry of Industry's order with existing yarn.

Purchasing Yarn for Sale in Other Ports

There have been many rumors about the Cotton Industry Control Committee's petition to the Ministry of Industry to restrict the business of the Yarn and Cloth Exchange, and some have accused the Committee of engaging in speculation because the Committee recently purchased 24,000 bales of cotton yarn from the market in order to raise yarn prices. However, Chen Guangfu, the chairman of the Cotton Industry Control Committee, told a reporter from the China Eastern News Agency yesterday that the rumors circulating outside were not worth the attention of those in the know. The Cotton Industry Control Committee's purchase of the cotton yarn was purely to raise yarn prices. Although it will still need to be sold to other places in the future, it will definitely not be sold in this city. The Committee will determine the needs of various places in other provinces and sell it there, so as not to affect the market price of cotton yarn, he said.

Newly Appointed French Ambassador to Japan Arrives in Shanghai; Supported by French Embassy in China

Havas Agency, Shanghai, 8th: The newly appointed French Ambassador to Japan, Mr. Billard, arrived in Shanghai today aboard the postal ship Aramis and will proceed to Tokyo to assume his post the day after tomorrow. This is because the former French Ambassador to Japan, Mr. Martel, has been transferred to be the High Commissioner in Syria. In addition, Mr. Hopenot, the counselor of the French Embassy in China, also arrived in Shanghai on the same ship and will go to Beiping soon to succeed Mr. Lagarde as the counselor of the French Embassy. The French Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Meyrier, and his wife will host a banquet tonight to welcome the two gentlemen.

Mr. Hope Pierre Billard

Born on March 29, 1874, he graduated from the School of Law and obtained a Bachelor of Arts and a Bachelor of Laws degree. He entered the diplomatic service in 1898. On April 7, 1900, he served as Acting Consul in Beijing. On April 5, 1902, he served as Acting Consul in Shanghai. On August 30, 1902, he served as Vice-Consul in Zhifu. On February 1, 1908, he served as Consul in Fuzhou. On January 11, 1909, he served as Commercial Counselor in the East. On February 26, 1916, he served as Consul General. On May 5, 1920, he served as Minister Plenipotentiary in Prague. On October 1, 1925, he served as Special Envoy to Siam to sign the Franco-Siamese Commercial Treaty. On June 1, 1926, he served as Director of the French Foreign Art Office. On July 23, 1930, he was awarded the Grand Cross of the Legion of Honour. In 1933, he was appointed French Minister to Tokyo.

Mr. Henri Ernest Hopenot

Born on October 25, 1891, he graduated from the School of Law. He entered the diplomatic service in 1914. On January 16, 1917, he served as Counselor at the Embassy in Bern. In 1919, he served as Minister in Rio de Janeiro. On October 25, 1920, he served as Chief of Special Affairs in Taranto. On July 31, 1925, he served as Secretary in Berlin. On July 29, 1927, he served at the Office of the High Commissioner in Syria. On August 13, 1927, he was awarded membership in the Legion of Honour. On July 16, 1931, he served as Counselor at the Embassy in Bern. In 1933, he served as Counselor at the Embassy in Beiping and will act as French Minister during Mr. Wilder's leave.

Combined Land and Sea Transport on the Longhai Railway to Officially Commence Operations on the 15th; First Voyage to Lao Yao Set for the 19th; More Daily Sailings on the Qinghai Section

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's combined land and sea transport on the Longhai Railway is scheduled to commence on the 15th of this month, and the first vessel to depart from Shanghai to Lao Yao is scheduled to set sail on the 19th of this month. Zhou Songnian, the section chief specially dispatched to Shanghai by the Railway Bureau, signed the contract with the Kang Zhenji Barge Company yesterday and left Shanghai for Zhengzhou that evening. All the procedures have been completed. The details are as follows:

Railway Bureau Representatives Arrive in Shanghai

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has specially established a dedicated section to handle the combined land and sea transport on the Longhai Railway. The Railway Bureau has also appointed eight representatives to come to Shanghai to cooperate in the operation, and has appointed Chen Shouchi as the resident director in Shanghai. Mr. Chen has already arrived in Shanghai and joined the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's combined transport section to handle matters. The remaining eight representatives are scheduled to arrive at the Bureau on the 15th of this month. Chen Shouchi and Zhou Fengtu are currently discussing and assigning the responsibilities of each person.

Tonghua to Sail First Voyage

Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and Zhou Songnian of the Railway Bureau agreed that the first vessel from Shanghai to Lao Yao, Haizhou, will be the Tonghua, scheduled to depart from Shanghai on the 19th of this month to begin transporting Northwest combined transport cargo. On the 21st, it will return to Shanghai fully loaded with goods from the railway. This vessel will be the first Shanghai merchant ship to sail to Lianyungang. If there is more cargo in the future, additional sailings will be added.

Products from Various Ports Along the Longhai Railway

The Longhai Railway runs through four provinces, and the output along the route is large. Once combined transport is implemented, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's business on this route will increase tenfold compared to before. According to the results of a survey conducted by the Railway Bureau, the goods produced on all the main and branch lines of the railway include: 500 train cars and 139,000 tons of wheat, 360,000 bags of flour, 36,000 tons of sorghum, 35,000 tons of beans, over 80,000 tons of raw peanuts, 1,000 tons of raw oil, over 5,000 tons of fruit, 4,530 tons of melon seeds, 2,000 tons of yellow vegetables, 18,000 tons of miscellaneous grains, 110,000 tons of salt, over 300 tons of eggs, 50,000 bales and 25,000 tons of cotton and yarn, 3,000 tons of timber, 200,000 tons of coal, 100,000 tons of limestone, 3,000 tons of medicinal materials, 3,000 tons of bean cake, 2,000 tons of wine, 200 tons of cattle and sheep hides, and over 20,000 tons of miscellaneous goods, totaling 787,030 tons, 50,000 bales, and 500 train cars.

Qinghai Still Has Daily Sailings

There is also a lot of freight traffic between Haizhou and Qingdao, and the coastal ports along the route include Gongkou, Taokou, Lankou, Zhewang, Qingkou, and Xiangshuikou. Currently, the companies operating on this route include Changji, Yingshuo, Yutai, Fuluo, and Nakamuragumi, with a total of over twenty vessels. Among them, the Japanese company Nakamuragumi has the largest business, with over ten vessels, and has been excessively lowering freight rates in an attempt to monopolize the market. After the combined transport between the Longhai and Jiaoji Railways, the shipping line on this Qinghai section should also be operated by state-owned vessels. However, there is still resistance, so the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is still in the process of handling this matter.

Current Locations of Noteworthy People

Liu Chongjie, the ambassador to Germany, left Beijing on the night express train last night and is expected to arrive in Shanghai this morning. He will stay for a few days before departing overseas.

Zou Lin, the Vice Minister of Finance, went to Beijing on the night train last night.

Mr. Dong Kang, a legal scholar, was invited by Waseda University, Meiji University, and the Chinese Legal System Research Association of the Japanese Empire to go to Tokyo to lecture on ancient Chinese legal systems. A reporter from the Central News Agency went to Mr. Dong's residence on Seymour Road yesterday morning to inquire. At that time, Mr. Dong and his secretaries, Sun Yizhai and Yang Wuyi, were getting into a car to go to Yangshupu to board the Shanghai Maru. Ya Qingqi, the Duke of the Right Wing of Qinghai, Arrived in Shanghai from Beijing Yesterday; To Visit Various Schools and Industrial and Commercial Conditions; Prepared to Return to Qinghai to Construct Various New Enterprises

Ya Qingqi, the Duke of the Right Wing of Qinghai and the head of the Torsak banner, recently went to Beijing from Qinghai to pay respects to important figures in the central government and report on the latest political and social conditions in Qing Province. Mr. Ya is a leader of the youth faction in Qinghai and has long aspired to develop the Northwest. He came to Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday to visit the various schools and industrial and commercial conditions in the city. A reporter from the People's Words News Agency met with Mr. Ya at his residence yesterday. According to him, Qinghai has a vast territory and is extremely rich in mineral and forest resources, making it the only treasure in the Northwest of China. However, due to traffic congestion, the situation in the interior is very isolated. The progress of education and industry and commerce in the advanced provinces and cities cannot be transmitted to Qing Province. Recently, the Qinghai Travel Group, undeterred by hardships, traveled from Shanghai to Qinghai. The situation in our province will undoubtedly gain a deeper understanding from the Chinese people. However, because travel is too difficult, it is not easy for people from other provinces to leave their hometowns and travel to remote areas for a while. Therefore, I have come to Beijing and Shanghai to investigate and strive to return to Qinghai as soon as possible to apply the details obtained from the investigation of education and industry and commerce, taking into account local conditions, and strive to build enterprises. At the same time, I hope that talents from all over the country will not abandon our province and will provide instructions at any time. This is not only my good fortune, but also the good fortune of the country.

The Flagship of the United States Asiatic Fleet, the USS Augusta, Will Arrive in Shanghai

The Shanghai Evening Post reports that the USS Augusta, the newly dispatched flagship of the United States Asiatic Fleet, is coming from the west coast of the United States and was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on Friday. It is now believed that it will arrive earlier. Rear Admiral Hepburn, the Commander-in-Chief of the United States Asiatic Fleet, will move aboard the ship after its arrival and is scheduled to depart from Shanghai with United States Minister Johnson on the 18th of this month to visit various ports in South China. Then, the American Minister will return north from Hong Kong, and Admiral Hepburn will return south to the Philippines. The flagship yacht USS Isabel will also return to the Philippines. The USS Augusta, although similar to the original flagship USS Houston as a 10,000-ton cruiser, is newly built and has the latest designs. Therefore, it is being dispatched to replace the USS Houston to strengthen the fleet. The USS Houston is expected to leave Shanghai around the 17th of this month to return to the United States.

Anti-Banditry Movement; Day Three of Propaganda Week; Over Four Hundred Representatives from Eighty-Plus Groups Attended

Yesterday was the third day of the Anti-Banditry Movement Week, the "Workers and Peasants' Anti-Banditry Propaganda Day." In addition to the police officers dispatched by the Public Security Bureau for protection, there were also twelve Boy Scouts from the Shanghai-Ningbo Steamboat Cabin Attendants' Union to maintain order. The details are as follows:

General Assembly Order

(1) Ringing the bell to start the meeting; (2) Singing the Party song; (3) Paying the highest respect to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the President; (4) The Chairman reading the President's will; (5) Silence; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Speeches; (8) Shouting slogans; (9) Performances; (10) Adjournment.

Chairman's Report

After the rituals were completed, Zhu Xuefan gave a report, followed by a speech by Zhou Funong, a representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, and then a speech by Lu Jingshi. The speeches are omitted.

Artistic Performances

In order to thoroughly educate all sectors of society on the significance of anti-banditry and to increase interest, the General Labor Union specially invited the Postal Workers' Union to perform silk and bamboo music, martial arts, and magic, and requested the Juvenile Propaganda Group to perform a costumed performance. The audience was very moved by the various performances.

Chamber of Commerce Propaganda

Today is the "Business Community Anti-Banditry Propaganda Day." The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce is scheduled to convene a Business Community Anti-Banditry Propaganda Movement at 2:00 PM in the meeting hall of the Tianhougong Bridge. It has been decided that Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, and Lu Wenshao will serve as the presidium.

The Business Community Solicits Donations for Disaster Relief in Pudong

Yesterday afternoon, Wang Xiaolai, the chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and committee members Du Yuesheng, Wang Yansong, and Lu Wenshao jointly invited the leaders of various trade associations to a tea party in the standing committee room of the Chamber of Commerce to discuss providing relief to the victims of the disaster in Pudong. Over a hundred representatives from ninety trade associations, including banks, money shops, new medicines, and silk, attended. Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, and others successively reported on the disaster situation in Pudong and the urgent need for relief. Everyone agreed that since other provinces have suffered disasters, Shanghai should collect a large sum of money and send it to Pudong, which is nearby. Seeing the impoverished people with their own eyes, they should do their best to help. It was decided that donation books would be distributed on the spot, and the representatives present would be asked to solicit donations from their respective trades and forward the collected funds immediately.

The Economic Hardship of the Rural Areas in Pudong

Pudong is located east of the Huangpu River, separated from Shanghai by only a river. It consists of the three counties of Fengxian, Nanhui, and Chuansha. Most of the residents live by farming. Every autumn, when the harvest matures, they sell rice and cotton to earn a living. In recent years, low grain prices have hurt farmers, and people have already felt the pain. Unexpectedly, this autumn, after suffering two typhoons, the crops were greatly damaged. In addition, continuous rain has washed away a lot of the cotton bolls. The harvest is less than one dan per mu. In previous years, each dan was worth twelve yuan, but this year it is less than ten yuan, and still no one cares. Farmers cannot sell their crops and look worried. It is hoped that the yarn mills in Shanghai will pay attention to this and make every effort to purchase the crops, so that the farmers' economy can be turned around, which will strengthen their purchasing power, and yarn and cloth will naturally be able to sell. If they are abandoned and only foreign cotton is valued, money will flow into the hands of foreigners and will never return. It is hoped that those who care about the rural areas will pay attention to this.

The Central Mint Resumed Operation Yesterday

The Central Mint in Zigong had previously lost its effectiveness due to the accumulation of sand, which led to the interruption of the water source in the factory, and it was forced to temporarily suspend work for about a week. It is now learned that the factory has hired workers to excavate the sand for days and completed the work the day before yesterday. It resumed operation as usual yesterday.

The Ministry of Industry Has Consulted the Ministry of Finance on the Tariff on Dumping of Foreign Rice

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously stated that the import of foreign rice has led to a decline in domestic rice prices, which has further deteriorated the rural economy. It requested the Ministries of Finance and Industry to implement tariffs on imported foreign rice as soon as possible in order to maintain the foundation of the country. It is now learned that the Ministry of Industry has replied yesterday. The original reply is as follows: "The telegram from the Eastern Representative has been read. We have consulted the Ministry of Finance to expedite the review and handling. You are hereby informed."

The Method for Reducing the Grade of Domestic Matches Has Been Extended for Another Year; The Ministry of Railways Instructs the Railway Bureau to Comply

The Two Railway Administration Bureau received instructions from the Ministry of Railways yesterday stating, "The China National Match Industry Association has submitted a report stating that the deadline for the method of reducing the grade of transportation for Chinese matches is approaching, and the Chinese match industry is still depressed. It has requested that the deadline be extended for another three years in order to provide relief and maintain the industry, etc. After reviewing the various points mentioned by the Association, they are still true. It should be approved to extend the deadline for another year from January 1, 1934, in order to maintain the industry. In addition to the approval, a copy of the original report is enclosed, and the Bureau is instructed to comply." After receiving the instructions, the Railway Bureau forwarded them to the Traffic Department for compliance.

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association Sent a Letter to the Municipal Council, Asking It to Pay Attention to the Disguised Price Increase of Telephones

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday stating, "Regarding the matter of Shanghai telephones proposing to increase prices again, we have previously sent a letter on October 16 requesting the Council to reject the request. Subsequently, we received letters from all walks of life expressing opposition to the price increase. We are pleased to learn that the Council has rejected the company's request. However, if the company still intends to change its approach and make another request, please firmly reject it again based on the contract and the contents of the company's letter requesting a price increase on August 15, 1930. Furthermore, judging from the current operating conditions of the company, there is no reason for a loss. There may be unreasonable items in its expenditures. It is difficult to understand the actual situation without a detailed examination of its accounts. However, this examination cannot be done by Mr. Ford, the Director of Finance of the Council. It is essential to find out the real situation in the slightest. If any unreasonable accounts are found, this is a direct problem with the patent contract and should be corrected. Even if we take a step back, even if a request for a price increase can be discussed in accordance with the contract in 1935, there will still be major problems. In addition to bearing reasonable costs, users should not and absolutely do not want to bear any unreasonable costs. We therefore request the Council to pay close attention to this matter and not allow the company to deceive or mislead. We are confident that the Council will maintain justice." This letter is addressed to the Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession.

A Visit to the Huang's Livestock and Planting Farm

Mr. Huang Yuezhou, a revolutionary predecessor from Fenghua, returned from his official career in the final years of the Qing Dynasty and purchased several acres of farmland in the Zhenru North area of the city, investing in developing a garden for livestock and planting. After decades of operation, it has now expanded to hundreds of acres and is a sight to behold. The reporter accepted Mr. Huang's invitation to visit, and the details are as follows:

Garden Arrangement

The Huang Family Livestock and Planting Farm is located about two miles north of Zhenru. Take the No. 3 public bus from the North Railway Station and get off at Southeast Medical College. Walk about a mile to reach it. The farm is surrounded by bamboo fences and planted with holly. Inside the farm, there are about sixty to seventy acres of farmland, and outside the farm, there are another forty to fifty acres, totaling over one hundred and dozens of acres. In the middle of the entrance, there are three thatched huts where the Huang family resides. The flowers and trees in the garden are arranged in an orderly manner. The trees are mainly woody plants, such as plum, pear, peach, osmanthus, maple, pine, and so on, totaling more than ten thousand plants. Orchids, chrysanthemums, peonies, etc., are also available in abundance. Several ponds are dug in the garden to raise fish. Rockeries and exotic bamboos are captivating. Among them, osmanthus, bamboo, and peonies have as many as fifty or sixty varieties, which is even more commendable and truly spectacular.

Resisting Japanese Goods

When Mr. Huang first started developing the land, he only had a few acres. Later, Japanese people in Shanghai engaged in horticulture, encroaching on the market. Mr. Huang, being a revolutionary veteran, felt distressed upon seeing this. Therefore, he used all his resources to expand and cultivate various exotic flowers and trees to compete with the Japanese, which proved to be surprisingly effective. Currently, many large flower gardens in various ports are ordering flowers and trees from Mr. Huang.

Establishment of the Takahashi Jiangxinsha Defense Corps

Since the municipal government designated Takahashi Jiangxinsha Island as an oil depot area, major oil companies such as Guanghua, Asia, and Texaco have successively established oil depots and built factories on the island. As a result, the market has become lively, and the population has increased sharply. Local gentry and merchants, considering the police force to be weak and fearing that villains might take the opportunity to infiltrate and disrupt public order, initiated the organization of a defense corps for self-defense. It has already been approved by the Shanghai Municipal Defense Corps Management Committee. Yesterday, a founding ceremony was held. There are more than sixty members in the corps, fully equipped with firearms. The captain is Zhu Gongfu, and it is under the jurisdiction of the Takahashi District Defense Corps. Guests included Zhu Xiaoyan, Gu Danchao, Xu Yunlong, etc. After a speech by the head of the Takahashi District, Mr. Lan, Zhu Xiaoyan and others successively gave speeches, all encouraging the members to protect the local area and love the people, so as to fulfill their responsibilities.

The Whole Story of the Tragic Murder of a Mother and Daughter in Lujiazhai, Pudong - Patrolman Zheng Wanming, Number Ten, is the Main Culprit - This Case is Definitely Not a Robbery, But a Revenge

Hu Changming, a butcher from Funing, residing in Maoyeli, Lujiazhai, Pudong, was suddenly invaded by three thugs at about 10:00 pm on the first day of this month. They robbed him of 200 yuan in cash and several gold-plated jewelry items, and shot and killed Hu's wife, Madam Yu, and Hu's daughter, Xiuzhen, both. When Hu's wife was dying, she cried out, "The one who killed me is Number Ten!" Thereupon, the Public Security Bureau immediately identified this statement as a clue to the case. After days of searching by police and detectives, it was confirmed that the main culprit in this case was the patrolman known as Number Ten, who is now a concession patrolman. Several key suspects and suspects have been arrested one after another. This case is by no means a robbery, but a revenge by the said Number Ten, deliberately using robbery to cover up his evil plan. The whole story is recorded below.

Patrolman Number Ten

The so-called Number Ten was formerly a patrolman Number Ten in the Xiang Sheng Iron Factory in Pudong. Now he is a gatekeeper patrolman in Renxingli at the Broadway intersection of the Public Concession, with the number 1206. His name is Zheng Wanming, he is in his forties, from Qingjiang, and lives at No. 44 Hutang Road, Lujiazhai, Pudong. He was originally acquainted with the plaintiff, Hu Changming. In the past, Zheng had acted as a matchmaker for Hu's only beloved daughter (namely the deceased Xiuzhen), trying to betroth her to Zheng's nephew as his wife. However, Hu's wife (namely the deceased Madam Yu) strongly opposed it and stopped it. Zheng knew that Hu was foolish and old, unable to do anything, and was only obstructed by Madam Yu, and the matter did not go as he wished. Therefore, he harbored resentment in his heart. The motive for the tragic case was planted here.

The Tragic Case Occurred

Recently, Hu recruited a son-in-law for his beloved daughter as an heir. On the day the son-in-law entered the family, a grand banquet was held to invite relatives and friends. Zheng knew about it beforehand, so on the 28th of last month, he invited his friends Li Wenqi and Jiang Chuanren to his home to secretly discuss a revenge plan. The night after Hu's family held the wine banquet, Zheng took a box cannon and led the way in, Jiang followed behind, and Li watched from outside the door. Thereupon, the blood case occurred in an instant. In addition to shooting and killing Hu, his wife, and his daughter, Zheng also robbed 200 yuan in cash and fled to the fields east of the house.

Extreme Suspicion

After the incident, Hu's mind was confused. The Public Security Bureau asked him whether the Number Ten mentioned by Hu's wife before her death was suspected in this case. Hu still tried his best to defend Number Ten (namely Zheng Wanming), insisting that Zheng was very friendly with him and would never use such means. He insisted that the ones who killed his wife and daughter were unfamiliar bandits. However, the Public Security Bureau still did not believe him. District Chief Zhang Mingqin ordered the police detectives to investigate strictly. After three or four days, Hu's mind calmed down slightly, and he suddenly remembered that about two hours before the incident, around 8:00 pm, a neighbor named Li Wenqi came to Hu's house to ask for cold water. Hu was having dinner, so he asked Li to stay and drink together. Li took the opportunity to ask Hu whether his family property was worth more than 1,000 gold. Hu strongly denied it. Li also said that if not 1,000, then 600 or 700 must be there. Hu smiled and ignored it. At the same time, another neighbor, Jiang Chuanren (nicknamed Jiang Dabianzi), also came to Hu's house to pay membership fees. Unexpectedly, two hours later, the incident occurred. Based on this imagined situation, Li and Jiang were highly suspected. He repeated the situation to the Third District and asked them to investigate.

Fleeing Upon Hearing the News

Upon receiving the report, District Chief Zhang immediately sent Patrol Officer Liu Huansheng and Police Chief Guo Yongliang, along with Detective Leader Zhang Yingpin, detectives Jiang Binru, Wang Jiheng, etc., to Li's residence at No. 41 Maoyeli, Lujiazhai, and arrested Li Wenqi. They also brought three suspects, Song Jinyu, Guo Yirong, and Shi Yucai, etc., to the district. After Li arrived at the district, he confessed that Zheng Wanming had ordered him to go together, and Jiang Chuanren had also gone. The District Chief then sent personnel to arrest Jiang. At the same time, he ordered Leader Zhang and the detectives to lead the detectives to Zheng Wanming's residence at No. 44 Hutang Road, Lujiazhai, to arrest Zheng. When they arrived, Zheng's house door was wide open, but there was no one inside, and only the furniture had not been moved at all. It was known that Zheng had fled with his family upon hearing the news. The court went to the Public Concession Police Station to investigate and learned that Zheng had not gone to work on the night of the incident and had asked someone else to take his place. Therefore, it was even more certain that he had committed the crime. District Chief Zhang was then reported to first seal Zheng's house and, at the same time, ordered the detectives and police to strictly investigate and arrest the main culprit Zheng Wanming and bring him to justice.

Confessions of the Suspects

After several accomplices and suspects in this case were detained in the district, District Chief Zhang interrogated them separately. According to Li Wenqi's confession, he was 33 years old, from Tengxian County, Shandong, and worked as a porter on the wharf. At first, he tried to evade the issue, claiming that he did not follow Zheng to rob and kill. Later, he admitted it without hesitation. According to him, in addition to being a patrolman, Zheng also lent out money at high interest. I borrowed seven yuan from him, and I had to pay 28 copper coins in interest every day. However, I was very poor, and after more than three years, the principal and interest totaled about one hundred and dozens of yuan, which I have not yet repaid. On the 28th of last month, Zheng suddenly invited me to his home to talk. Zheng directly asked me for the debt, and I replied that I was unable to repay it at the moment. Zheng then said, "If you do something for me, not only can you not have to repay the debt, but you can also make a small fortune." Jiang Chuanren also participated in the discussion at that time. After the plan was decided, the three of them went to implement it together. After the goal was achieved, the three of them fled to the fields of Wujia Hall, which had been agreed upon in advance. I received 50 yuan on the spot, which is true. I ask for leniency in the sentence. According to Jiang Chuanren's confession, he was from Yushan County, Jiangxi, and lived at No. 72 Wufu Road, Lujiazhai, running the Jianglou Teahouse. He firmly denied that he had participated in the robbery and murder. According to Song Jinyu's confession, I lived in the same house as Li Wenqi, but I was completely unaware of Li's crime. Guo Yirong confessed that he lived at No. 43 Taiping Bridge in the French Concession and worked in Zhang's residence. He went to Song Jinyu's house to find a friend on that day and was suddenly arrested. According to Shi Wangcai's confession, he lived at No. 28 Maoyeli and worked as a small worker in a cigarette factory. At that time, I was standing in front of Li Wenqi's door and was suddenly arrested by the police detectives in the district. The District Chief then found out that the person who helped Zheng find a guaranteed rental house was Zheng's brother-in-law, Fang Wumen, from Yancheng, who lived at No. 10 Hutangbang. He sent the police to bring Fang to the case and ordered all the people, together with Yu Lianshan, a resident of Qingjiang who first reported the tragic case to the district, to be sent to the Public Security Bureau yesterday for interrogation.

The Minhang Guangci Hospital Chrysanthemum Exhibition and Play Performance

The Minhang Guangci Hospital was founded by Mr. Shen Menglian and others.
