A Solemn Statement by the Film Censorship Committee Regarding the Appeal of Three Film Merchants Published in Western Newspapers

The Film Censorship Committee of the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior made a solemn statement regarding a news article titled "The Appeal of Three Film Merchants" published in the editorial of the North China Daily News on September 14th and the Greater Shanghai Evening Post on the 15th, which involved the committee in many ways. The committee stated that the item "each film requires a fee of 1,500 yuan" was particularly alarming. The committee stated, "The committee is responsible for film censorship administration, and the legal procedures are very strict. Film censorship is conducted in the order of applications. The censorship fee for foreign-made films is 10 yuan for every 500 meters, and films less than 500 meters are also calculated as 500 meters. The consumption fee for domestic films is 15 yuan for long films and 5 yuan for short films. The license fee for each approved film is 3 yuan. Regarding the censorship work, films are screened and censored once each morning and afternoon, and sometimes also at night to ensure promptness. With such strict procedures, there should be no cause for concern. However, it is feared that the outside world is not fully aware, and unscrupulous individuals may take advantage of this to defraud merchants of money directly and indirectly damage the reputation of the committee. Therefore, in November of last year, the committee made all procedures into a complete notice (attached separately) and published them in various newspapers in Beijing and Shànghǎi for five or six days in a row, which was visible to all. But now, according to the aforementioned records, it is quite unexpected. For the sake of the future of the film industry and the reputation of the committee, various company representatives in Beijing, including Ge Weichang, Yu Daorui, Gu Zurong, Zhou Fangzhi, Liang Bo, and Ding Bowen, were summoned to the committee to inquire about the details. They all stated, 'The handling fee for each foreign-made long film is 30 yuan, and the handling fee for each short film is 3 yuan. From application to receiving the license, the total cost, including printing, transportation, and censorship consumption fees, is about 80 to 120 yuan. There are no other special fees or entertainment expenses. The application procedures for domestic films are either handled by friends or entrusted to theater managers in Beijing, and the handling fees are roughly the same as for foreign films.' At the same time, a letter was sent to the China Film Federation in Shànghǎi to inquire with various companies, and the reply stated, 'All members of this federation are aware that the censorship fee has a fixed amount, which is absolutely uniform. The reported fee of 1,500 yuan per film may be the combined calculation of tariffs, miscellaneous fees, and censorship fees required for foreign films entering China.' Recently, a film expense survey form filled out by MGM, sent by the China Film Federation in Shànghǎi, showed that the maximum cost of transporting each film to China was no more than 1,036 yuan, and the average cost was about 750 yuan. After this multifaceted investigation, it is clear that this record is completely untrue and needs to be solemnly corrected. It is urgent to list the facts of the process and send a letter to your office to disclose the truth as news and correct the public opinion. We are deeply grateful to the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior Film Censorship Committee." The original manuscript of the notice distributed to various newspapers in Beijing and Shànghǎi in November of the 21st year is attached below: "The committee's inspection of films has set procedures for the handling of the film, payment of fees, registration, arrangement of the schedule, receipt of the license, and receipt of the film, which are difficult to change. Regarding the expenses, domestic films are not charged a censorship fee, only a consumption fee of 15 yuan for long films and 5 yuan for short films. Foreign films are charged a censorship fee of 10 yuan for every 500 meters, and the license fee is 2 yuan, plus a stamp duty of 1 yuan, all within the scope of laws and regulations, which must not be exceeded. Recently, it has been heard that some people are arbitrarily making a show outside, or deceiving film merchants, claiming to be able to help with lobbying, provide convenience, or making illegal demands from film merchants under the pretext of agency applications, or fabricating facts and slandering each other, which are all violations of the law. In order to uphold the law, this committee will search for evidence and pursue the matter according to law. If anyone obtains evidence of making a show, they should report it to this committee for legal action. Film merchants are also requested to pay close attention and not be fooled by those who make a show because of expectations, resulting in losses and inconvenience. This is hereby announced."

Local News

The Sino-German Art Exhibition is Collecting Works for Exhibition in Shànghǎi ▲Location: World Academy, Fúkāisēn Road

The Sino-German joint Berlin Art Exhibition is scheduled to be held at the Berlin National Academy next spring. The first batch of more than 300 works is scheduled to be transported to Germany by the organizing committee member Liu Haisu on the 13th of this month for arrangement. Recently, Central Committee member Wang Qi and others expressed their opinions that the exhibition is of great importance, and for the sake of caution, a preliminary exhibition should be held first, and ancient works should be added. According to Liu Haisu, after the exhibits were collected, they were carefully reviewed. It has now been decided to hold a preliminary exhibition on the 10th and 11th of this month at the World Academy on Fúkāisēn Road for two days. After the exhibition, they will be transported to Germany for arrangement on the 13th, with no delay. The collection of modern and contemporary works was requested by the Germans, as they already have a lot of ancient Chinese collections and do not need much more.

Shànghǎi University Students' Mandarin Speech Contest ▲The final will be held on December 9th ▲The deadline for registration is the 25th of this month

The Mandarin Speech Contest for University Students, organized by the Shànghǎi University Federation, has been decided to hold the preliminary on December 2nd and the final on the 9th. The deadline for registration is the 25th of this month. The contest rules are as follows: (1) November 25th is the deadline for registration. The registration location is Guānghuá University. (2) Two students from each school participate in the competition. (3) The topic of the speech is chosen by the student and registered at the time of registration. (4) The order of speeches will be drawn before the competition. (5) The speech is divided into two rounds: the preliminary will be held at 2:00 PM on December 2nd, and the final will be held at 2:00 PM on December 9th. If the number of registrants exceeds 14, the preliminary will be held in two groups. If it exceeds 28, it will be held in three groups. (6) The order of speeches in the preliminary will be drawn and must be based on individuals. The top four will be selected from each group. (7) The prizes will be collected by the executive committee. The number of prizes will depend on the number of groups in the preliminary. If the preliminary is held in one or two groups, prizes will be awarded to the top three in the final. If the preliminary is held in three groups, prizes will be awarded to the top five in the final. (8) Three judges will be invited for each group in the preliminary, and another three will be invited to serve as judges in the final, all of which will be handled by the executive committee. All current faculty and staff of the universities participating in the speech contest may not be judges. (9) The location of the preliminary and final will be determined by the executive committee, but the final should be held in a public place. (10) The time limit for each speech is ten minutes. (11) The judging criteria are: structure 30%, thought 30%, voice 20%, and demeanor 20%. (12) The audience must remain calm before the results of the speech contest are announced. (13) When the speech reaches eight minutes, the timekeeper will ring the preparation bell once. When it reaches ten minutes, they will ring it again. At this time, the speaker must stop speaking immediately upon hearing the bell. (14) The speech results will be calculated by converting the scores given by each judge into rankings, and then adding the rankings together to get a number. The speaker with the smallest number is the first place, and so on. If the speakers have the same number of rankings, the order will be determined by the total score. (15) After the judges have assessed the scores, they will be sent to the chairman for calculation and announcement.

The Registration for the Slapstick Competition Organized by the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Education Bureau is Closed ▲More than 60 Contestants ▲The Competition Schedule Will Be Announced Tomorrow

The registration for the slapstick performance competition organized by the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Education Bureau has been closed yesterday. There are 32 participating units, including contestants Liu Chunshan, Sheng Daidai, Jiang Xiaoxiao, Bao Lele, Lu Xixi, Lu Qiqi, Pei Yanghua, Fan Haha, Zhao Xixi, Ding Guaiguai, Lü Kufeng, Zhu Xiangfei, and female contestants Xia Xiuying, Xia Xiuzhen, and 64 others. The prizes for the winners have been collected by the Education Bureau from Mayor Wu, Secretary-General Yu, and various bureau chiefs, section chiefs, and committee members of the Municipal Party Headquarters. Each participant will be given a certificate and a medal, and a travel allowance of one yuan. The opening ceremony is scheduled to be held at the Citizen Education Center at 1:00 PM on the 12th of this month. All contestants must be present to participate. It is expected that the competition will be completed in three days. In order to limit the audience, the Municipal Education Bureau will charge two dimes per ticket, and the venue can accommodate 200 people each day. The revenue from three days of ticket sales is 90 yuan. After deducting the travel allowance for the contestants and the cost of purchasing prizes, the shortfall will be subsidized by the Education Bureau. The competition schedule will be finalized and announced today.

Municipal Education Center and Frontier Bank Solicit Essays from Primary and Secondary School Students ▲The Topic Is "My Savings Plan" with Substantial Prizes ▲Submissions Accepted from Today Until the End of This Month

The Shanghai Municipal Public Education Center, which previously jointly prepared to establish a Public Savings Office with the Shanghai China Frontier Bank, is now ready and scheduled to hold an opening ceremony on the 12th of this month. In order to encourage primary and secondary school students to have a deep understanding of savings, it has specially jointly launched a solicitation of essays from primary and secondary school students, titled "My Savings Plan." The essay solicitation methods are recorded as follows: (1) Origin: In order to encourage primary and secondary school students to have a deep understanding of savings, this office will solicit personal savings plans from primary and secondary school students at the beginning of its operation. In the future, it plans to select and publish a special collection, which will be distributed to the contributors to encourage each other to achieve success, so that they can be diligent and thrifty students in school and diligent and thrifty citizens in society. The enrichment of personal and national economic strength will naturally be among them. This is the humble intention of this office to initiate a micro-essay competition. (2) Topic: My Savings Plan. (3) Style: Classical Chinese or vernacular Chinese are both acceptable, with simplicity and practicality as the main points. Empty talk is not accepted. (4) Paper: The paper is not limited, but it is best to transcribe it on school-used exercise paper. (5) Stamps: Each manuscript must indicate the name, age, grade in school, and mailing address of the contributor, and affix the essay solicitation stamp of this office. (6) Deadline: The deadline is the end of November this year. Contributors must submit their entries to the Public Education Center at Wenmiao Road, Ximen, Shanghai before the deadline. (7) Announcement: Famous people will be invited to judge, and the winners will be announced on New Year's Day of the 23rd year of the Republic of China. The selected students will be notified by special letter. The list of winners can be obtained from this office at that time. (8) Prizes: The first place will receive the first collection of the Commercial Press's Elementary School Student Library (valued at 70 yuan). The second to fifth places will each receive a night-light desk clock from the Ya Pu Er Electric Appliance Factory (each valued at 35 yuan). The sixth to fifteenth places will each receive a pair of double-lens glass inkwells from the China Pottery Company (each valued at 4 yuan). The fifteenth place and below will each receive a specially made commemorative silver coin (the number of places will be determined at the time).

Preparatory Committee Meeting for the City's Boy Scout Review

The Preparatory Committee for the Fifth Shanghai Boy Scout Review and Jamboree held its sixth meeting yesterday. The committee members present were Wu Tiecheng (represented by Li Dachao), Tong Xingbai, Pan Gongzhan (represented by Du Gang), Qu Yue, Zhang Xunfang, Leng Xueqiao, Luo Lie, Yu Kuiyuan, Zhao Weizu, Ye Chunnian (represented by Xu Guozhi), Gong Jingyuan, etc. Leng Xueqiao chaired the meeting, and Luo Lie recorded the minutes. (A) Report Items: (1) The number of registered participants for the review and jamboree is 56 group units, 246 tents, and 3,539 Boy Scouts. (2) Judges Yao Linshu and Liu Zao were unable to attend the meeting to perform their duties due to other matters. (3) The headquarters and the preparatory office of the General Association sent Gu Shusen as a representative to Shanghai to provide guidance and issued various prizes. (4) A total of 86 prize silver shields, silver cups, and award flags have been received, and a total of 4,730 other items. (5) The campsite layout has already started today, including archways, review stands, and toilets. (B) Discussion Items: (1) The request from Groups 113, 129, 677, and 846 to demarcate the campsite in one continuous area was discussed and resolved that it was difficult to approve. (2) The motion to retroactively approve the delegation of the campsite vending section to the Greater Shanghai Consumer Cooperative was discussed and resolved to approve the retroactive approval, but the items sold and prices should be approved by the General Affairs Section of this association. (3) The motion to add a campsite post office was discussed and resolved to hire the Postal Worker Boy Scout Group to take on the task. (4) The motion to hire additional reception staff was discussed and resolved to hire Zhao Weizu, Sun Yiming, Wang Gang, Xu Guozhi, Zou Halu, and Fan Xiaoliu. (5) The motion on how to handle the situation if Sun Yixin, the general commander of the review, is unable to participate due to returning to his hometown for mourning was discussed and resolved to promote Qu Yue to take on the role.

Preferential Treatment for Primary and Secondary School Students to Visit the Circus

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau previously received a report from Gu Jiwu, the principal of the Municipal Shuji Elementary School, stating that the importance of direct observation in common sense education has been generally recognized by educators. The German Haikingbo Circus troupe has come to Shanghai to perform, and it has a variety of rare and exotic animals. If children can witness it in person, they will benefit greatly. Therefore, it is sincerely requested to negotiate with the Haikingbo Circus troupe to give all children in the city a good opportunity to visit for free. When the bureau sent personnel to negotiate, a preferential treatment method has been agreed upon. All visitors will be charged a discount of 50 cents per person, with the principle of being able to get a seat. Visitors to the zoo will be charged a discount of 10 cents per person. If schools want to lead students to visit the zoo or performances, they should report the number of people to the bureau before this Saturday (the 11th), and pay the fees. The bureau will then notify them to go to visit in batches on a scheduled basis.

Sports

Students Studying in Japan Expelled and Returned to Shanghai ▲This Year, the Number of Laborers and Students Expelled and Returned to China Has Reached More Than 1,000 ▲Taking Landscape Photos, Accused of Violating the Prohibition Order, Detained in the Police Station, and Finally Expelled

Japan is excluding Chinese people, prohibiting Chinese workers from entering the country, and even those engaged in kimono and barbering businesses are only allowed to leave Japan and return to China, and are not allowed to go to Japan from China. This year, the number of Chinese people and students studying in Japan who have been successively expelled and returned to China has reached more than 1,000. Every month, there are often batches of overseas Chinese who have been expelled arriving in Shanghai, mostly from Qingtian, Yongjia, and Fujian in Zhejiang Province, etc. This has become commonplace and cannot be fully recorded. This time, the Shanghai Maru of the Japan Mail Steamship Company came to Shanghai, and our Chinese students Wu Chengxian, Liu Qiaosen, Li Rong, and Zhong Yuli were also arrested by the Japanese authorities from Tokyo, Kobe and other places, first detained in the police station, and then escorted onto the ship and expelled back to Shanghai. What the Japanese used to apply to Chinese laborers is now being applied to students. It is found that the expulsion of these students this time was due to taking landscape photos while traveling in various parts of Japan, which aroused the jealousy of the Japanese police, who accused them of violating the entry prohibition order and suspected them, and detained each person in the police station. Without asking right or wrong, they forced them to be expelled and ordered them to take the Shanghai Maru wheel to Shanghai, and were not allowed to go to Japan again.

Yesterday's Friendly Football Match Donghua Wins Against the British Army 丨Five to Two丨

The Donghua Football Team has made some changes in its lineup this year in preparation for winning the championship, so it has stepped up its training. Yesterday afternoon, it specially invited the British Army stationed in Shanghai to play a friendly match. The Army was represented by the Survey Team. As a result, Donghua won by a large margin of five to two. The referee was Li Silian.

▲New Faces Donghua is actively training new talents to prepare for the gap between generations. Yesterday's forwards included several players from Shanghai and the masters of small ball games. Their performance was not bad, but they lacked experience and their movements were still slow. They missed several opportunities to shoot at the goal and lacked cooperation. They only knew how to rush forward and lacked communication. With more training, they should be able to improve. The opponent was a Group B team. The goalkeeper and the defense were good, and the right winger was the most stable.

▲First Half The strength of the British army was mediocre, so the difference in strength was immediately apparent. For the first 15 minutes of the match, neither side established a lead. Xiao Hu Cao Qiuting and right winger Jia Youliang were very familiar with each other from their small ball days, so their connection yesterday was very active. After Yuan Qingwu missed twice, Jia Youliang launched a long shot from the eastern suburbs. Shi Te was unable to nail it down, and Hai Fute tried to be clever but shot himself in the foot. The ball fell into the middle of the 12-yard area, and Chen Hongguang rushed to it immediately and kicked it in, opening the scoring. From then on, the Donghua flag could be seen everywhere on the British army's territory. Xu Jingcheng and Hongguang constantly probed and probed, making the opponent feel extremely uneasy. Finally, Xiao Jia made a comeback and hooked the ball into the center, with a very good landing point. Chen Hongguang rushed to meet it with his head, and Ximen was distracted and lost another goal. The British army became more and more discouraged after the restart. At the 40th minute, Cao Qiuting reached a heavily defended area, and Hongguang scored another goal. The score at halftime was 4-0.

▲Second Half Donghua saw that getting the ball was as easy as picking something out of a bag, and inevitably became arrogant. Not long after the start of the second half, the three center backs, due to helping the forwards attack, left the defense empty, allowing Shi Te to sneak in, and suddenly broke into the interior. A cross from Huishoulu, who fired a shot from afar, Lu Zhongen was absent-minded and lost a goal. The Chen brothers joined forces in the southern expedition, and Ximen's save was the most exciting scene. Chen Yutian, the desperate Saburo, was a veteran craftsman, and with the help of Dr. Tu, he made great contributions. Before five minutes had passed, Cao Xiaohu and Jia Youliang echoed each other, crossed the center back line, and Qiuting used all his strength to shoot the ball out like an arrow. Ximen failed to save the ball, making it a 5-1 situation. After a long time of melee, the British army center forward Fulun shot in another goal from afar, making it 2-5. The battle ended. Shanghai Secondary School Sports Federation Football League Schedule

▲A Total of Nine Schools Will Participate on the 15th

The Shanghai Secondary School Sports Federation organized the Secondary School Football Championship League. Since the start of the report, a total of nine schools have participated in this year's league as of the previous day. Zhang Xien (Chairman), Jiang Jingnan, Han Kuiyong, (Lu Xiangqian's representative) of the Football Committee of the Association held a meeting at the Sports Association yesterday afternoon to discuss the competition rules of this year's football competition and draw up the competition schedule. The resolutions are recorded as follows:

(1) Competition Dates The competition will start on the 15th of this month and end on the 20th of next month. Every Wednesday at 2:30 pm, the competition will be held in rotation at each school. That is, if the competition was held in School A last year, it will be held in School B this year. Any team that fails to appear for the competition within 15 minutes of the start will be considered to have forfeited the match. (This does not apply if the delay is caused by unforeseen circumstances en route.)

(2) Group Competition In order to facilitate the competition and save time, the nine participating schools will be divided into two groups, "Zhong" and "Ti". The "Zhong" group includes Daxia, Chizhi, Minli, Fuzhong, and Pudong, a total of five schools. The "Ti" group includes Guanghua, Jinan, Yuqing, and Fushi, a total of four schools.

(3) Competition System Both groups will adopt a single round-robin competition system. The winner will get two points, the loser will get zero points, and a draw will get one point each. The teams with the most points in the two groups will then hold a final to determine the championship.

(4) Competition Rules The football rules set by the National Games will be implemented in full. However, the competition time will be changed to 70 minutes (35 minutes for each half) with a 10-minute break. The competition time for the final will also be handled in the same way.

(5) Referees The referees will be hired by the home team with the consent of the visiting team. The linesmen will be appointed by each side. The referees and linesmen for the final will be hired by the Chairman of the Football Committee.

(6) Postponement of Competition 1. If it rains or the ground is wet, the two sides will jointly select a date for the makeup match. 2. If a postponement is requested due to special circumstances, the Chairman of the Committee must be notified five days in advance. If the Chairman of the Committee deems that there are sufficient reasons after reviewing, the makeup match date may be negotiated with the other party, but the makeup match must be completed before December 20.

(7) Player List The player list of each team must be sent to the Football Chairman Zhang Xien (Chizhi Affiliated Middle School, Kunshan Road) before the 15th of this month for verification. When each school competes, it must still submit the list of players of the team to the referee. After the referee signs it, the home team will be responsible for reporting the results of the competition to the Football Chairman Zhang Xien (within two days), otherwise, it will be regarded as a waiver. (8) Competition Schedule The committee decided to draw the following:

▲Zhong Group

This month 15th Daxia vs. Pudong at Pudong Fuzhong vs. Minli at Minli

This month 22nd Minli vs. Chizhi at Chizhi Fuzhong vs. Pudong at Pudong

This month 29th Chizhi vs. Fuzhong at Fuzhong Minli vs. Daxia at Daxia

Next month 6th Chizhi vs. Daxia at Daxia Pudong vs. Minli at Minli

Next month 13th Pudong vs. Chizhi at Chizhi Daxia vs. Fuzhong at Fuzhong

▲Ti Group

Essays

New Village

—Yanqiao

I often hear people say that to improve the lives of farmers and increase their welfare, we must build new villages. But in reality, I have not seen any new village that is sufficient to achieve this extravagant hope. The Good Samaritan Bridge in Suzhou has a new village, which is being planned and is in progress, but it is not yet mature. But I heard from someone who had been there that they are now using all their strength in education, and have no time for other constructions, and without a solid educational foundation, even if there are tall and magnificent buildings, they will soon collapse. Therefore, the construction of a new village is a meticulous task, like an old woman cutting the bottom of a sock, and it cannot be accomplished by large-scale, careless, and impetuous planning.

The day before yesterday, the education community of Wujiang visited Xugong Bridge in Kunshan and outside the West Gate of Wuxi and came back. They told me that the glimpse of Xugong Bridge gave them an impression that "there are no idle people in the village, and no waste on the road." It is said that even the police in the police station are so free that they have nothing to police. As for the most common gambling and opium, they are absolutely not allowed to stay within dozens of miles. An unknown opium peddler was driven out of the country. I ask, do other rural areas have this impression? Outside the West Gate of Wuxi is a world of thatched huts. Those coolies are struggling to feed themselves, let alone recognize characters and read books. At first, the educators were exhausted, but they still turned a blind eye, and it was rare for a few to come and join in the fun for a few minutes. Later, they implemented Lu Dianhu's thatched pavilion lecture from the past, and built a slightly scientific thatched hut in the group of thatched huts. The educators lived there, met them day and night, and then taught them after they finished their work. On the one hand, they also jointly run a nursery with the leaders of the factory, so that each has a place to go. In less than a year, the atmosphere has been completely new. When they went to visit that day, it was still early, and they did not see the teaching, but there were two rickshaw pullers playing chess there. It is said that they originally did not recognize a single character, but now they can read slogans.

In the city, we often see children from wealthy families who study carelessly. No matter how earnestly you speak, they not only ignore you, but even want to argue with you. It is better to go to reclaim wasteland, and get as much harvest as you put in effort.

Liquor Money and "Come-See"

— Shi Chun

Some people say that today's society is completely a society of money, where everything is about monetary transactions. This is certainly true, especially in big cities. Going out to do anything requires spending money that disappears without a trace. If you use the very fashionable term "come-see" (some call it "compson" in pidgin English, actually a mispronunciation of "come-see," meaning kickback, but in Shanghai, it's used as a general term for tips), or if you don't want to sound so fancy, you call it "liquor money."

I remember the first time I traveled. When I got on the train, the porter asked me for liquor money because I had some luggage. I was young at the time and asked him how much liquor he wanted to drink. The relative traveling with me laughed so hard he bent over. Later, I learned that liquor money wasn't really for buying liquor. But the origin of the term "liquor money" remains unknown to me. What's strange is that in Germany, there's also the term "Trinkgeld," which is similar. However, in the United States or England, it's called "Tip," which is different from Germany. Japan doesn't have the bad habit of liquor money at all, so there's no such term, which is much more convenient.

In Shanghai, the amount spent on liquor money during festivals is considerable. Starting from home, street sweepers, toilet cleaners, lane managers, watchmen, and policemen guarding the lanes all line up with outstretched hands to ask for money. In winter, there are even people on the streets shouting about fire safety. The amount ranges from a few copper coins for the cheap ones to silver dollars for the expensive ones. You have to take care of them during every festival, it is even more important than owing a debt. Working in a business is even worse. From the errand boy in the shop to the tea server, to the elevator operator and doorman, everyone wants liquor money. If you give too little, they'll curse you behind your back, roll their eyes at you. The situation when no liquor money is given is self-evident.

In Shanghai, it's even easier to encounter liquor money demands. An employee from the water company only needs to touch your water pipe to ask for liquor money. An electrician who fixes your fuse box will ask for at least twenty cents for liquor money. There are countless other places where money is spent on liquor, too many to list.

Once, a postman came to my house to ask for liquor money. I gave him a bottle of sorghum wine and told him he didn't need to ask for money to buy it, just take the bottle. He knew I was making fun of him, and that postmen asking for liquor money was against postal regulations, so he left without a word. But later, I couldn't help but regret it, because I knew he must have been cursing me behind my back with vulgar words.

When I was a student, I had to pay several dollars in liquor money every semester. The tea server and the doorman had to be paid. If you went out for a snack, you had to pay liquor money in addition to the tip. Double the expense! On a ship, the liquor money on the Ningbo steamer was even more than the fare, which was alarming, and shows the prevalence of this social bad habit.

### Suzhou to Hold Fish and Chrysanthemum Show

— Yu Chi (Fish Addict)

Suzhou is a place that people colloquially call "xie yi chang hua" (a place where people can relax and enjoy life). Friends who live there like to study raising fish, growing bamboo, cultivating orchids, and planting chrysanthemums. Moreover, it is a public entertainment area. Therefore, there are many goldfish and chrysanthemums cultivated there. Every year, when the autumn sky is clear and the air is crisp, they will definitely collect the privately produced goldfish and chrysanthemums, gather them together, and hold a fish and chrysanthemum exhibition to embellish this autumn scenery. On the one hand, it can arouse the interest of tourists, and on the other hand, it can also compete for the achievements of each family. During the days of the exhibition, ladies and gentlemen gather, causing a sensation throughout the city. I remember that when last year's fish and chrysanthemum exhibition was held, it also attracted many people from the Shanghai literary and art circles to visit, which shows the value of this exhibition. This year, the park management director, Mr. Fan Yunshu, in order to increase the interest of tourists, in addition to collecting the local private famous products, also invited Shanghai's "Yu Le Guo Goldfish Garden" to participate in the event. Yu Le Guo is a large-scale organized goldfish garden, with countless rare and famous species. It is said that many rare species that are rarely seen outside will be transported to Suzhou to participate, which can also allow viewers to increase their knowledge. Now, the exhibition period of the Fish and Chrysanthemum Exhibition has been set to be held in Suzhou Wusa Road Park for three days starting from the tenth of this month. If any individual in Shanghai is willing to send products for display, they can contact Mr. Wu Jiren at the Mingxing Film Company on Xipushi Road, French Concession, Shanghai, which is the most welcome at the exhibition.

The Fever for Getting Rich, The Belief in Numerology, and The Craving for Laziness

— Fei Wenbao

In recent years, the situation has been unclear, the countryside has gone bankrupt, and the social economy has shown signs of collapse. The general public, feeling that income does not meet expenses, harbors a fluke mentality of speculation, those who think about getting rich every day are called fever for getting rich; those who blindly believe in numerology are called the belief in numerology; and those who dream of gold falling from the sky, without labor and gain are called the craving for laziness. These three types of people together constitute the fever for getting rich, the belief in numerology, and the craving for laziness, which are composed into a simple tune, 435323, which is the same as the winning lottery number of this air lottery, is it not strange? (Que Chou)

Postscript to Cheng Yanqiu's Wonderful Double Meeting

— Qi Sheng

Cheng Yanqiu went to Europe to study drama, which lasted for a year and a half. After returning to China in August, he returned to the stage, and there were many improvements. Last week, he was hired by the Nanjing Fund-raising Committee for the Yellow River Flood Disaster to perform two days of charity performances at the Lizhi Society. The ticket prices were divided into three grades of ten yuan, five yuan, and three yuan. Every day was full, which shows the enthusiasm of his social popularity. I listened to his wonderful double meeting on the second night. The beauty of his appearance was as good as before, and his voice was clearer and more melodious than it was two years ago. His expression was delicate and appropriate, and the details were exquisite. The wonderful thing is that he can put himself in the role and the emotions are consistent with the ancients. It can be said that the sorrow is touching, and the art has reached a wonderful realm. The reader can guess who is playing his husband, Zhao Chong. It is not Jiang Miaoxiang, but the Red Bean Hall Master who has not been on stage for a long time. The Hall Master is nearly sixty years old. Because he plays the role of a young student, he shaved off his beard, and it became the bare and treeless Niu Mountain. Once he put on makeup, his demeanor was elegant, and he was still like a young man of the Five Tombs, with a natural and noble grace, which is difficult to learn by human power. As for his gestures and movements, they all have laws and standards, and there is a wonderful effect of success. It is said that he has obtained the true inheritance of the famous young student Wang Guiguan, and his skills have also reached the point of perfection, with no trace of human fireworks. Seeing this, I know that the wonderfulness of the old drama art is incredible. When watching the wonderful realm, thousands of people in the audience, regardless of whether they are insiders or outsiders, all rejoiced and praised. Listening to his pronunciation, it is also unusually exquisite. The Hall Master is talented and versatile, enough to add color to the world of amateur opera, but it is a pity that it is limited by space and cannot be discussed in detail. There is an interesting story in this play. When Yanqiu took the complaint and went off the stage, he touched the chin of the Hall Master with his hand, and the audience smiled. The joy of the boudoir is greater than painting eyebrows, is this what it means?

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18 Whispering Tea Conveys Sorrow to Comfort Her Husband, Suddenly Leaving the Border with a Forced Smile to Say Goodbye to Her Family

Qizhi followed her into the house and placed a handkerchief on the tea table. Jiang, taking advantage of his inattention, pinched the handkerchief, as if it had been washed in water. Therefore, she dared not speak. Zhao Ziqiang stood in the courtyard, also thinking that when the mother and daughter met, there would surely be a bout of sorrow. So he stood outside and waited for a while. But after standing for a long time, he heard no sound, thinking that nothing was wrong. So he went to the backyard. Zhao Weng, with his hands behind his back, was pacing slowly back and forth on the corridor. So he said to Zhao Ziqiang: You came back late enough, shouldn't you return to camp? Zhao Ziqiang stood up straight and said to Zhao Weng: Do you, old man, have anything else to say to me? Zhao Weng was originally walking with his hands behind his back when he spoke. At this time, he stopped and suddenly turned his head to look at Zhao Ziqiang's face for a while. Then he touched his beard, as if he had a breath to sigh out. But when he raised his head and rolled his eyes, he held the words back again. Zhao Ziqiang saw that his father did not speak, and could not force his father to speak. So he said in a low voice: This matter is really very unfortunate. But people who are soldiers have the possibility of leaving every day. So it is a matter of course to get a command temporarily and leave temporarily. As he said this, he looked at his father, but could not continue to speak, slowly lowering his hands, and slowly lowering his eyelids. Zhao Weng put his hands in his sleeves, tilted his head slightly and looked at his son. After a long time, he suddenly straightened his face and said: Since it is time for you to return to camp, you should go, what are you doing wasting time here? I... I... He paused and said: I have nothing to say. Go! As he spoke, he did not take out his hands that were in his sleeves, but moved them up and down, as if he was making a bow to his son. But his old eyes were filled with tears, rolling in his eyes, almost flowing out. (235)

Short Story

One Morning (Part 1)

— Gu Mingdao

"Dark-skinned, healthy country girls... a flock of white geese... brown old cows... farmers with chestnut flesh on their rolled-up sleeves, backs, and legs... people pedaling waterwheels under the scorching sun... no three-dimensional buildings... no grand mansions... no melodious Cantonese opera... no women with red lips, long eyebrows, white faces, and high-heeled shoes..." All of this swirled in Ping's mind as he came to his uncle's house in the countryside to escape the summer heat. Although he was sitting under an old willow tree by a lake with his cousin Jin Fu, fishing, his attention was long gone from the fishing rod.

"What are you thinking about?" Jin Fu turned his head and asked.

"Nothing." Ping smiled, moved the fishing rod in his hand, indicating that he was trying to perk up. "I think everything in the countryside is strange. Things you can't see in the city, you can see here. Things you're used to seeing in the city, it's the opposite here."

"The city is fun, right? You're not used to living in the countryside, right?"

"Not necessarily, but I think the farmers are too poor."

"How do you know?"

"Oh, they work in the sun in such hot weather, and the reward they get is too small."

"Reward?" Jin Fu seemed not to understand.

"That is, what they deserve to maintain their lives, such as food, drink, clothing, housing, etc..." Ping said with a smile.

"They are just farmers who grow fields!" Jin Fu thought his cousin was mistaken.

A gust of wind blew, stirring up the water. Ping thought there were fish and quickly pulled up the fishing rod, but he knew that it was just seaweed. He said disappointedly,

"Let's go back and eat watermelon!"

Ping's aunt, who ate vegetarian food and chanted Buddhist scriptures in the summer, heard her son Jin Fu say how Ping sympathized with the farmers, and said,

"Amitabha, Ping is really compassionate."

"Young master, the newspaper is here." A barefoot little maid brought in a copy of the "local newspaper."

"This local newspaper is not late, how do they deliver it?"

"They walk here every day."

"Walk here. How far is it?"

"More than ten li!" Jin Fu said, "You probably think he's pitiful too!"

"No, not really, I was just asking."

His uncle was a landlord, so naturally everything in the house was very beautiful. Jin Fu told the maid to cut two watermelons, and opened the Dianhua (radio).

Ping lay on the sofa, looking at the newspaper and listening to Wang Renmei's "The Flower of Love" and the violin solo that would make you cry that were being broadcast on the radio.

"Dianhua... sofa... electric fan... watermelon... refrigerator... cold food..." Naturally, everything was available in the landlord's house. Ping thought, "Wild rose-like, healthy dark-skinned girls... white geese... old cows... men in blue cloth shirts with chestnut flesh... workers under the scorching sun..." It came again, mixed up in his mind again. He knew that what was done in the movies was just acting. He seemed to understand that these people lived a life that movie stars didn't.

There was a storm in his clothes.

The morning was much cooler. Ping went to the lake early in the morning to enjoy this rural morning. The color of the mountains, the light of the water, the green fields, and the towering old trees, children wearing only a pair of pants leading cows to graze. These were things that Ping did not often see in the city. The wild children looked at him face to face, and even the dogs barked at him.

Page 17

Free Talk

Searching for Living Vocabulary in Ancient Books

— Luo Wu

Searching for living vocabulary in ancient books is something that can be said but not done. He cannot find a living vocabulary in those ancient books.

Suppose there are "young people who can read 'Wen Xuan'" here, just a few high school students. He opens "Wen Xuan" and is determined to find a living vocabulary. Of course, he knows that some words are already dead. However, how does he distinguish which words are dead and alive? Probably only by whether he understands them or not. However, words that are understood only after reading the annotations of the Six Ministers cannot be counted, because this is originally a dead body, carried into his brain by the Six Ministers. This is only considered a living person. Even if it is resurrected in his brain, it is still a dead thing in the eyes of "young people who cannot read 'Wen Xuan'." So he must read the plain text.

Indeed, there are also some that can be understood without reading the annotations. This is a living vocabulary. However, how would he understand it in the first place? This must be because he has seen it in other books, or it is a vocabulary that is still in use now, so he understands it. So, what did he find from a "Wen Xuan"?

However, Mr. Shi said that it is useful when describing palaces and the like. This is very good. There are many fu in "Wen Xuan" that talk about palaces, and there are also special fu for what palace. If a young person wants to write a historical novel of the Han and Jin dynasties, describing the palaces of that time, it is extremely appropriate to look for "Wen Xuan", and it is also necessary to look at "The Four Histories", "The Book of Jin" and the like. However, the remote characters taken are only raising the dead bodies, and calling them "resurrection" when speaking mysteriously. If what is to be described is the Qing Forbidden City, then the relationship with "Wen Xuan" is extremely small.

If even the Qing Forbidden City is not wanted to be described, but the preparatory work is used so extensively, then it is really in vain and still insufficient. Because there are also "The Book of Changes" and "The Book of Rites". The vocabulary inside is useful when describing the divination lessons and weddings and funerals of the Zhou Dynasty, and it must also be used as the basis of literary cultivation, which is more like the appearance of a "literary youth".

Talking About Tobacco and Opium Again

— Zi Zhan

I have already written an article on "Tobacco and Opium", and now there are things that can be continued. Wang Fuzhi's Chuanshan Poems Collection has a poem about poppy:

Petite head drooping, full and graceful face.

Flower king should not be jealous, I do not bloom in spring.

There is also a sentence in the Miscellaneous Yong Four Quatrains: "Poppy seedlings are light and green, and the petals are delicate." Using poppies as an ornamental flower is seen again in Wang's poems. I think that during the Ming Dynasty, Wang was not the only one who planted this flower, nor was it limited to Hunan. In the middle of the Ming Dynasty, the emperor did not meet with his ministers often. During the Wanli period, Emperor Shenzong lived in seclusion for twenty years and never met with ministers. If he was misled by opium addiction, then poppies should be blamed for the fall of the Ming Dynasty. However, it is suspected that what was taken in the palace at that time were all goods from various countries in Nanyang, not produced in China.

Tobacco addiction also began in the Ming Dynasty. Wang Hong's Pillow Worm Small Talk said that "Tobacco leaves come from Fujian. People in the borderlands cannot cure cold diseases without this. Outside the Pass, they even exchange a horse for a jin. During the Chongzhen period, an order was issued to ban it, but there were still many private growers among the people. The profit was high and the law was light, and the people disobeyed the ban as before. Soon, an order was issued that those who violated it would be beheaded. However, not long after, the ban was lifted because the army could not cure cold diseases. When I was a child, I still did not know what tobacco was. At the end of Chongzhen, children as young as three feet old smoked tobacco." See the reference in Gai Yu Cong Kao. Smoking tobacco was also punishable by beheading. No wonder it was later forbidden to smoke opium, which had to be threatened with the death penalty.

Going to the Market

— Sheng Huanming

At the market, people shouted in high-pitched voices, and it was extremely lively and noisy. But very few people carried "zha ma dai" (Note), or carried light "luo dan" to the market specifically to buy goods. A chicken, seven or eight pairs of straw sandals, or a dozen eggs were all this kind of small transaction. A young man carried a load of bamboo baskets filled with piglets to the eaves of the "White Horse Temple" to rest. He wiped the sweat from his forehead, opened his jacket, used a "liang mao" to fan himself, concentrating, savoring the fatigue given by hard work and stuffiness.

"How much are you willing to pay? Eighteen? The salt shop wants to sell for twenty-four! Okay, I'll sell it to you at a loss, hey! Pay back eighteen..." The "private salt" seller shouted straight up his throat to a middle-aged man who was holding a hen upside down. The hen holder only turned his head and did not stop his feet.

"Hey, how about it? Isn't it okay for you to pay eighteen coins?"

"...Oh! Wait for me to sell the chicken and come back to buy it."

"..." The private salt seller was stunned, "Cao!" He slumped down and put down the scale.

The goods in the market seemed to be particularly cheap in the abstract: straw sandals were four copper coins a pair: eggs were thirty-five copper coins a dime. In this busy season, everyone plans to sell their goods a little cheaper as soon as possible, and buy some necessary things and rush home early. But there are still not many people who want to buy, not really not wanting to: most people have to sell their goods first before they can buy goods.

In the past, when market day came, those selling plaster for bruises, fortune-telling, making "leper grabbing relatives" wooden puppet shows, and monkey performers could be seen everywhere in the market. But in recent years, they have almost disappeared. There was only one load of wooden puppet shows in such a large market. The "Shandong people" hid in the tent, blowing squeaky sounds with their mouths, and two lepers bumped their heads against each other on the wooden puppet stage, but this was obviously no longer able to attract those who were willing to pay copper coins.

The sky suddenly covered with haze again, and misty drizzle diffused down from the gray sky. The prices of goods fell: eggs were three copper coins each, and piglets under the eaves of the "White Horse Temple" were only selling for two yuan and fifty cents each.

"Really cheap! These piglets are probably raised for a month or so!" Some people said that, but no one talked about buying them.

Many people have changed their trading methods: for example, a lunch basket is exchanged for three catties of rice, and one catty of rice is exchanged for three pairs of straw sandals...

"Cooked beef is one dollar and five jins, guests, take some back for a drink!" The beef stall owner yawned as he raised the meat knife.

The "Shandong people" who made wooden puppet shows spent four copper coins to buy a large piece of beef tendon, carrying the wooden puppet show frame, humming "The third girl is beautiful and charming, ah yo, those little feet..." step by step, leaving this market on the "official road" that was muddied by the plum rain.

Dusk crawled out, and this market was old.

(Note) Zha ma dai: A kind of bag used by people in the countryside to store money and sundries.

Jews

— Xu Maoyong

When I was compiling a small book on the Jewish question for the Current Affairs Problem Series of the Life Bookstore, I first encountered difficulties with the materials. This difficulty was not due to a lack of materials, as there were many books and newspapers in Japan discussing it. However, I felt that all their discussions were useless, because these materials were all based on Anti-Semitism, deliberately fabricated, and used to insult Jews with rumors that were almost entirely unreliable. This is not surprising. Japan, which always follows Germany in everything, would naturally not disagree with Hitler's policies. Therefore, Lieutenant General Shikotenno Nobutaka publicly declared: "In order to protect the national polity and history of the Japanese Empire, and for the sake of the eternal Heaven and Earth and the everlasting Imperial Throne, we must repel them (Jews)." Because Jews are "spies" who "evilly use the capitalism they created to destroy political and economic institutions," and "hold the sword of socialism and communism to carry out movements to destroy national organizations."

However, I cannot see what harm these "spies" have done to our Republic of China's "national polity," "history," "Heaven and Earth," and "everlasting Imperial Throne." Therefore, I have no obligation to "repel" them. Moreover, what the editor of the Current Affairs Problem Series wanted me to describe was the real face of the Jews, but unfortunately, there were too few materials on this aspect.

My little book was finally barely compiled. Because there were too few true materials, the content was naturally not very substantial. But fortunately, there were still several reliable Western books and newspapers that allowed me to provide a general explanation of several important issues; and what I am most comforted by is that I have not said anything to distort or insult the Jews.

But what I regret most is that at the time of compilation, I forgot an important article, namely, Hakukawa Shiratsuki's "Why the Insult," which was included in Going to the Crossroads. This article defends the Jews and is extremely stern and righteous. In addition to listing the amazing achievements of Jews in culture, he also provides the following explanation for the greed of Jews, which is most despised by the world:

"The majority of Jews have no choice but to rely on the power of money as the only impregnable wall to ensure their own safety. Because if they do not rely on this, even their right to survival will be endangered. In certain periods of the European Middle Ages, it was clear that Jews were strictly prohibited from owning land, and noble professions were also closed to them. As a result, they had no choice but to save money, greedily collect interest, and barely survive in order to assert their right to survival. Therefore, over time, many greedy and stingy people were born, which is also a phenomenon worthy of sympathy. Are not the Christians who persecuted them to this point hateful and blameworthy?"

Dr. Hakukawa also predicted long ago that the Japanese would also repel Jews. He said:

"Thinking carefully, the fact that even Japan is paying attention to the Jewish question, which has never been involved until now, is indeed because Japan has become a world-class Japan. We should be happy! There is no need to worry about anything! In this era when the French occupation of the Ruhr immediately affects the market price of iron and dyes in Japan, this matter may be a matter of course. In the future, Japan will also hear extremely strange Anti-Semitism voices."

Japan is like this, what about China? The Jewish question is a long-standing question, but we have never paid attention to it, let alone since Hitler came to power and put great pressure on the Jews, making this question more serious, our people are still not without any sense of the situation. What is the reason for this silence?

Broite said: "In Japan and China, because the indigenous bourgeoisie do not have conflicts of interest with the Jews, there is no anti-Semitism." Let this be the reason why the Chinese do not throw stones down the well at the Jews, although Japan has anti-Jewish movements due to the prevalence of Fascism. However, why is there not even one person who speaks up for the Jews?

Perhaps, this is because the Chinese are too self-aware, because they know that their fate is the same as that of the Jews, and even worse than the Jews. If they rashly express sympathy for the Jews, they are afraid of being laughed at, and therefore remain silent?

In fact, the Chinese are indeed far behind the Jews. More than two thousand years after losing their homeland, the Jews can still maintain their national language and make great contributions to mankind in culture; and they occupy a great influence in modern capitalist and socialist activities; and the restoration movement is also unyielding.

However, the Jewish restoration movement still has many problems after all. Professor Van Loon has such a passage in his book "Our World":

"If the Jews themselves knew what to do with their old homeland, things would be much simpler. Today, the general orthodox Jews in Eastern Europe, especially in Russia, advocate maintaining its current state, that is, treating it as a huge seminary with a small museum for collecting Hebrew antiquities. As for the older generation, they all remember the famous saying of the prophets, "Let the dead bury the dead," and feel that weeping for the past glory can hinder the glory of the future, so they all hope to build Palestine into a proper modern country like Switzerland or Denmark, and from then on, everyone will forget everything in the past and stop fighting with the Arabs for a few meaningless stones, but focus on road construction and river dredging."

This passage is good to offer to the Jews, and it is especially useful to offer to Chinese youth. However, if it is slightly misinterpreted, the danger is also very great.

Two Brothers (23)

— Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

Old Man Roland shrugged his shoulders and said:

"Ah, ah, the life of the wisest man is to live it comfortably. We are not cattle and horses, but human beings. If we are born poor, then we should work! What can we do, we just have to work. But since we have income from property interest, haha, then it would be extremely stupid for people to work hard."

Pierre proudly replied:

"Our tendencies are different! As for me, I only respect learning and reason in everything in the world, and I don't bother with the rest."

Mrs. Roland always tried her best to ease the constant conflict between father and son; so she changed the subject and talked about a murder case that happened last week in Borberclo Antoine. Everyone immediately paid attention to the case, and felt a keen interest in the interesting and terrible situation, and the moving secrets of the crime. Even if this crime is vulgar, shameful, and hateful, it can still give mankind's curiosity a strange and universal temptation.

But Old Man Roland still took out his watch to look at it from time to time, saying:

"Hurry up, we're about to leave."

Pierre laughed and said:

"It's not even one o'clock yet. Really, there's really no need to make me eat a cold pork chop."

"Are you going to the notary too?" his mother asked him.

He replied bluntly:

"Me? No, what am I going to do? There's no need for me to go to this."

Zhe An didn't say a word, as if it had nothing to do with him at all. When they were talking about the murder case in Borberclo, he had expressed some opinions from the perspective of a jurist, and made a few observations about crime and criminals. Now, he didn't say another word, but the radiance in his eyes, the lively red color on his cheeks, and the glowing beard, seemed to be announcing his happiness.

After the family left, Pierre, who was left alone again, continued his work of finding a house in the morning. After running up and down the stairs for two or three hours, he finally found a beautiful house on Frank Shah I Street: This was a tall Entreso (a house between the basement and the first floor), with two doors leading to two different streets, two living rooms, a glass corridor, where patients could wait for their examination while walking around the decorated flowers, and another exquisite circular dining room with a view of the sea.

Because the current month can directly draw spot flour, they are very keen to take the current month's standard. It was once decreased by the long side in the afternoon, but the result was recovered by the passenger factory and rose again. Finally, the closing price of this month was two points lower, the next month was one and a half points higher, the December was seven and a half points higher, the March was two and a half points higher, and the April was two and a half points lower, because there was a factory out.

Before the Arrival of Foreign Wheat, the Standard Wheat Market is Temporarily Optimistic

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat market, the merchants did not come out, and the factory had the intention of inquiring. The bulls were firm and continued to collect. The vacant households in the railing gang made up for it. Although some floating vacant sales were sold, the market was still strong. The market sentiment was unanimously optimistic. It is estimated that before the arrival of spot foreign wheat and the completion of new transactions, the market can stand firm. The closing price of the current month in January and March was one point higher, and the next month in February and April was three points higher. The current wheat Kai Zhenjiang wheat 2,500 bags, priced at 3.72 yuan, was handled by Xinda.

The Rice Market at Hexia Lacks Progress

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, shipments arrived from over forty sources, totaling 5400 packages. The purchasing power of local shops improved compared to previous days, absorbing approximately 4000 piculs of rice. Consequently, the sluggish market showed signs of recovery. However, overall sentiment remained unstable, resulting in only a general stabilization. Although both Northern and Southern merchants were active in purchasing yesterday, Fujian merchants only bought a little over 100 packages of late rice. Merchants from Yantai and other regions also only bought 7-800 packages. Sales volume slightly decreased. Thus, the prices of late rice varieties like Qingjiao and Sifeng edged closer to the going rate. Prices for japonica varieties like Changshu and Suzhou-Tong, and thick rice varieties like Nangang, remained unchanged. Demand for Du Jian rice was relatively strong, and prices stabilized. Yang Jian sales were slow and sluggish, continuing to decline slightly. Yin Yuanfeng and Yuanjun exhibited the same trend.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, a total of 37-38 boats arrived at Hexia from various routes. Sales were slow in the morning. The market turned around after noon, and large transactions began to occur. Prices for new japonica, Yang, Du, Bu, and Xian rice varieties increased slightly. Yin Bai Yuan also dropped by 10-20 cents. Early rice, thin rice, and passenger Xian rice stabilized, with no fluctuations reported.

First Batch of Hunan Unpolished Rice and New Rice Arrives in Shanghai ▲ The City Holds 224,885 Packages of Foreign Rice in Storage

Yesterday's market for foreign passenger Xian rice remained weak due to the suspension of purchasing by passenger merchants. However, cargo owners were no longer willing to sell at low prices as they had done previously. Thus, the market remained generally stable. Due to the cheap prices, there was continued interest from local merchants, and Ningbo merchants also considered purchasing in small quantities. As a result, the market became more stable in the afternoon. The whole market opened with 100 packages of old Hunan machine-milled oil rice, priced at 7.10 yuan, and 200 packages of Wuxi Yangjian rice, priced at 7.75 yuan. 400 packages of recycled Xiaojiao rice were also sold, priced at 7.05 yuan, all purchased by local merchants. Ningbo merchants bought 100 packages of Nanshixiaochangxian rice at 6.35 yuan.

The Hunan old machine-milled oil rice sold yesterday had recently arrived. At the same time, 206 packages of unpolished rice and new rice also arrived, but they had not yet been sold. Oil rice is welcomed by Zhejiang merchants, and merchants from the North are also purchasing it. It is possible that more shipments will continue to arrive.

Regarding the tax on foreign rice, it is rumored that a decision has been made to levy a tax of 2.5 gold units per hundred catties, which, based on current market prices, amounts to 90%. If this is implemented, rice imports will be immediately halted. Currently, the city's total rice inventory, excluding the 24,900+ packages of recycled Xiaojiao rice stored by the Japanese merchants in the Daxing warehouse, is 224,885 packages. This is broken down as follows: 120,060 packages in Yitaixing warehouse, 78,852 packages in Longmao warehouse, 17,100 packages in Qichang warehouse, 8,347 packages in Yuan Yi warehouse, and 526 packages in Zhaoshang Hua warehouse, totaling 224,885 packages.

High-Quality Soybeans Rise by 4-5 Cents

The supply of soybeans is indeed abundant, but high-quality soybeans are scarce. Medium-quality soybeans are increasingly weak. Yesterday, various merchants took advantage of the low prices and traded 14-15 cartloads of soybeans. As a result, high-quality soybeans rose by 4-5 cents, while medium and lower-quality soybeans are unlikely to improve in the short term. Jiujiang soybeans are still not favored. Du soybeans are still not available. Sha Huang soybeans are average. Recently, Ningbo merchants have been inquiring about green soybeans. The market is relatively stable.

North-South Goods Dried Lily Flowers Increase by One Yuan Again

Dried lily flowers have been selling very well for several days, but the supply has not increased. Therefore, merchants are very interested in purchasing them. Prices have been quoted tightly and have become more favorable. Yesterday, the market price increased sharply. Top-quality dried lily flowers opened at 19 yuan, a sharp increase of one yuan. The price increases for medium and lower-quality varieties were similar. If sales remain strong, further price increases are expected.

Silk and Tea Overseas Silk Prices Continue to Decline

▲ Lyon Chinese Silk Plummets Again The price of Chinese silk on the Lyon silk market has struggled to stabilize since the fluctuations in the French exchange rate. Initially, B-grade white filature silk dropped from 80 francs per kilogram to 78.75 francs. Yesterday morning, French firms like Credit Lyonnais received a telegram from Lyon reporting another sharp decline in the price of white filature silk. A-grade opened at only 83.75 francs per kilogram, a decrease of 2.5 francs. B-grade opened at 73.75 francs, a decrease of 5 francs.

▲ Thirty Pieces of Wuxi Raw Silk Arrive in Shanghai Recently, silk mills in Wuxi have been reducing production and shutting down machines due to the sharp decline in silk sales in Europe and America. The amount of Wuxi raw silk transported to Shanghai has decreased daily. Yesterday morning, thirty pieces arrived on the Shanghai-Wuxi passenger train.

▲ Sales of Rayon Remain Sluggish Lately, the exchange rate has been loosened, and the price of rayon has become weaker. Sales remain sluggish. Yesterday, only local silk factories purchased 16 boxes of Red, Blue, and Golden Bell brand immediate delivery goods, priced from 172.25 yuan to 160.75 yuan net.

▲ Sales of Foreign Silk are Unlikely to Improve Recently, overseas silk weaving mills have seen little demand for raw silk and have ample stocks. Chinese merchants are competing to sell their silk, and prices are gradually declining. Electronic transfer prices are increasingly small. European and American firms are all taking a wait-and-see approach. Chinese silk merchants are suffering increasing losses and are taking a passive stance. Sales of silk are unlikely to improve. Yesterday, only ten bales of grey silk and five bales of reeled silk were traded, and prices remained weak.

Moroccan Tea Market is Sluggish

According to recent news received by industry insiders, the Moroccan green tea market has suddenly become sluggish. Sales of Japanese green tea have almost completely stopped. Sales of Chinese Lu Zhuang Pingshui Zhenmei pearl tea have also decreased significantly compared to the past. Taking Zhenmei as an example, normal monthly sales are 5-6000 boxes, but currently only 4000 boxes are being sold. In addition, various foreign firms have recently received large shipments of new goods, making the market even more crowded. As a result, the selling price of all teas, except for high-quality varieties which have remained stable, has fallen by 10-20 francs.

Piece Goods Broadcloth Sells Well and Prices Rise

The popular 1005 broadcloth has recently seen a rapid increase in popularity. After 36 boxes of spot goods were released by De Ji Foreign Firm the other day, the standard public price immediately increased. Because the supply of this fabric has been cut off, and the sales season is in full swing, the wholesale price yesterday was 8.25 yuan across the board. Tailors still need to add more for retail. Because of the popular sale of eighteen two twenty-four color broadcloth, sellers are hoarding goods, and the wholesale price is 8.5 yuan net. Most also require cash payment upon invoicing. It is heard that the price of the 36 boxes released by De Ji Foreign Firm was only 7.6 yuan per yard.

Business Economics (47)

The Business of Peanuts and Peanut Kernels (Continued)

— E

Peanuts and peanut kernels are mostly transported from the north. This business should seem to belong to the northern goods industry, but the peanut and peanut kernel business in Shanghai, especially large-scale operations, still belongs to the miscellaneous grains industry. Sometimes the miscellaneous grains industry completely controls it, and the northern goods industry wholesale from them. In addition to the northern goods and miscellaneous grain industries, the local goods industry which also carries fruit also has this peanut and peanut kernel buying and selling wholesale business. Because peanuts are produced in sandy soil, they are naturally a kind of local goods. Also, because their planting shape is similar to various food grains, and they belong to the legume family, it is suitable for the rice, wheat, miscellaneous grains, and land products industries to manage. Furthermore, because they are northern goods, they seem like dried fruit. Hence the northern goods industry manages them. Therefore, the miscellaneous grains, northern goods, and local goods industries each manage them individually. The broker licenses issued by the government in the past also included these items. This is only based on Shanghai. It is not the same outside of Shanghai. For example, rice and grain stores in inland counties have never been seen selling peanuts and peanut kernels. As for the producing areas, many are managed by grain stores.

The source of peanut kernels for the miscellaneous grain industry and the northern goods industry is the same, which is transported by train, ship, and sandboat from the three provinces of Shandong, Henan, and Zhili in the north. The sales routes are not entirely the same. In addition to foreign firms exporting northern goods, both the northern goods and grain industries have transactions, but southern goods, dismantled goods, and tea food stores are exclusively controlled by the northern goods industry. The transaction quantities are small and tight, that is, one bag, two bags, eight bags, or ten bags are all sold wholesale. The grain industry is different. The sales routes are all in whole lots, transactions of eighty or one hundred bags are already rare, mostly calculated by the cartload, or by whole incoming cargo receipt, (when new goods first appear on the market, each lot is also small). The sales routes are foreign firms, oil mills, Guangdong and Fujian merchants, and other passenger merchants, as well as inland areas of this street (that is, wholesale to the northern goods industry). The raw oil produced into finished goods in the producing areas entirely belongs to the rice and grain industry. Passenger ports have resident purchasing staff from the grain industry. Visiting customers in Shanghai also concurrently manage oil bean cake and miscellaneous grains. Before the development of trains, it was the prosperous era of sandboats (sailing boats). The sandboat groups all joined the oil bean cake industry. There is a deep historical relationship. Therefore, grain industry arrivals have been prosperous from the past to the present. As for the arrivals and sales of the local goods industry, there are differences from the two industries mentioned above. The local goods industry focuses on peanuts, and the production area is only in Chongming and various places in Pudong. There is no northern source. The sales routes are only dismantled goods and retail households. (End)
