Talks

An Ideal Teacher

— Guanghan

A teacher bears the heavy responsibility of education, constantly interacting with students, directly and indirectly influencing them deeply. Therefore, the quality of a teacher is of great importance to national education. But what are the standards for a good teacher? How should we choose? Although this is not easy to answer, I would like to write down the qualifications that an ideal teacher should possess and discuss them with everyone.

1. Rich Knowledge The greatest purpose of reading is to seek knowledge. Therefore, a good teacher should be a learned and versatile person who can impart rich knowledge to students to satisfy their desire for knowledge. Of course, teachers are not omnipotent and do not know everything. But at least they should have sufficient research in the subject they teach in order to be qualified. If they are proficient in everything, that would be even better.

2. Good Teaching Methods A teacher cannot fulfill the task of education solely with rich knowledge. In addition to knowledge, good teaching methods are also important. Because with good teaching methods, students can understand and comprehend everything that is explained, and teachers can share what they have gained with students. But this does not only refer to the kind of injection-style teaching method. It is useless for a teacher to simply pour knowledge into the students' minds. They must always pay attention to whether the students can absorb and digest it. Most importantly, they must also give students ample opportunity to develop their innate abilities freely. On the one hand, teachers should answer all the students' questions and make them understand. On the other hand, they should encourage students to think for themselves in order to develop their inherent nature. In addition, they must use appropriate methods everywhere to arouse students' interest in learning, and constantly allow students to express their opinions freely. Only in this way can teaching achieve twice the result with half the effort.

3. Eloquent Eloquence We often see some teachers who have accumulated a lot of knowledge, but because their eloquence is dull and their words are not exhaustive, they often cannot express themselves fluently, causing students to fail to understand and gain nothing. Conversely, some who are good at eloquence, although their talents and learning are ordinary, when they are in the classroom, they speak eloquently and tirelessly, lecturing with great enthusiasm, eventually moving the listeners and enabling them to understand. Therefore, a fluent tongue is also indispensable for an excellent teacher.

4. Novel Ideas Ideas are also very important. The times are advancing, and old ideas are certainly not suitable for today. Even new ideas are constantly changing. Therefore, an ideal teacher must also have ideas that are in line with the times. Because teachers should not only increase students' knowledge but also train their thinking. If the teacher's mind is full of some rotten old ideas, then the students who are trained will certainly not be able to adapt to the trend of the times and will eventually become laggards of the times. Therefore, we believe that a good teacher should be an educator with fresh ideas.

5. Perfect Personality In education, I feel that the influence of personality is more powerful than the infusion of knowledge. Because humans are emotional animals, and emotion is the best way to guide them. A teacher with a perfect personality becomes a role model for students through his every move. Every word he says can move students. Through such subtle influence, students' character will naturally be cultivated and become more perfect.

An ideal teacher should at least possess the above five qualities to be worthy of being called an excellent educator and to be worthy of bearing the responsibility of education. Indeed, perhaps these conditions are too strict. I have also thought about this. But the task of education is very important, so how can we allow ourselves to be perfunctory?

Reminiscences of a Past Summer

— Yiping

Miss Spring came and went hastily, without bestowing on us a mysterious smile; while Mr. Summer's tyrannical power has already descended upon us.

The asphalt on the road is compressed into patterned patterns by the wheels. The rickshaw pullers' heels are like hitting moist mud, and a wave of heat turns into sweat droplets from their foreheads. People in the rickshaw feel a good breeze blowing in their faces, unbutton their collars or suit ties, and enjoy the happiness of this day. They cross their legs and shout, "Faster! Faster!"

The heads of rickshaw pullers are always wrapped in towels. Do they know? The sun is closer to you. This is the time to resist!

Cars shoot past like arrows. The fashionable old men and ladies in the cars are going to the invitation of the movie theater. Sensual movies, air conditioning pipes, and frozen ripples are waiting for their patronage. The drivers are much happier than the rickshaw pullers. Although they do not have the enjoyment of the latter, they also unbutton their collars when the wind blows in their faces.

Western-style houses connect to the sky. Exhausted, Miss slips her ankles and draped in a silk bathrobe, steps into the bedroom from the bathroom. The electric fan blows the hem of the bathrobe. She lights a cigarette, lies on the leather sofa, flips through a few pages of romance novels or the local supplement's movie advertisements, and falls into a hazy sleep.

At night, neon lights replace the daylight. People, cars, cars, people, Xujiahui, Caohejing…

The game room is crowded with audiences, carbonic acid gas steams, and gongs and drums are noisy. The bodies of prostitutes are wrapped in tight cheongsams, flirting and scolding. The young hooligans in open-necked silk shirts smile contentedly, exchanging banknotes for flesh.

Moonlight shines from the shade of the trees onto the ground, like a broken mirror. A pair of lovers walking side by side, the woman's disheveled hair resting on the man's shoulder. They step on the scattered moon shadows, walking slowly and whispering. The situation in the park is filled with a romantic atmosphere. There is no summer here, only night.

A typical Shanghai young master rushes into dance halls, massage parlors... enjoying the perverted stimulation of sex from a perverted life.

Mr. Wang, a foreign firm clerk in a small room, lights a British candle and frantically attacks the bedbugs attacking him. The lady from the sock factory upstairs also opens her eyes wide, listening to the Ningbo landlord's laughter of drawing three hundred points.

Streets, alleys. Top-notch cries for ten coins. Children, coolies, promoters of epidemics. Flies fly in groups on the discarded garbage heaps. A naked man lies on the plank door, humming the song of reaching out to touch his sister, and two neatly dressed silk sisters walk past, giggling.

In their dreams, the children in the countryside hear the sound of car horns. He asks his mother, "Dad bought a car?"

The lives of the poor roll under the wheels of cars, and the lives of the rich fall into the pond.

A Scene of Rural Life in Late Autumn

— Qian Xu

Don’t we often eat yellow sparrows? That thing is so plump and delicious, it’s best to have with wine. If we say that crabs are a unique taste in the water, then there is nothing better than yellow sparrows on land; so yellow sparrows and crabs can be called the “two wonders” in late autumn food.

Autumn is deep, and the grains in the fields are growing very full, with grains of white rice wrapped in thin shells, tender and solid. So the yellow sparrows become active, flying in groups to the rice fields to peck at them, and often a good acre of rice, with the grains growing full, is suddenly pecked to pieces by them. The farmers hate them, but there is nothing they can do, but to go and check it from time to time.

However, many farmers rely on catching yellow sparrows for an income at this time. Their methods of catching them are extremely skillful. They know that the nests of yellow sparrows are mostly on the滩边 of the reed pond, so every time the vast twilight casts shadows on the water, they go to the bank to check where the sparrows gather to roost. After checking, they go back to prepare. The tools for catching are very simple, a long-handled silk net bucket and a small glass lamp are enough.

After a while, it gets dark, and they all dress up. The so-called “dressing up” is not like the “modern girls” in Shanghai applying powder and makeup when they go out, nor is it like the gentlemen tidying up their clothes: they just take off their shoes and tie a belt around their waists for work convenience, and unbutton the buttons in front of their chests.

They are as if facing a big enemy, as if stealing a camp and robbing a village, walking quickly with gags in their mouths, not talking to each other. When they get to the reed beach, they walk towards the place they have seen in the sun. At this time, they are so quiet that they dare not even breathe out, and their steps are gently put down and then gently lifted up, step by step to reach the destination, and they continue to walk down into the water. The water in the reed pond is almost a foot deep, and it soaks to the knees when they step down, but they don't care about these things, and they concentrate on netting the roosting places of the sparrows with one bucket after another, but whether they net three or five, they must strangle them to death and throw them into their chests with the buttons undone. If they are not strangled to death, once there is a call, then the other yellow sparrows will fly away, and not only will they gain nothing, but they will also implicate all their companions to return empty-handed.

So on windy nights, it is even a good opportunity for them to show off their skills.

Now they are much smarter than before. On nights without strong winds, they will ask their wives and children to knock on gongs or kerosene tanks outside the reeds to disturb their hearing. They work while knocking, so they can achieve a lot of results.

However, have the people who eat them ever thought of the farmers who wade through the water and stay up all night when they are holding sparrows and drinking wine and talking loudly?

Mr. Editor

— Meng Ren

Stepping into the door of the editor’s office, my chest swelled. The desk was piled high with a lot of things, some red, some white, some light yellow, some…

Under the lake-green light, it was gloomy. If it weren’t for this, the old glasses on the bridge of my nose would have been a thousand degrees deeper.

I randomly grabbed a letter, cut it open with scissors, pulled out the work and took a look, it was simply a joke. My brow furrowed and I threw it away! Then I looked at the second letter, the beginning was…

×× My Love:

My heart is broken! Now…………………

I still threw it away. Then I looked at the third letter, lake-colored stationery, rough pen writing, and the green light, good, it was actually imitating drawing, so I threw it away again. The fourth letter was a poem, written very carefully, but it didn’t suit the nature of the journal, so I threw it away again. The fifth letter was like this, the sixth letter was attached with a letter, the letter roughly said, “How he suffered from the pain of being driven by life, and asking Mr. Editor for help.” It wasn’t until the seventh letter that I reluctantly kept it. The eighth letter was even funnier. The manuscript paper was signed ×× Miss, but in the meaning it fully expressed that he was a male, undoubtedly, it was eliminated again. The ninth and tenth were attached with letters. The former manuscript was introduced by a friend, and it was written:

Mr. ××:

×× is a pseudonym of ××, …… if there is anything incomplete, please

Mr. take care of it……………

The next one was a scolding letter 丨丨丨

Mr. ××:

The two clumsy works “×××” and “××××” that were previously discarded have now been published in ×× journal. With the reputation of ×× journal, it is ultimately better than

Your journal…………………

I smiled. It was a common thing for editors to encounter. I put the manuscript and the letter into the wastepaper basket. Looking further down, the eleventh letter, the twelfth letter, some with crab-walking writing style, some with English words filling the entire page, were all thrown into the wastepaper basket.

Looking further down, one letter, two letters, three letters,……… one letter, two letters, three letters……… My eyes are a little blurry. I’ll rest for a while, take a cigarette, and then look further down, one letter, two letters, three letters……… It’s about time, the manuscripts are finished. Calculating, about fifteen out of a hundred and ten letters were selected. Because of the limited space, I had to sacrifice seven of the fifteen letters. How sad! Those that were selected were discarded again, but how could the editor not know that they were made by the author’s painstaking efforts, but because of the limited space! It was just a helpless cry!

Because of “limited space,” the editor became the invisible enemy of “disappointed authors.”

Modern Celebrity Painting and Calligraphy: Mr. Lu Di's Landscapes

Page 21

Fate

— Jian

Fate has ruled us Chinese for who knows how many thousands of years. Countless people have died miserably in its iron grip in the past, and are now groaning under its iron hooves. People are fooled by it, anesthetized by it, and naturally listen to it willingly, letting it trample on them, letting it beheaded. Although there have been a few people who have risen up to oppose it, denouncing it as superstition, it has not had much effect.

After the Xinhai Revolution, the May Fourth Movement, the National Revolution, and several political and cultural shocks, fate also shook and became unlucky; but it was only a “flash in the pan,” and soon it “resurrected from the ashes” and came back even more fiercely.

Now that the revolution is over, fate is sprouting up like bamboo shoots after the rain. It is naturally to be expected that the business of fortune-tellers is booming everywhere. Since the sentence “The Chinese are destined to suffer” was published, fate has seized the opportunity to move restlessly, and its momentum has become stronger and stronger. Recently, the concept of fate has been widely discussed in people’s conversations, articles, and correspondence. Fate has shrouded all of China, and fate has occupied the hearts of all Chinese people. Great is fate!

They are all the same people; some are rich and successful, some are down and out for life; some hold important positions, some are displaced. As for the victims in disaster areas where the flames of war are raging and floods and droughts are everywhere, they eat wind and dew and look haggard; the bourgeoisie in the big cities are drinking and singing wildly in a world of wine, green, and red, living a life of extreme pleasure. This contradictory phenomenon is generally attributed to fate by superficial views, and only fate can easily solve this problem vaguely.

However, this is not the truth, it is just a mistake. Fate has absolutely no relationship with people’s actions, and of course it cannot produce cause and effect; at most, people first believe in the fallacy of fate, change direction, change attitude, and become putting the cart before the horse. If everything is determined by fate, then people become zombies, unable to move, and have to listen to nature. What is the point of “effort” and “struggle,” what is the point of “resisting Japan” and “anti-imperialism”? It’s all nonsense, what does it look like?

Fate originally arose in an unequal social system. People encounter all kinds of difficulties, but they have neither the courage to overcome them nor the willingness to do so out of selfishness. They say it is fate, and there is nothing they can do; so they bow their heads and calm down, and forget about everything. This is a manifestation of human laziness, a good way to escape reality.

It is not fate that determines life, but people who create fate. Here we can find a conclusion: fate and the doctrine of determinism, like “theocracy,” are unique to a deformed, morbid society, and are things that reduce resistance and eliminate aggressiveness.

Drama

Eliminating Evil and Pacifying the Good

— Wan Cheng

Scene One

A panoramic view of the village, bathed in the nascent sunlight, is exceptionally fresh and serene. The door of a house in the village opens, and a farmer emerges from within. He appears to be in his forties. In his right hand, he holds a kitchen knife, and in his left, a hen, ready to slaughter it outside. A peasant woman, roughly the same age as the farmer, stands inside the courtyard near the doorway, peacefully watching the farmer, holding an infant.

Farmer (Looking up at the sky as he exits the door, a smile on his face, he says to the peasant woman inside): Siliu's Mother, look how clear the sky is today. This child is truly lucky!

Peasant Woman: Yes, the heavens know it's Siliu's one-month celebration today, so they've gifted us with a clear day for us to celebrate joyfully. (Speaking, she lowers her head toward the infant in her arms): [Babbling sounds to the baby] Even the Bodhisattva is helping... (Making cooing sounds to the child, the peasant woman cannot resist kissing his face wildly.)

Farmer (Smiling as he slaughters the chicken, muttering to himself): This chicken is so plump and delightful! If I hadn't bought it early, someone else would have snatched it up. It's not just anything; if the chicken isn't fat, the soup won't be flavorful. This is a once-in-a-lifetime event, and I can't let the guests be anything less than delighted! (Having finished slaughtering the chicken, the couple goes inside together. After a while, the farmer emerges again, carrying a bamboo basket, calling into the house as he leaves): Siliu's Mother, hurry up and start simmering the chicken over the fire. The soup won't be rich if the fire isn't strong enough. And you need to tidy up the house, so when the guests arrive in a little while, things aren't messy and unclean. I'm going to the market in town to buy some vegetables now, and I'll be right back. (A chorus of "Okay, okay" comes from inside the house. The farmer strides off energetically. After a short pause, the peasant woman comes out with a rice winnowing basket, casually closing the door behind her. She has gone to the stream to wash rice.)

A young village head rushes over from afar, accompanied by a servant. Reaching the farmer's door, the servant says:

Servant: Young Master, I just saw them slaughtering a chicken. Do you think they deserve to eat chicken? (Staring at the doorway, he sees chicken blood on the ground): Look, isn't that blood on the ground? There's no doubt they stole the chicken from our manor!

Village Head (Believing him without question, he becomes furious): Damn them, damn them! They're really audacious, daring to steal my chicken! Do they think they can swat flies on a tiger's head? Well, since they've brought this upon themselves, they can't blame me for being harsh! (With that, he angrily bursts through the bamboo fence, ordering the servant to return first.)

Scene Two

Three thatched huts, arranged quite neatly: the central one is the main room, the left one is the kitchen, and the right one is the bedroom. The village head searches everywhere, only finding the chicken simmering in the kitchen. He can't help but become ten times angrier. However, no one is home, and he can't wait for the farmer to return to argue with him. He goes straight to the bedroom on the right, picks up the infant lying in the cradle, and throws it forcefully to the ground. There is a tragic cry, and he rushes out the door and leaves. Just as he exits, the servant rushes back, hurriedly saying to him:

Servant: Young Master, the chicken from the manor has been found. Someone had covered it with a bamboo basket. Young Master, since they didn't steal it, please forgive them!

Village Head (Seeming regretful, he remains silent.)

Scene Three

A major village road, with a constant stream of people coming and going. Some are going to town, others are returning from town. Suddenly, a crazed man and woman rush in, none other than the farmer and his wife. They are crying and lamenting, their appearance extremely pitiful.

Couple: My heart! My little darling! My ill-fated child!

The pedestrians, seeing this, are terrified and scatter in all directions, fearing being grabbed by the mad people.

After a while, the village head brings several strong laborers, ordering them to bind the two mad people and immediately drive them out of the village.

Village Head (Addressing the villagers): As the village head of this village, I bear the responsibility of "eliminating evil and pacifying the good." Therefore, I am now driving them away to prevent everyone from living in peace.

Villagers (Clapping and cheering loudly): Ah, we must all support the village head who seeks happiness for us! We should all present the village head with a plaque that says "Eliminating Evil and Pacifying the Good"!

Crowd: Yes, everyone agrees! And we wish our village head a long life!

Amidst this clamorous cheering, the village head returns home with a smile. | The End |

Movie Supplement

Hollywood's Method of Protecting Young Actors - The Strictness of California Law - Enough for Lawyers to Study for a Year

— Mao De

After writing an article yesterday about "Hollywood's Most Adorable Child," I felt it was quite interesting and wanted to add more. This article, "Hollywood's Method of Protecting Young Actors," continues from the previous one. The central employment agency for film professionals in Hollywood always has thousands of children's names on file, waiting to be selected by various companies. It includes people of all nationalities: Chinese, Japanese, Indian, African black people, Mexican people, Siamese, or Bornean people, all of them. They each have their own uses, and when needed, the value of black children is no lower than that of white children, or even more expensive due to their rarity.

Since these child actors occupy a very important position on set, the local authorities cannot help but think of ways to protect their health and safety. California law is extremely strict in protecting these child actors. We can now briefly describe some of it, hoping that our film companies can adopt all possible methods of protecting young actors without waiting for legal judgments, creating happiness for these adorable young actors.

According to California law, children under six months of age are only allowed to stay in the company for two hours each day, and work on set must not exceed twenty minutes per day, and each take must not exceed thirty seconds. Children over six months of age and under two years of age are only allowed to stay in the company for four hours each day, of which work must not exceed two hours. Child actors from two to six years old can stay in the company for six hours each day, but work must not exceed three hours. Child actors from six to eighteen years old can stay in the company for eight hours each day, and work must not exceed four hours. The salary that child actors should receive is also stipulated by the local authorities. For child actors less than one month old, the daily salary is US$75; for those over one month and under three months, it is US$50 per day; and for those from three to six months, it is US$25 per day.

The above are just some brief outlines. In reality, the laws protecting child actors in Hollywood are extraordinarily complex. Many prohibitions are enough for lawyers to study as a specialized subject. For example, in order to protect the eyesight of child actors, it is forbidden to use strong lights on their faces. There must be nurses on set. In addition, there are women's associations, childcare associations, and their representatives come to supervise every day. There are specific time regulations for the breastfeeding or food of child actors. When a company hires a child actor, they must first have their physical examined by an educational institution. If they continue to work afterwards, they must be re-examined every three months. How to arrange the nursery in the company, etc., are also detailed in the law. Child actors' working hours cannot be after 10 p.m. The rest cannot be described in detail due to space limitations.

Movie Reviews

Review of "The Tears of a Daughter-in-Law" - Another Language - Produced by MGM - Premieres at Cathay

— Ling He

Since the premiere of "White Sister," Helen Hayes has given us the most profound impression. Regardless of whether she is the leading tragic star of the time, she has certainly been very successful in tragedies such as "The White Sister" and "A Farewell to Arms." In "White Sister," when we see her wearing a white headscarf in the monastery, saying goodbye to her lover through the iron gate, and facing the altar to cut her hair, that kind of solemn sentiment shatters the feelings of every audience member. In "A Farewell to Arms," when she receives her lover's affection in front of the hero's statue, only she can show that kind of passionate yet timid inner performance with such real emotion. Such acting skills are worthy of our sincere attention in any case. Similarly, in this film, she writes about her own love for her husband, although her husband's love is not as sweet as she ideally imagined, and although her husband's family often teases her in an unbearable way, she endures it and still waits for the revival of love with her entire pure heart. However, she is always a timid person. She finally accepts the affection of her nephew, although she rationally feels that this action is inappropriate. Especially after that climax of breaking the plaster statue, when the husband leaves in anger, and she kisses the nephew but pushes him away, that kind of profound expression of contradictory emotions truly shows her unique talent.

At the same time, the husband, Robert Montgomery, is consistent, just like in "The Single Standard" and "Between Two Women", as relaxed, flirty, and suave as ever. Isn't it so? When an actor has their own unique personality, they can always achieve great success in a suitable script. Here, although we cannot see that he has made any more drastic progress than before, the fact that he has appropriately fulfilled his due responsibilities is very clear. We see, when he is reading the newspaper, impatiently asking, "Who opened that window?" watching his nephew take his wife out, watching his wife and nephew dance infatuatedly, and waiting at his mother's house for his naughty wife who had been out all night to come to him, are all scenes that others cannot do without laughter and tears.

In addition to the protagonists, all the other supporting roles are also very diligent. Even the young John Beal tried his best to bring out that simple and rich emotion, such as before and after breaking the plaster statue, and when his parents questioned him about last night's whereabouts at his grandmother's house.

With excellent actors, the work will always gain most of its success in any case. Conversely, under the current state of Chinese films, the richness of their content is not superior to that of American films, but it is often because of the lack of good actors that everything cannot be perfectly expressed on the screen with all the skills.

We cannot deny that American films already have mature acting skills, especially since many actors have sufficient academic qualifications, which adds a lot of color to their films. Therefore, I would like to advise Chinese film actors to not use all their energy to pursue empty fame, but to work hard to improve their skills in cultivation, and at the same time fulfill their great responsibilities to Chinese films, assuming that they also recognize the future of Chinese films.

I have said a few digressive words, but these are by no means nonsense. Now let's talk about the other aspects of "The Tears of a Daughter-in-Law."

First of all, we have to pay attention to the structure of this script, which is a very literary and meticulously described work. It is often said that pure literary films are not welcomed by the general audience (the fact that "Spring Silkworms" didn't sell as well as "Man Jiang Hong" is a good example), but this kind of script has its own very high value, which is undeniable. As for this film, we must admit the playwright's high level of descriptive skill in any case.

He takes the family affairs of a small bourgeois family as his subject matter, meticulously writing about the common love twists and turns of young couples. I think everyone who has been married has had this strange experience. No matter how much one trusts one's love for the other party, there will always be a few moments of mischief. After a calm explanation, they will reconcile as before.

Here, we are reminded of "Waterloo Bridge," which explained the worries of a husband who was wilful due to economic difficulties, leading to a break with his wife, until they reunited ten years later. "Waterloo Bridge" can point out this economic relationship, so it is naturally more emphatic than this "Tears of a Daughter-in-Law." However, the latter also realistically depicts this kind of small matter, writing a very frank part of the life of the small bourgeoisie, and it also has its value. As for the meticulous depiction, we only need to see it expressed in the nephew personally smashing his uncle's statue, or the petty eating of cakes by the sisters-in-law.

The director's high level, limited by space, cannot be discussed in detail. It is clear that the director has had great success here.

Review of "Three Escorts" | Premieres at Central | ▲ A Little Commentary

— Moore

Because of the audience's demand, the themes of Chinese films roughly have to touch on some social realities. This point is reflected even in the productions of the relatively backward so-called "small companies." The recently premiered "Blood Road" and "Dawn" are clear examples. But the development of history is always a curve. After "Mad Current" and before "Spring Silkworms," there was even a so-called "Man Jiang Hong" for us to watch. Then, the martial arts film "Three Escorts," which was produced two years ago, is being screened today, and we don't need to be surprised!

"Burning of the Red Lotus Temple" was banned, saying it was too absurd, but American Western films are flooding the market. Of course, "Burning of the Red Lotus Temple" and "Western films" are a little different, but this difference is only in degree, not in essence. Therefore, there is a reason why many people find it difficult to recognize that Chinese films have already surpassed American films in terms of content. Then, although "Three Escorts" is similar to Western films, in the development of Chinese films, the screening of "Three Escorts" has to be considered more serious.

But from this film "Three Escorts," we see that the progress of Chinese films is not only in terms of content, but also in technical aspects (including directing, etc.) There has also been considerable progress, which increases our optimism about the future of Chinese films. This is just small talk.

▲ The Film Itself

The story of "Three Escorts" is formulaic: chivalrous heroes, eliminating evil and pacifying the good. Originally, there was also a happy ending, and even the brochure wrote, "Huifen and Huifang are paired with Da Song," "Meigu is paired with Wang Bin," "Three pairs of lovebirds and Zhang Fa the old man enjoy their remaining years in the mortal world." (Original text) As such, on the screen, we only see Wang Bin recover, followed by a swaying wind skill, which was probably cut out, and cutting it out is at least a bit clever.

I would like to specifically write down some of the shortcomings of "Three Escorts":

First, in terms of the story, the county magistrate is riding on an official ship, but the crew happens to be a bandit gang. Since they are a bandit gang, why don't they rob the wealth first? Or respond during the great battle between Jade Butterfly and the "Three Escorts," and rob the wealth after Jade Butterfly is dead? The other coincidences are even more numerous.

Second, in terms of directing, the introduction of the characters at the opening is too dull, one shot, one subtitle. It's the same in the middle, too many subtitles, interrupting the audience's attention.

Third, using daylight photography, the lighting is too poor, the outdoor scenery and clothes move too much!

Fourth, the actors Wang Yuanlong, Da Zichun, and Song Yuquan are all very bad. Although Zhang Meiyu is not good, she has a few good expressions.

Novel Movie Extravaganza No More Dinner at Eight (9)

— Ma Teng

Max has left, and Renaud stands unsteadily, trembling, his hand touching his forehead. His hat has fallen off, and he doesn't even notice. He looks around, but feels that everything around him is mocking him, teasing him, threatening him. He stumbles to the dressing mirror, and sees himself. He covers his face with his hands, and dares not look again. He picks up the telegram, reads half of it, and throws it away. There is a wine bottle lying on the floor. He picks it up and pours it into his mouth, but there is not a drop left. He throws the wine bottle away again.

After a while, the hotel manager comes again. He very politely discusses with Renaud, asking him to move out of that large room, because an old customer is used to living in that room, just like at home, and they must get it. Renaud asks him, if he moves out of that room, what other room will he be given to live in? The manager says, "Now is the peak season for the Expo, people are coming from all over, and there really isn't a single empty room in the hotel." Hearing this, Renault laughed strangely and said, "It doesn't matter, it doesn't matter, I'm just about to notify the accounting office that I'm moving out soon. I have some friends in Palm Beach inviting me to go. The parade car has already been booked... when do you want this room?" The manager said, "No rush, no rush, is tomorrow at noon okay?" Renaud nods subconsciously. The manager said, "Thank you, Mr. Renaud. I'm really sorry for all the inconvenience." He bowed and went out.

Renaud stares blankly as the hotel manager leaves. After a while, he gradually wakes up. He hears the sound of a hurdy-gurdy in the street outside. He goes to the window and looks at the many people gathered in the street. He picks up the telegram, takes out that one dollar and seven cents from his pocket, looks at it for a while, wraps the money in the telegram paper, and throws it out the window to the street musician. He slams the window shut, takes a few steps back, and collapses into a chair. He tries his best to cheer up, but he no longer has the strength to cheer up. He looks dizzyingly at Pola's graceful shadow on the mantelpiece. He mumbles to it as if in a dream, "Let's imagine that this is our home. And let's imagine that this is a real stove, not a fake wooden one that burns gas."

"Gas! Gas!" He suddenly has an idea. He bends over and tests it, and a terrifying thought attacks his brain. He opens the small door of the gas pipe, listens to the hissing sound of the gas coming out, and feels that he has won. He closes the gas pipe again, and inspects the room all around. He sees black shadows in every corner of the room, preparing to immediately crawl onto his body. He jumps forward, runs to the door, turns the key, and locks the door. He takes off his tuxedo and tears it down, stuffing the cracks under the door. He also goes to the bathroom and takes many clothes, and stuffs all the empty cracks. He inspects all around again, and feels very satisfied. He straightens his tie, and puts on a robe. He doesn't want to neglect the final appearance at all. He also turns off all the lights, leaving only one on. He opens the door of the gas pipe again. He lies back in the chair, looking at Pola's photograph. Next to him is a telephone, and his hand gropes for it, wanting to make a call to Pola. (To be continued)
